Understanding the Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: The Role of 'Qawa'id' and 'Tawassul'
Commentary on the definition's key terms and exclusions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the definition of Usul al-Fiqh by identifying the roles of 'qawa'id' and 'tawassul' and distinguishing the science from other disciplines.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is defined by its distinct subject matter — universal rules that directly lead to fiqh, not mere debate.

The passage you are about to study is a commentary on the classical definition of Usul al-Fiqh. It unpacks two critical terms: 'qawa'id' (universal propositions) and 'tawassul' (reacment). Understanding these terms is essential to grasp what makes Usul al-Fiqh a unique science, separate from Arabic grammar or dialectics. This lesson will guide you through the logical structure of the definition and its exclusions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentia
The definition includes 'knowledge' as the genus and 'reacment' as the differentia. Determine what each part excludes from the science.
The genus is 'ilm' and the differentia is 'tawassul qarib ila al-fiqh'.
2
Analyze the term 'qawa'id'
The text explains that 'rules' refer to universal propositions that serve as premises in syllogisms. Distinguish between conjunctive and disjunctive syllogisms.
These are the building blocks of istidlal (deduction).
3
Examine the restriction 'near reacment'
The 'ba' in 'biha' and 'ila al-fiqh' indicate direct attainment without intermediary. See what this excludes — namely, Arabic sciences that do not directly lead to fiqh.
This is the key differentia.
4
Understand the exclusion of debate sciences
The purpose of dialectic is to compel an opponent, not to investigate fiqh. Hence it is excluded by the 'near reacment' condition.
This includes ilm al-jadal and ilm al-munazara.
5
Apply the definition to distinguish Usul from other sciences
Use the definition as a test: does a given inquiry focus on universal premises for directly reaching fiqh? If not, it is not Usul al-Fiqh.
This is a practical tool for classifying books and disciplines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طرف توصل قریب حاصل ہو تحقیق کے طور پر قواعد سے مراد ایسے قضا یا کلیہ ہیں جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک مقدمہ واقع ہوتے ہیں یعنی اگر دلیل قیاس استثنائی سے پیش کی جائے تو اس کا ملازمہ کلیہ قضیہ کلیہ واقع ہوتا ہے اور اگر دلیل قیاس اقترانی کے ذریعہ پیش کی جائے تو شکل اول کا کبری قضیہ کلیہ بنتا ہے اس کی مزید تفصیل علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے خود کتاب میں کر دی ہے

فوائد قیود
علم بمنزل جنس کے ہے اور توصل کی قید بمنزل فصل کے ہے اس سے علوم عربیہ نکل گئے کیونکہ توصل سے مراد توصل قریب ہے یعنی بغیر واسطہ کے فقہ تک پہنچا دیں کیونکہ بہا میں باء سیبیہ ہے اور الی الفقہ سے معلوم ہورہا ہے کہ توصل فقہ تک بلا واسطہ ہو اور علوم عربیہ سے فقہ تک توصل قریب حاصل نہیں ہوتا علی وجہ اتحقیق یہ فصل ثانی ہے اس سے علم مناظرہ و جدل وغیرہ خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ ان سے مقصود خصم کو الزام دینا ہوتا ہے مسائل فقہ کی تحقیق مقصود نہیں ہوتی
Regarding the aspect that near reacment [to fiqh] is obtained through research: by 'rules' are meant such propositions or universal statements that form one of the two premises of a proof. That is, if the proof is presented through a conjunctive syllogism, its consequent becomes a universal proposition; and if the proof is presented through a disjunctive syllogism, the major premise of the first figure becomes a universal proposition. More detail has been given by Sadr al-Shari'ah himself in the book.

Benefits of the restrictions:
'Knowledge' is like a genus, and the restriction of 'reacment' is like a differentia. By this, the Arabic sciences are excluded because what is meant by 'reacment' is near reacment, i.e., reaching fiqh without an intermediary. The 'ba' in 'biha' is for companionship, and 'ila al-fiqh' indicates that reacment to fiqh is without intermediary. From the Arabic sciences, near reacment to fiqh is not obtained in reality. This is a second differentia. By this, the sciences of debate and disputation etc. are excluded because their purpose is to compel the opponent, not to investigate fiqh issues.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of Usul al-Fiqh. The author explains that 'rules' in the definition refer to universal propositions that serve as premises in logical proofs. He distinguishes between two types of syllogisms: conjunctive (istithna'i) and disjunctive (iqtirani). Then he discusses the restrictions in the definition: 'knowledge' (ilm) is the genus, and 'reacment' (tawassul) is the differentia that excludes Arabic sciences, since they do not directly lead to fiqh. The restriction 'near' (qarib) further excludes sciences like dialectic that aim at debate rather than fiqh investigation. This precision ensures the definition encompasses only the intended science.

Key Terms
توصل (tawassul): Near reacment; bringing one to fiqh directly without intermediary
قواعد (qawa'id): Universal propositions that serve as premises in deduction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the 'rules' (قواعد) in the definition of Usul al-Fiqh refer to?
A) General fiqh principles
B) Universal propositions that are premises in proofs
C) Arabic grammatical rules
D) The rulings of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the science of universal rules (qawa'id) that directly lead to fiqh rulings, distinguishing it from other sciences by its purpose of near reacment.

The Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the subject matter as the four sources focusing on method of deduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DEFINE the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh and DISTINGUISH its perspective from that of Fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh studies the four sources as tools for method, not as direct sources of rulings.

This passage establishes the very subject of Usul al-Fiqh—the four primary sources viewed from a specific angle: how to deduce rulings from them and the relative weight of each. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it sets the foundation for every subsequent rule of deduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
Pinpoint the exact objects of study stated: the four proofs (adillah arba'ah).
The Hanafi school also includes istihsan, but the passage focuses on the primary four.
2
Specify the perspective
The passage says 'from this aspect: that through them the method of deduction and ranks of authority are known.' So the perspective is methodological and hierarchical, not content-focused.
3
Contrast with Fiqh
Compare with fiqh's approach: fiqh extracts detailed rulings, while usul learns the method of deduction.
4
Recognize the practical consequence
This distinction means that usul al-fiqh is the tool for ijtihad, not a collection of rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضوع اصول فقه
اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اربعہ یعنی کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اللہ اجماع اور قیاس ہیں اس حیثیت سے کہ ان سے طریق استنباط اور مراتب حجیت معلوم ہوں خلاصہ یہ کہ فقہ اور اصول فقہ میں علوم کا تو ارد ادلہ پر ہی ہوتا ہے لیکن ڈرود کی حیثیت مختلف ہے کہ فقہ کا ورو د ادلہ پر اس حیثیت سے ہوتا ہے کہ اولہ سے احکام جزئیہ عملیہ کا استخراج ہو سکے اور اصول فقہ کا ورود ادلہ پر اس حیثیت سے ہوتا ہے کہ ان ادلہ اربعہ سے استنباط مسائل اور اجتہاد مسائل کا طریقہ معلوم ہو سکے
Subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh
The subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh is the four proofs: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy. From the aspect that through them the method of deduction and the ranks of authority are known. In summary, both fiqh and usul al-fiqh deal with the proofs, but the manner of dealing is different. Fiqh deals with the proofs so that from them detailed practical rulings can be extracted. Usul al-Fiqh deals with the proofs so that from these four proofs the method of deducing issues and ijtihad may be known.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh. It states that the subject is the four primary sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma), and analogy (qiyas). However, the perspective is specific: the goal is to understand the methods of deduction (istinbat) from these sources and the hierarchy of their authority (maratib al-hujjiyyah). The text contrasts this with fiqh itself: fiqh uses the sources to directly obtain detailed rulings, whereas usul al-fiqh studies the sources to learn the methodology of deriving rulings. Thus, fiqh is the product, and usul is the tool.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter or field of study
ادلہ اربعہ (adillah arba'ah): The four primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes the perspective of Usul al-Fiqh on the four sources from that of Fiqh?
A) Both perspectives are identical.
B) Usul focuses on the method of deduction and authority ranks, while Fiqh extracts specific rulings.
C) Usul focuses on historical context, while Fiqh focuses on text.
D) Usul only deals with Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the methodology for deriving rulings from the four sources, distinct from fiqh which is the collection of those rulings.

The Necessity of Usul al-Fiqh: Answering the Objection of Codification
Defending the need for codified Usul al-Fiqh after the Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Companions did not need codified Usul al-Fiqh and why later generations require it.

Core Idea
The Sahaba's spiritual proximity to revelation made formal rules unnecessary, but later Muslims need systematic deduction.

This passage addresses a common objection: if the best generations did not need Usul al-Fiqh, why was it developed later? The author provides two complementary answers—one based on the unique spiritual capacity of early Muslims, and another on the historical process of disciplinarization. Understanding this defense is essential for appreciating the legitimacy and necessity of Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What exactly is the critique? The objection states that the Companions (Sahaba) lived without codified Usul al-Fiqh, so why did later scholars create it?
The objection is that if the best generation didn't need it, it may be an innovation.
2
Analyze the first answer: spiritual purity
The author says the Companions had 'jala-e-qalbi' (purity of heart) and direct company of the Prophet, enabling intuitive deduction without rules.
This is a unique quality that later generations lack.
3
Analyze the second answer: historical development
Alternatively, the Sahaba knew these principles but did not compile them as a separate discipline, just as other sciences were not codified then.
Later, when all sciences were systematized, Usul al-Fiqh was also codified.
4
Evaluate why later generations cannot be analogized to the Sahaba
The text warns: 'since later people did not possess this characteristic, they cannot be compared to those blessed personalities.' So the analogy fails.
The need for rules arises because of increased incidents and loss of spiritual ability.
5
Conclude the necessity of Usul al-Fiqh
Man's actions are endless, new events occur until Judgment Day, so systematic rules (qawa'id) are needed to deduce rulings from the sources.
This is a rational necessity for consistent fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضرورت ایں فن
عام طور پر یہ اشکال عوام و خواص کی زباں زد ہے کہ دین کا مدار صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کی قدسیہ صفات جماعت پر ہے جبکہ ان کے دور میں ان علوم یعنی فقہ اصول فقہ اصول حدیث اصول تغییر وغیرہ کو مدون نہیں کیا گیا اور نہ ہی اس کی ضرورت کبھی گئی پھر آخر خیر القرون کے ادوار کے بعد ان کو مدون کرنے کی ضرورت کیوں پیش آئی ؟
جواب:۔ اس اشکال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ انسان کو بیہ کار اور سدی پیدا نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ اس کے ہر فعل کے ساتھ کوئی نہ کوئی حکم شرعی متعلق ہے اور افعال انسانیت غیر متناہی ہیں نئے نئے حوادثات و واقعات روز بروز معرض وجود میں آتے رہتے ہیں اور قیامت تک ان کا اضافہ ہوتا رہے گا اب ہر فعل اور جزئی کا حکم معلوم کرنا مشکل ہے اس لئے ایسے قواعد کی تدوین کی ضرورت

تھی جن کے ذریعے سے احکام کو دلائل شرعیہ سے مستنبط کرنے کا طریقہ معلوم ہو سکے
باقی رہا یہ اعتراض که صحابه کرام و تابعین عظام کے دور میں اس کی ضرورت کیوں پیش نہ آئی ؟ تو اس عقدہ کا حل یہ ہے کہ صحابہ کرام اپنی جلا قلبی اور صحبت نبوی کے فیض کے باعث اس فن سے اور ایسے قواعد کے معلوم کرنے سے مستغنی تھے یعنی نور نبوت کے مشاہدہ کی وجہ سے ان کے دلوں میں اپنی استعداد پیدا ہو گئی تھی کہ بغیر وسائل کے اور بغیر راستوں کے متعین کرنے کے وہ مقصود تک پہنچ جاتے تھے یعنی بغیر ان قواعد کی احتیاج کے ان کو جزئیات کے احکام معلوم کرنے کی استعداد و صلاحیت حاصل تھی اسی طرح تابعین بھی حضور کے زمانہ کے قریب تھے اور ان کے عقائد بھی درست تھے اور حوادثات اور واقعات بھی قلیل الوقوع تھے اور ان کو ثقات کی طرف مراجعت کی قدرت بھی حاصل تھی اس لئے وہ بھی اس فن سے مستغنی تھے چونکہ یہ خصوصیت بعد میں آنے والے لوگوں کو حاصل نہ تھی اس لئے ان کو ان برگزیدہ شخصیات پر قیاس نہیں کیا جا سکتا فافهم فانہ دقیق نیز اس کو آپ یوں بھی تعبیر کر سکتے ہیں کہ صحابہ کرام اور تابعین کو گو یہ اصول اور قواعد معلوم تھے لیکن ان کے عہد میں دوسرے علوم کی طرح اس علم یعنی اصول فقہ نے بھی صنعت اور فن کی صورت اختیار نہ کی تھی اس لئے جہاں اور علوم کی تدوین اس دور میں نہیں ہوئی وہیں اصول فقہ کی تدوین بھی عمل میں نہیں آئی اور چونکہ عہد صحابہ گزر جانے کے بعد ہر علم نے فن اور صنعت کی صورت اختیار کی تو اس فن کی تدوین بھی صنعت کی شکل میں کی گئی
Need for this science:
Commonly, this objection is on the tongues of commoners and elites: that the religion is based on the sanctified qualities of the Companions - may Allah be pleased with them all - while in their era these sciences (Fiqh, Usul al-Fiqh, Principles of Hadith, Principles of Exegesis, etc.) were not codified, nor was there ever a need for them. Then why after the era of the best generations did the need arise to codify them?
Answer: The answer to this objection is that man was not created idle and in vain; rather, every action of his has some legal ruling attached to it. Human actions are infinite; new events and occurrences keep appearing day by day, and they will continue to increase until the Day of Judgment. Now it is difficult to know the ruling of every action and particular incident. Therefore, there arose a need to codify such rules

through which the method of deducing rulings from the legal proofs could be known.
As for the remaining objection: why did this need not arise in the era of the noble Companions and the great Successors? The solution to this knot is that the Companions, due to their purity of heart and the blessing of the company of the Prophet, were independent of this science and of knowing such rules. That is, through observing the light of prophethood, an ability was created in their hearts that they would reach the goal without means and without defining paths. That is, they had the ability and capacity to know the rulings of particulars without needing these rules. Similarly, the Successors were close to the time of the Prophet, their beliefs were correct, events and occurrences were few, and they had the ability to refer to reliable authorities. Therefore, they too were independent of this science. Since later people did not possess this characteristic, they cannot be compared to those blessed personalities. So understand, for it is delicate. Also, you can express it in this way: that the Companions and Successors, although they knew these principles and rules, yet in their era this science of Usul al-Fiqh, like other sciences, had not taken the form of an art and discipline. Therefore, just as other sciences were not codified in that period, so too Usul al-Fiqh was not codified. And since after the era of the Companions passed, every science took the form of an art and discipline, so the codification of this science was also done in the form of a discipline.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage addresses a common objection: if the Sahaba and Tabi'un did not need codified Usul al-Fiqh, why was it developed later? The author gives two key answers. First, man's actions are endless, and new events constantly arise, making it necessary to have systematic rules to deduce rulings from the sources. Second, the Sahaba and Tabi'un had a unique spiritual purity and proximity to the Prophet that enabled them to derive rulings intuitively without formal rules. Later generations lack this, so they need codified principles. An alternative explanation is that the Sahaba knew these principles but did not compile them as a distinct discipline until later, when all fields were systematized. The author emphasizes that the later generations cannot be analogized to the Sahaba in this regard.

Key Terms
جلا قلبی (jala-e-qalbi): Purity and clarity of heart, a spiritual quality that enabled intuitive understanding
مستغنی (mustaghni): Independent, not needing something

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason later generations needed codified Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Because the Sahaba asked them to create it.
B) Because human actions are infinite and new events occur continuously, making systematic deduction necessary.
C) Because the Sahaba made mistakes in rulings.
D) Because the Prophet ordered it after his death.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is not an innovation but a necessary development to systematically derive rulings for ever-new situations, compensating for the loss of the unique spiritual capacity of the early Muslims.

Historical Survey of Usul al-Fiqh Compilations
Historical survey of usul al-fiqh literature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the development of usul al-fiqh literature from the 2nd to 7th century, identifying key works and their authors and the scholarly trends of each period.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh literature evolved through foundation, mutakallimun dominance, rational deduction, and then abridgment and commentary.

This lesson provides a historical overview of the compilations of usul al-fiqh, spanning from the 2nd to the 7th century Hijri. Understanding this timeline helps contextualize the sources and methods you will study later. You will see how the field progressed from early efforts to comprehensive works, and later to concise manuals and their commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the century divisions
The passage is organized by century. Note the chronological sequence and the approximate dates of key works in each period.
Historians often divide the development into early (2nd-4th), middle (5th-7th), and later (8th-13th) periods.
2
Note key authors and works per century
For each century, list the prominent books and their authors. For example, in the 3rd century, al-Maturidi's Kitab al-Jadal and Makhidh al-Shar'; in the 4th, al-Jassas's Kitab al-Usul.
Some works are cited as foundational in the Hanafi tradition.
3
Recognize the dominant scholarly style
Observe that in the 5th century the mutakallimun style became prominent, while the 6th century focused on logical deduction. The 7th century saw a blend of juristic and mutakallim approaches.
This stylistic shift affected how legal principles were argued and taught.
4
Understand the later trend of abridgment and commentary
After the 7th century, scholars prioritized concise works for easy memorization, leading to abridgments like al-Tanqih and commentaries like al-Tawdih and al-Talwih.
These later works became central in Hanafi usul curricula.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويح لحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح وَالتَّلويج یه کوشش دوسری صدی ہجری کے آخر میں ہوئی اصول فقہ اور تیسری صدی تیسری صدی کے شروع میں شیخ ابو منصور ماتریدی علیہ الرحمہ نے اصول فقہ میں دو کتابیں تصنیف کیں (۱) کتاب الجدل (۲) ماخذ الشرع یہ دونوں کتابیں غایت احکام اور اتقان میں بے مثل ہیں اور ان میں اصول و فروع کو کثرت سے ذکر کیا گیا ہے اصول فقہ اور چوتھی صدی اس صدی میں اصول فقہ کی متعدد کتابیں معرض وجود میں آئیں اور اس دور کی عمدہ ترین کتابیں دو ہیں (۱) کتاب الذخیرہ جو شیخ احمد بن برہان فارسی کی تالیف ہے (۲) کتاب الاصول جو امام ابو بکر جصاص احمد بن علی حنفی کی تصنیف ہے۔ اصول فقہ اور پانچویں صدی اس صدی میں علماء نے اس فن پر بہت زیادہ کام کیا جس کے نتیجہ میں تقریبا دس عمدہ کتابیں وجود میں آئیں مثلاً (۱) الانوار (۲) تقویم الادلہ (۳) کفایه (۴) تبصره (۵) تذكرة العالم والطريق السالم (۶) اللہ (۷) کتاب البرہان (۸) اصول فخر اسلام ( کشف) جس کے ضوابط کو علامہ صدر الشریعہ نے تنقیح میں ذکر کیا ہے لیکن اس دور میں اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں متکلمانہ طرز نمایاں ہے یعنی اکثر کتابوں کی تصنیف متکلمین کے طرز پر کی گئی ہے جن میں اہل بدعت پر الزام طرزنمایاں اور ان پر سخت تنقید کی گئی ہے اصول فقہ اور چھٹی صدی چھٹی صدی میں جو کہتا ہیں اصول فقہ میں تصنیف کی گئیں ان میں استدلال اور احتجاج کی طرف زیادہ میلان ہے یعنی دلائل کو منطقی انداز میں پیش کیا گیا ہے اور اس دور کی مشہور کتا ہیں یہ ہیں (۱) الاصول جو علامہ قاضی القضاة حنفی کی تصنیف ہے (۲) المغنی (۳) محصول جو علامہ فخر الدین رازی کی تصنیف ہے اور تنقیح میں اس کا خلاصہ بھی موجود ہے اصول فقہ اور ساتویں صدی اس دور میں اصول فقہ پر کئی کتب تصنیف کی گئیں اور ان میں سے اکثر کتابوں میں قواعد پر مسائل کی تفریح کی طرف زیادہ توجہ دیہ گئی ہے اور کچھ کتابوں میں فقیہانہ اور متکلمانہ دونوں طرزوں کو جمع کیا گیا ہے اس کے بعد تیرہویں صدی تک فن اصول فقہ پر تصنیفات کا سلسلہ جاری رہا لیکن ان ادوار میں اکثر پہلے والی مفصل کتب کا اختصار کیا گیا ہے اور اس پر توجہ دی گئی ہے کہ اصول فقہ کے مسائل کو کم از کم الفاظ میں سمیٹ دیا جائے تاکہ طلباء کیلئے یاد کرنا آسان ہو چنانچہ حسامی المنار تنقیح وغیرہ کو دیکھنے سے یہ بات واضح ہو جاتی ہے پھر انہی ادوار میں بعض لوگوں نے ان مختصر کتابوں کی تشریح بھی کی ہے مثلا نور الانوار توضیح تلویح و غیره
Al-Tarwih li Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. This effort occurred at the end of the second century Hijri. Usul al-fiqh and the third century: At the beginning of the third century, Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, may Allah have mercy on him, authored two books on usul al-fiqh: (1) Kitab al-Jadal, (2) Makhidh al-Shar'. Both books are unparalleled in extreme precision and perfection, and they mention many principles and branches. Usul al-fiqh and the fourth century: In this century, numerous books on usul al-fiqh came into existence, and the best books of this period are two: (1) Kitab al-Dhakhirah, written by Shaykh Ahmad ibn Burhan al-Farsi, (2) Kitab al-Usul, written by Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hanafi. Usul al-fiqh and the fifth century: In this century, scholars worked extensively on this science, resulting in about ten excellent books, e.g., (1) al-Anwar, (2) Taqwim al-Adillah, (3) Kifayah, (4) Tabsirah, (5) Tadhkirat al-Alim wa al-Tariq al-Salim, (6) Allah (perhaps a typo for al-Luma'), (7) Kitab al-Burhan, (8) Usul Fakhr al-Islam (Kashf), whose principles were mentioned by Allamah Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tanqih. But in this period, the mutakallimun style is prominent in usul books, that is, most books were authored in the style of the mutakallimun, showing refutation of the innovators and severe criticism. Usul al-fiqh and the sixth century: In the sixth century, the books authored in usul al-fiqh show a tendency towards deduction and argumentation, i.e., presenting evidences in a logical manner. The famous books of this period are: (1) al-Usul, authored by Allamah Qadi al-Qudat al-Hanafi, (2) al-Mughni, (3) al-Mahsul, authored by Allamah Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, and its summary is also present in al-Tanqih. Usul al-fiqh and the seventh century: In this period, several books on usul al-fiqh were written, and most of these books paid more attention to deriving issues from the principles. Some books combined both the jurist and mutakallim styles. After this, the series of compilations on usul al-fiqh continued until the thirteenth century. But in these later periods, mostly the earlier detailed books were abridged, and attention was given to summarizing the issues of usul al-fiqh in the fewest words so that it would be easy for students to memorize. Thus, looking at Husami al-Manar, al-Tanqih, etc., this becomes clear. Then, in the same periods, some people also wrote commentaries on these abridged books, for example, Nur al-Anwar, al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, etc.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a historical survey of usul al-fiqh literature. It begins by noting that efforts started at the end of the 2nd century Hijri. Then it proceeds century by century, listing key works and their authors. The 3rd century saw al-Maturidi's works. The 4th century highlights al-Dhakhirah and al-Usul by al-Jassas. The 5th century is noted for the prominence of the mutakallimun style, with works like al-Anwar and Kashf, which was later used by Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tanqih. The 6th century shows a shift towards logical deduction, with al-Mahsul by al-Razi being summarized in al-Tanqih. The 7th century combined juristic and mutakallim approaches. After that, the trend was abridgment and commentary, aiming for easy memorization, leading to works like Nur al-Anwar, al-Tawdih, and al-Talwih.

Key Terms
متکلمین (mutakallimūn): Scholarly theologians who used dialectical methods to defend Islamic beliefs, often incorporating their approach into usul al-fiqh.
تفریع (tafrī‘): Derivation of subsidiary rulings from principles. The passage notes that in the 7th century, attention was given to deriving issues from principles.
تنقیح (Tanqīḥ): An abridged work on usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shariah, based on earlier works like Kashf and al-Mahsul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which century did the mutakallimun style become prominent in usul al-fiqh books, according to the passage?
A) 3rd century
B) 4th century
C) 5th century
D) 6th century

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh literature evolved through distinct phases: early foundational works, dominance of mutakallimun, shift to logical deduction, and later abridgment and commentary for pedagogical ease.

The Four Elements of a Scholarly Introduction in Usul al-Fiqh
Explanation of the typical structure of a book's introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four typical components of an author's introduction in Hanafi usul works and explain why a commentator adds a fifth element.

Core Idea
Every Hanafi usul book's introduction reveals its purpose, scope, and method — a key to understanding the text.

When you open a classical Hanafi usul al-fiqh text, the introduction is not decorative. It is a structured statement of the author's method, purpose, and choice of subject. This lesson unpacks that convention, based on the commentator's own explanation. Understanding this framework will help you read any Hanafi usul work with better comprehension of the author's intent.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the authorial habit
The passage states that authors generally mention four matters. Identify that this is a meta-commentary on book structure.
This is a convention observed across Islamic scholarly works.
2
List the first three points
These are: (1) reason for choosing the discipline, (2) purpose of compilation, (3) description of the book's qualities.
3
Identify the fourth point for commentators
A commentator adds the reason for choosing the base text (matn) and the book he is commenting on.
This is an additional element beyond the first three.
4
Apply to the current text
Note that the author of this commentary (Sharh al-Tawdih) is following this pattern, as implied by the passage.
The passage is itself part of the introduction of that commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمہیدی مقدمہ :۔ عام طور پر مصنفین کی عادت ہے کہ وہ کتاب کے شروع میں مندرجہ ذیل امور بیان کرتے ہیں (۱) علت تعیین فن یعنی یہ بیان کرتے ہیں کہ کتاب لکھنے کے لئے اس فن کو کیوں منتخب کیا (۲) وجہ تالیف یعنی کتاب لکھنے کی غرض بیان کرتے ہیں (۳) کیفیت مصنف یعنی اپنی کتاب کی صفات بیان کرتے ہیں کہ میری یہ کتاب کس طرز پر لکھی گئی ہے (۴) اور اگر مصیف شاریخ ہو تو مذکورہ امور کے علاوہ وہ علت تعیین کتاب و متن بھی ذکر کرتا ہے یعنی میں نے شرح لکھنے کے لئے اس
Preliminary discourse: It is generally the habit of authors that at the beginning of the book they mention the following matters: (1) The reason for choosing the subject—that is, they explain why they selected this particular discipline for writing the book. (2) The reason for compilation—that is, they state the purpose of writing the book. (3) The quality of the work—that is, they describe the characteristics of their book and the style in which it is written. (4) And if the author is a commentator, then in addition to the above matters, he also mentions the reason for choosing the book and the matn, i.e., 'I selected this [book] for commentary'.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This section is a methodological note explaining the standard structure of introductions in Islamic scholarly works. The commentator outlines four common elements: (1) the reason for choosing the discipline (like usul al-fiqh), (2) the purpose of writing (to benefit students or clarify issues), (3) a description of the book's style and features, and (4) for commentaries specifically, the reason for selecting the base text (matn) and the book itself. This framework helps the reader understand the author's intentions and the context of the work. The passage ends abruptly, but the intended point is that the commentator of this very work (Sharh al-Tawdih) is following this pattern, having already praised his book and author.

Key Terms
متن (matn): The base text being commented upon.
شرح (sharh): A commentary on a matn, explaining its meanings and arguments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preliminary discourse, what is the fourth point that a commentator should mention in the introduction?
A) The reason for choosing the discipline
B) The purpose of writing the book
C) The quality of his own work
D) The reason for choosing the specific book and matn for commentary

Key Takeaway
The introduction of a Hanafi usul work is a structured methodological statement, not mere formality; it sets the stage for understanding the author's purpose and method.

Metaphor of 'Mannassah' for Revealed Meanings
Explains 'mannassah' metaphor for textual meanings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'mannassah' and explain its metaphorical significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the nature of derived rulings as divine decrees uncovered through ijtihad.

Core Idea
Derived rulings are divine decrees unveiled, not human inventions.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary uses a striking metaphor to clarify a foundational principle: the rulings that mujtahids derive from the Quran and Sunnah are not their own creative products but rather divine decrees that are displayed and clarified through the texts. The metaphor of the bride on the platform (mannassah) elegantly captures this idea. As you work through this lesson, you will unpack both the linguistic meaning of mannassah and its deeper implications for understanding ijtihad in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Linguistic breakdown
Begin by understanding the literal meaning of 'mannassah' (منصة). The text tells us it is a place where a bride is raised for display, derived from the root 'nasasa' meaning 'to raise'. Note that the word 'arus' applies to both male and female during their wedding.
The linguistic analysis sets the stage for the metaphor.
2
Identify the metaphor
Now see how the commentator extends the literal meaning: the meanings (ma'ani) shown through the texts (nusus) and clarified to the beholders are like the bride on the platform. The rulings derived (ahkam mustafadah) are the 'bride' – beautiful and displayed – while the texts are the 'platform' that elevates them.
The bride represents the revealed meaning; the platform represents the textual evidence.
3
Extract the principle
The key legal principle is that these derived rulings are not the 'results of the thinkers' thoughts' (nata'ij afkarihim) but rather divine rulings from the 'true and clear King'. Hence, ijtihad does not create rulings; it uncovers pre-existing divine determinations.
This is a core Hanafi tenet that distinguishes the school from those who view ijtihad as more constructive.
4
Contrast with the misconception
Finally, reflect on the common misunderstanding that mujtahids invent rulings. The metaphor shows that just as a bride is already there before being displayed, the rulings are already present in the divine law; the mujtahid's role is to contemplate and extract them accurately.
This reinforces the objective nature of shari'ah rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ مَنَصَّةٌ بِفَتح المِيمِ المَكَانُ الَّذِي يُرْفَعُ عَلَيْهِ العَرُوسُ لِلجِلَوَةِ مِن نَصَصْتَ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا رَفَعَتَهُ وَالعَرُوسُ نَعَتْ يَستَوِى فِيهِ الرَّجُلُ وَالمَرأَةُ مَا دَامَا فِي إعْرَاسِهِمَا يُجمَعُ المُؤَنَّتُ عَلَى عَرَايْسَ وَالمُذَكَّرُ عَلَى عُرُسٍ بِضَمَّتَينِ وَفِي هَذَا الكَلَامِ نَوعُ خَزَازَةٍ لِأَنَّ المَعَانِيَ الَّتِي أُظْهِرَت بِالنُّصُوصِ وَجُلِيَت بِهَا عَلَى النَّاظِرِينَ هِىَ مَفهُومَاتُهَا وَالأحكامُ المُستَفَادَةُ مِنهَا وَهِيَ لَيسَت نَتَايْجَ أَفَكَارِ المُتَفَكْرِينَ بَل أَحكَامُ المَلِكِ الحَقِّ المُبِينِ فَكَأَنَّهُ أَرَادَ أَنَّ المُجْتَهِدِينَ يَتَأَمَّلُونَ فِي النُّصُوصِ فَيَطَّلِعُونَ عَلَى مَعَانِ وَدَفَائِقَ وَيَسْتَخْرِجُونَ أَحَكَامًا وَحَقَائِقَ وَهِيَ نتائج أفكارهم الظَّاهِرَةِ عَلَى النُّصُوص بِمَنزِلَةِ الْعَرُوسِ عَلَى المَنَصَّةِ .
His statement: 'mannassah' with a fatha on the meem is the place upon which the bride is raised for display, from 'nasastu al-shay'a' meaning 'I raised it'. The bride is called 'arus' (male and female alike while in their wedding). The feminine plural is 'ara'is' and the masculine plural is 'urus' with two dammas. In this speech there is a kind of elegance, because the meanings that are shown through the texts and clarified by them to the beholders are their concepts and the rulings derived from them. They are not the results of the thinkers' thoughts, but the rulings of the true and clear King. So it is as if he intended that the mujtahids contemplate the texts and attain meanings and subtleties and extract rulings and truths, which are the results of their thoughts apparent upon the texts, just like the bride upon the platform.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage defines 'mannassah' (منصة) as a platform upon which a bride is displayed. The commentator then uses it as a metaphor: the meanings and rulings that mujtahids derive from the Quranic and Hadith texts are not products of their own minds; rather, they are divine rulings that they uncover through contemplation. Just as a bride is displayed on a platform for everyone to see, so too the meanings of the texts are displayed and clarified. The mujtahid's role is to reflect and extract, but the rulings themselves are from Allah. This emphasizes that ijtihad does not create rulings but discovers them, a key Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
منصة (mannassah): A platform on which the bride is raised for display; used metaphorically to describe how the meanings of texts are presented to observers.
نتائج أفكارهم (nata'ij afkarihim): Results of their thoughts; the passage clarifies that the derived rulings are not mere products of human thinking but divine decrees made manifest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the metaphor of the bride on the platform (mannassah) illustrate?
A) That brides should be displayed publicly
B) That derived rulings are created by mujtahids
C) That the meanings of texts are manifested and displayed to observers
D) That the Quran is like a bride

Key Takeaway
The mannassah metaphor powerfully illustrates that fiqh rulings uncovered by ijtihad are divine decrees made manifest, not human constructions.

Author's Reason for Selecting al-Bazdawi's Usul
Author's preface explaining his choice of base text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the methodological reasons an author selects a particular text for a commentary and apply this to understanding the purpose of Tanqih al-Usul.

Core Idea
An author's choice of base text reveals his scholarly method and the problems he seeks to solve.

In this preface, the author explains why he chose Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh as the foundation for his own work, Tanqih al-Usul. His reasons are not arbitrary; they reflect the scholarly context of his time and his specific goals. Understanding this choice helps us appreciate the purpose of the Tanqih and its place in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated reasons
From the tashrih commentary, list the three reasons given for selecting al-Bazdawi's work.
Reasons: (1) all scholars were turning to it, (2) its meanings were hidden in difficult expressions, (3) some scholars criticized it based on apparent reading.
2
Analyze each reason methodologically
Consider what each reason implies about the text's authority, the need for clarification, and the defensive aim of the commentary.
Widespread use indicates authority; hidden meanings justify the need for a commentary; criticism requires a refutation.
3
Connect to the author's work Tanqih
Explain how the Tanqih addresses each of the three issues: it clarifies the text, defends it, and provides a refined version.
The title 'Tanqih' itself means 'refinement', suggesting improvement and clarification.
4
Assess the rhetorical style of the preface
The author uses a rhetorical comparison between i'jaz (inimitability) and sihr (magic) to illustrate his stylistic choices. Understand what this shows about his literary approach.
The comparison may indicate the author's attempt to demonstrate eloquence and methodological precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويح تھا ضبط اور اختصار کے طریق پر ۔ چنگل مارنے والا تھا۔ سحر کے پھندنوں کے ساتھ مضبوطی سے پکڑنے والا تھا اعجاز [?] کڑے کو ) ۔ اختیار کیا اعجاز میں عروہ کو اور سحر میں احد اب کو اس لیے کہ اعجاز مضبوط ہے اور زیادہ با اعتماد ہے سحر سے ۔ اور اختیار کیا عروہ میں واحد کے لفظ کو اور احد اب میں جمع کے لفظ کو اس لیے کہ کلام میں اعجاز یہ ہے کہ معنی کو ایسے طریقہ پر ادا کیا جائے جو اس کے ماسوا تمام طریقوں سے زیادہ بلیغ ہو۔ اور نہیں ہو سکتا اس کا طریق مگر ایک لیکن سحرفی الکلام پس وہ اعجاز سے کم درجہ ہے۔ اور اس کے طرق ایک سے زائد ہیں پس لایا اس میں جمع کے لفظ کو۔ اور نام رکھا میں نے اس کا تنقیح الاصول کے ساتھ اور اللہ تعالیٰ سے سوال ہے یہ کہ نفع دے اس کے ساتھ اس کے مصنف کو اور اس کے کاتب کو اور اس کے پڑھنے والے کو اور اس کے طالب کو اور بنائے اس کو خالص اپنی ذات کریم کے لیے۔ تحقیق وہی نیکی قبول کرنے والا ہے۔ رحم کرنے والا ہے۔
تالیف تنقیح کیلئے اصول فخر الاسلام کو متعین کرنے کی وجہ
تشریح:۔ اس عبارت میں ماتن نے علت تعیین متن کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ میں نے تنقیح لکھنے کے لیے فخر الاسلام علی بزدوی کی کتاب اصول فقہ کو چند وجوہ سے متعین کیا ہے ۔ (۱) اس وقت کے سارے علماء اس کتاب کی طرف متوجہ تھے۔ (۲) اس کتاب کے معانی اس کی مشکل عبارتوں میں بند تھے ۔ میں نے سوچا کہ تشریح کردوں۔ (۳) بعض علماء اس کتاب کی ظاہری عبارت دیکھ کرطعن کرتے تھے میں نے ان کا رد کرنے کے لیے تنقیح لکھی ہے۔
Promotion for solving al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. It was on the method of discipline and brevity. It was one who clutches. It was one who grasps firmly with the snares of magic. I chose in i'jaz 'urwa and in sihr ahadab because i'jaz is stronger and more reliable than sihr. And I chose in 'urwa the singular word and in ahadab the plural word because i'jaz in speech is to convey meaning in a way that is more eloquent than all other ways, and it cannot have more than one way. But sihr in speech is lower than i'jaz and its ways are multiple, so I used the plural word. And I named it Tanqih al-Usul. And I ask Allah the Exalted to benefit by it its author, its scribe, its reader, its seeker, and to make it purely for His noble sake. Truly He is the acceptor of good deeds, the Merciful. The reason for selecting the Usul of Fakhr al-Islam for composing Tanqih. Commentary: In this passage the matn author mentioned the reason for selecting the text: I selected Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali al-Bazdawi's book of Usul al-Fiqh for writing Tanqih for several reasons: (1) All scholars of the time were turning to this book. (2) The meanings of this book were locked in its difficult expressions; I thought I would explain them. (3) Some scholars criticized the book by looking at its apparent expression; I wrote Tanqih to refute them.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is from the preface of the commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. The author (the commentator) explains his motivation for writing this work. He states that he selected the famous Hanafi usul work by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi as the basis for his own book, Tanqih al-Usul. The reasons are practical: first, it was widely studied; second, its dense expressions needed clarification; third, some critics misunderstood it based on surface reading, so he aimed to defend it. The passage also includes a prayer and a brief rhetorical discussion comparing i'jaz (inimitability) and sihr (magic) in speech, which serves as an example of the author's stylistic choice. The commentary section (Tashrih) elaborates on these reasons.

Key Terms
تنقیح الاصول (Tanqih al-Usul): The title of the author's own work, meaning 'Refinement of the Principles'.
فخر الاسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific title of 'Ali al-Bazdawi, a prominent Hanafi usuli scholar.
اعجاز (i'jaz): Inimitability; the quality of being matchless, especially in the context of the Qur'an.
سحر (sihr): Magic; here used metaphorically for eloquent but lesser speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tashrih, which of the following is NOT a reason the author selected al-Bazdawi's work?
A) It was widely studied.
B) Its meanings were obscure.
C) It needed correction of grammatical errors.
D) Some scholars criticized it based on apparent meaning.

Key Takeaway
The choice of a base text for a commentary is a deliberate methodological decision, often driven by the text's authority, complexity, and the need to defend it against critics.

Author's Criticism of Fakhr al-Islam and Precedence of Early Scholars
Commentary analyzing author's criticism and defending early scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the linguistic nuances in the author's indirect criticism of Fakhr al-Islam and justify the precedence of early Hanafi scholars over later ones.

Core Idea
Ta'rid is indirect criticism: the author's word choice reveals his assessment of Fakhr al-Islam's work and defends the primacy of early scholars.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the author's choice of words in the matn, revealing a veiled criticism of Fakhr al-Islam's usul work. He defines key terms like 'tanqih' and 'tanzim' to show that the author believed Fakhr al-Islam's principles needed pruning and ordering. He then counters a potential misunderstanding that later scholars who refine usul are superior, affirming that early scholars who extracted principles from the primary sources hold a higher rank.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the Linguistic Definitions
Identify and understand the precise meanings of 'nazar', 'lafz', 'lihaz', 'tanqih', and 'tanzim' as provided. Note how these terms carry connotations of depth, cursory glance, refinement, and ordering.
These terms are not merely lexical; they are used by the author to frame his criticism.
2
Unpack the Ta'rid (Indirect Criticism)
Recognize that by using 'tanqih', the author indicates Fakhr al-Islam's usul contained excesses that needed removal. By 'tanzim', he indicates the contents were disorganized. The author then claims to have rectified both issues.
The commentator explicitly labels this as 'ta'rid' – indirect criticism.
3
Examine the Rebuttal of Potential Doubt
Understand the commentator's argument: early scholars are superior because they extracted the foundational jewels from the Qur'an and hadith. Later scholars only organize and refine; thus they do not surpass the early masters in rank.
This rebuttal addresses a common misconception that refinement implies superiority.
4
Apply Pronoun Tracking
Trace the pronoun 'fihi' and subsequent pronouns. Note that they refer to 'tanqih', not the entire book of usul al-fiqh. This clarifies the focus of the author's criticism.
Misidentifying the referent would lead to misunderstanding the entire passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنظر التامل : لغوی تحقیق بیان کی ہے ۔ نظر کا معنی ہے کسی چیز کو خوب غور کے ساتھ دیکھنا۔ اور لفظ کا معنی ہوتا ہے کسی چیز کو آنکھ کے کنارے سے دیکھنا یعنی سرسری دیکھنا۔ اسی مناسبت سے لحاظ آنکھ کے کنارے کو کہتے ہیں ۔ اور تنقیح کا معنیٰ ہے تہذیب ۔ مثلاً جب تو ان زائد ٹہنیوں کو کاٹ دے جو تنے کے سر میں نہ ہوں تو تو کہتا ہے، قتحت الجذع ، اور تنظیم کا معنی ہوتا ہے موتیوں کو دھاگے میں پرونا اس ترتیب کے ساتھ جو مناسب ہو۔
ماتن کی فخر الاسلام پر تعریض
والکلام لا تخلو :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے کہ ماتن نے فخر الاسلام پر تعریض کی ہے۔ تعریض کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اشارہ چوٹ کرنا ۔ یعنی تنقیح میں اشارہ کیا ہے۔ کہ فخر الاسلام کے اصول میں کچھ زوائد تھے جن کو حذف کرنا واجب تھا۔ اور تنظیم میں اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ فخر الاسلام کی کتاب کے مضامین بکھرے ہوئے تھے جن کو ترتیب دینا ضروری تھا۔ تو میں نے ان کو مرتب کر دیا ہے اور حاولت تعیین مرادہ، میں اس طرف اشارہ کیا کہ وہ کتاب مشکل تھی میں نے اس کو آسان کر دیا ہے اور علی قواعد المعقول ،، میں اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے کہ اصول فقہ منطقی قواعد پرمشتمل نہ تھی بایں طور پر کہ تعریفات اور حج میں ان شرائط کی رعایت رکھی جائے ۔ جو علم میزان میں مذکور ہیں ۔ جن شرائط کی وجہ سے ایک قسم کی تعریف دوسری قسم پر صادق نہیں آتی۔
متقدمیں رتبہ متاخرین سے فائق ہیں
ممالم يلتفت الیہ المشائخ :۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے ایک وہ کا ازالہ کیا ہےکہ علامہ فخرالاسلام مشائخ میں سے ہیں اور مشائخ کا مقصود معانی ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ الفاظ کی بناوٹ و سجاوٹ ۔ اس لیے یہ وہم نہ کیا جائے کہ متاخرین کا درجہ متقدمین سے زیادہ ہو گیا۔ بلکہ متقدمین کی فضلیت متاخرین سے زیادہ ہے۔ اس لیے کہ متقدمین نے قرآن وحدیث کے سمندر سے جواہر نکال دیے ہیں اب متأخرین کا کام ہے کہ ان کو تر تیب دیں۔ قولہ موراد فیہ:۔ اس عبارت میں صرف ایک بات بیان فرمائی ہے کہ فیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع تنقیح ہے اور اس سے آگے بھی جتنی ضمیریں ہیں سب تنقیح کی طرف راجع ہیں۔ اور یہ بات بتانے کی ضرورت اس لیے پیش آئی کہ اس سے ماقبل جتنی بھی ضمیر میں تھیں وہ کتاب اصول فقہ کی طرف راجع تھیں۔ تو یہ وہم ہو سکتا تھا کہ فیہ کی ضمیر کا مرجع بھی اصول فقہ ہے۔ اس لیے وہم کو دور کر دیا اور تصریح کردی کہ مرجع اصول فقہ نہیں بلکہ تنقیح ہے۔
And 'nazar' and 'ta'ammul': a linguistic investigation is explained. The meaning of 'nazar' is to look at something with deep reflection. And the meaning of 'lafz' is to look at something from the corner of the eye, i.e., a cursory look. Hence, 'lihaz' is called the corner of the eye. And 'tanqih' means refinement; for example, when you cut off the excess branches that are not at the top of the trunk, you say 'qata'tu al-jidh'a'. And 'tanzim' means stringing pearls in a thread in a suitable order. The author's criticism of Fakhr al-Islam: 'Wa al-kalam la takhlu': this is the last part of the commentary's expression. In this expression, the commentator explains the text, that the author criticized Fakhr al-Islam. 'Ta'rid' means to make an indirect attack. That is, in 'tanqih' he indicated that there were some excesses in Fakhr al-Islam's principles which had to be removed. And in 'tanzim' he indicated that the contents of Fakhr al-Islam's book were scattered, needing to be arranged. So I have organized them, and 'wa hawwaltu ta'yin muradahu' I indicated that the book was difficult, I have made it easy, and 'ala qawa'id al-ma'qul' I indicated that usul al-fiqh was not based on logical principles in the sense that definitions and proofs observe the conditions mentioned in the science of logic, due to which one type of definition does not apply to another type. Early scholars are superior in rank to later scholars: 'Mimmalam yaltafit ilayhi al-mashayikh': In this expression, the commentator removes a doubt that Allamah Fakhr al-Islam is among the mashayikh, and the mashayikh aim at meanings, not the construction and adornment of words. So it should not be imagined that later scholars have a higher rank than early scholars. Rather, the virtue of early scholars is greater than that of later scholars, because early scholars extracted jewels from the ocean of Qur'an and hadith; now the work of later scholars is to organize them. 'Qawlahu murad fihi': In this expression, he states only one thing: that the pronoun 'fihi' refers to 'tanqih', and all subsequent pronouns also refer to 'tanqih'. The need to state this arose because all previous pronouns referred to the book of usul al-fiqh. So it could be imagined that the pronoun 'fihi' also refers to usul al-fiqh. Therefore, he removed the doubt and clarified that the referent is not usul al-fiqh but tanqih.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the author's criticism of Fakhr al-Islam in his work 'Tanqih'. The commentator first provides linguistic definitions of terms like 'nazar' (deep reflection), 'lafz' (cursory glance), 'tanqih' (pruning/refinement), and 'tanzim' (arranging). He then explains the author's indirect criticism ('ta'rid'): the author indicated that Fakhr al-Islam's usul contained unnecessary elements that needed removal, and his book was disorganized, requiring rearrangement. The author also made the work easier and introduced logical standards. The commentator addresses a potential misunderstanding: since Fakhr al-Islam is among the early masters (mashayikh) who focus on meanings, not florid language, later scholars are not superior; rather, early scholars extracted the foundational jewels from Qur'an and hadith, and later ones only organize them. Finally, he clarifies pronoun references to avoid confusion: 'fihi' and subsequent pronouns refer to 'tanqih', not the book of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): deep reflection or careful looking
لحاظ (lihaz): cursory glance from the corner of the eye
تنقیح (tanqih): refinement or pruning away excess
تنظیم (tanzim): arranging in proper order, like stringing pearls
تعریض (ta'rid): indirect criticism or allusion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the author indicate by using the word 'tanqih' in his criticism of Fakhr al-Islam?
A) That Fakhr al-Islam's principles were perfectly arranged
B) That there were excesses in Fakhr al-Islam's principles that needed removal
C) That Fakhr al-Islam's book was too concise
D) That logical standards were unnecessary

Key Takeaway
Tanqih and tanzim are terms of indirect criticism that, when understood alongside the hierarchy of scholars, reveal the author's respect for early masters while allowing refinement.

Defining I'jaz: Unity and Strength vs. Magic's Multiplicity
Definition of i'jaz with contrast to sihr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DEFINE i'jaz according to the Hanafi usul and DISTINGUISH it from sihr al-kalām based on the condition of impossibility of imitation.

Core Idea
I'jaz is a singular, unbreakable limit; sihr is a subtle art with many levels.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the true meaning of i'jaz (inimitability) in the context of Qur'anic speech. He warns against conflating it with mere eloquence and emphasizes that the essence of i'jaz is the impossibility of opposition or imitation. Moreover, he contrasts i'jaz with the magic of speech (sihr al-kalām), which is a human artistry of many levels. Understanding this distinction is fundamental to Hanafi usul al-fiqh, as it underpins the proof of prophethood through the Qur'an's miraculous nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of i'jaz from the text
The text begins with a statement about i'jaz in speech, then clarifies that this is not the full definition; i'jaz is about the speech being such that it cannot be opposed.
The operative phrase is 'لا يمكن معارضته والإتيان بمثله'.
2
Contrast i'jaz with sihr al-kalām
I'jaz is one fixed limit, while sihr has multiple levels and methods. The author uses the metaphor of hu'dab (fringes) for sihr and 'urwah (handle) for i'jaz.
3
Analyze the metaphor
The 'urwah is stronger and singular, symbolizing i'jaz's reliability and unity. The hu'dab are multiple and weaker.
This shows i'jaz is a fixed, unbreakable standard.
4
List the different views on the aspect (jihah) of i'jaz of the Qur'an
Scholars differed: some said eloquence, some said predictions of the unseen, some said unique style, some said divine prevention of opposition.
Despite disagreement, all agree it is a miracle.
5
State the Hanafi preferred view and its implication
The correct view according to the author is that i'jaz is due to utmost eloquence and clarity (balāghah wa faṣāḥah).
This implies that the Qur'an's eloquence is at a level that no human speech can reach, proving its divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله الإِعْجَازُ فِي الكَلامِ أَن يُؤدَّى المعنى بِطَرِيقٍ هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ مِن الطُّرُقِ لَيسَ تَفسِيراً لِمَفهُوم إعجازِ الكَلامِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَلْزَمُ أَن يَكُونَ بِالبَلاغَةِ بَل هُوَ عِبَارَة عَن كَونِ الكَلامِ بِحَيثُ لَا يُمكِنُ مُعَارَضَتْهُ وَالإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ مِن أَعجَرْتُهُ إِذَا جَعَلته عَاجِرًا وَلِهَذَا اختَلَفُوا فِي جِهَةِ إعجاز القرآن مَعَ أَنَّهُ يُشتَرَطُ فِى إعجازِ الكَلامِ كُونُهُ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ يَكُونُ وَاحِدًا لَا تَعَدُّدَ فِيهِ بِخِلَافِ سِحرِ الكَلَامِ فَإِنَّهُ عِبَارَةٌ عَن دِقَّتِهِ وَلُطفِ مَا خَذِهِ وَهَذَا يَقَعُ عَلَى طُرُقٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ وَمَرَاتِبَ مُختَلِفَةٍ فَلِهَذَا قَالَ أَهْدَابُ السِّحرِ بِلَفظِ الجَمع وَعُرَوَةُ الإِعْجَازِ بِلَفظ المُفرَدِ وَهُدَبُ الثّوبِ مَا عَلَى أَطْرَافِهِ وَعُرَوَةُ الكوز كُليَّتُهُ الَّذِى تُؤحَدٌ عِندَ أَخْذِهِ وَهِىَ أقوَى مِن الهُدَبِ فَخَصَّهَا بِالإِعجاز الَّذِي هُوَ أَوثَقُ مِن السِّحرِ وَفِى الصَّحَاحِ السّحرُ الأخذَةُ وَكُلُّ مَا لَطْف مَاخَذُهُ وَدَقَّ فَهُوَ سِحرٌ وَمَعَنَى تَمَسُّكِهِ بِذَلِكَ مُبَالَغَتْهُ فِي تَلْطِيفِ الكَلَامِ وَتَادِيَةِ المَعَانِي بِالعِبَارَاتِ اللَّايُقَةِ الفَايْقَةِ حَتَّى كَأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّبُ إِلَى السِّحْرِ وَالإِعْجَازِ وَهَاهُنَا بَحثَانِ الأَوَّلُ أَنْ كَونَ طَرِيقِ تَـادِيَة المَعنى أبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ مِن الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ المَوجُودَةِ غَيْرُ كَافٍ فِى الإعجازِ بَل لَا بُدَّ مِن العَجزِ عَن مُعَارَضَتِهِ وَالإِنْيَان بِمِثْلِهِ وَمِنَ الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ وَالمُقَدَّرَةِ حَتَّى لَا يُمكِنَ الإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوطٍ ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَادِرٌ عَلَى الإِنيَانِ بِمِثْلِ القُرآنِ مَعَ كَونِهِ مُعَجِزًا فَمَا مَعَنَىٰ قَولِهِ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ وَالثَّانِي أَنَّ الطَّرَف الأعلَى مِن البَلاغَةِ وَمَا يَقرُبُ مِنهُ مِن المَرَاتِبِ العَلِيَّةِ الَّتِى لَا يُمكِنُ لِلبَشَرِ الإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ كَلاهُمَا مُعجز عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِى المفتاح وَنِهَايَةِ الإعجاز وَحِينَيْد يَتَعَدَّدُ طَرِيقُ الإعجازِ أَيْضًا بِأَن يَكُونَ عَلَى الطَّرَفِ الأعلى أو عَلَى بَعضِ المَرَاتِبِ القَرِيبَةِ مِنْهُ وَالجَوَابُ عَنِ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّ الإِعْجَازَ لَيسَ إلَّا فِي كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَمَعَنَى كَونِهِ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ أَنَّهُ أَبْلَغُ مِن كُلِّ مَا هُوَ غَيْرُ كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مُحَقَّفًا اَوْمُقَدَّرًا حَتَّى لَا يُمكِنَ لِلْغَيْرِ الْإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ وَعَنِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ الإِعْجَازَ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ فِي الطَّرَفِ الأعلى أو فِيمَا يَقرُبُ مِنهُ مُتَّحِدٌ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ حَدٌ من الكَلامِ هُوَ أَبْلَعُ مِمَّا عَدَاهُ بِمَعنَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُمكِنُ لِلغَيرِ مُعَارَضَتْهُ وَالإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ بِخِلَافِ سِحرِ الكَلَامِ فَإِنَّهُ لَيسَ لَهُ حَدٌ يَصْبِطُهُ
His statement: 'I'jaz in speech is that the meaning is conveyed by a method that is more eloquent than all other methods' is not an explanation of the concept of i'jaz of speech; because it is not necessary that it be through eloquence. Rather, it is an expression of the speech being such that it cannot be opposed nor can one produce its like, derived from a'jartuhu when you make someone incapable. For this reason, they disagreed about the aspect of the i'jaz of the Qur'an, despite agreement that it is a miracle. It was said it is due to its eloquence, and said due to its informing of the unseen, and said due to its strange style, and said due to Allah turning minds away from opposition. Rather, the intended meaning is that the i'jaz of Allah's speech is only by this method, and it is its being at the utmost of eloquence and the peak of clarity, according to the correct view. By considering that it is required in i'jaz of speech that it be more eloquent than all others, it becomes singular with no multiplicity, unlike the magic of speech, for it is an expression of its subtlety and delicacy of its source, and this occurs in multiple ways and different levels. For this reason, he said 'hu'dab of magic' in the plural and 'urwah of i'jaz' in the singular. Hu'dab of a garment are its fringes; the 'urwah of a ewer is its handle by which it is grasped. And it is stronger than the fringes, so he specified it for i'jaz which is more reliable than magic. In al-Sihah: 'Good magic is a trick, and everything whose source is subtle and delicate is magic.' And the meaning of his clinging to that is his exaggeration in refining speech and conveying meanings with appropriate and excellent expressions until he seems to draw near to magic and i'jaz. And here are two investigations: First, that the method of conveying meaning being more eloquent than all other verified existing methods is not sufficient for i'jaz; rather, inability to oppose it and produce its like is necessary, and from the verified and estimated methods, so that inability to produce its like is not conditional? Because Allah is able to produce the like of the Qur'an despite its being a miracle. So what is the meaning of his statement 'more eloquent than all others'? Second, that the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it among the high levels that humans cannot produce their like, both are miraculous according to what is mentioned in al-Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz. Then the method of i'jaz would also be multiple by being at the highest level or at some of the levels close to it. The answer to the first: that i'jaz is only in Allah's speech, and the meaning of its being more eloquent than all others is that it is more eloquent than everything that is not Allah's speech, whether actual or estimated, so that no other can produce its like. And regarding the second: that i'jaz, whether at the highest level or what is close to it, is unified in consideration that it is a limit of speech that is more eloquent than what is other than it, meaning that no other can oppose it or produce its like, unlike the magic of speech for it has no fixed limit.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage defines i'jaz (inimitability/miracle) of the Qur'an in the Hanafi usul context. The author first clarifies a common misconception: i'jaz is not simply about the speech being extremely eloquent (balaghah) in conveying meaning; rather, it refers to the speech being such that no one can oppose it (mu'āraḍah) or produce something like it (ityān bi-mithlihī). The root is 'ajaza (to be unable). Despite agreement that the Qur'an is a miracle, scholars differed on the exact aspect: some said eloquence, some said predictions of the unseen, some said unique style, some said Allah turned people away from opposing. The author prefers eloquence at the highest degree. Then he distinguishes i'jaz from sihr al-kalām (magic of speech): i'jaz is singular and fixed (one level that cannot be matched), whereas sihr is subtle and can occur in multiple levels and methods. The metaphor of hu'dab (fringes) for magic vs. 'urwah (handle) for i'jaz illustrates that i'jaz is stronger and more reliable. Finally, two investigations are resolved: (1) Is being more eloquent than all other speech sufficient for i'jaz? Answer: Yes, but only because i'jaz is specifically in Allah's speech, and being more eloquent than all other speech implies inability to produce its like. (2) Can i'jaz be both at the highest level and near it? Answer: Yes, but it remains unified as a fixed limit that none can cross, unlike sihr which has no fixed limit.

Key Terms
الإعجاز (al-iʿjāz): The quality of speech that makes it impossible for others to oppose or produce its like, specifically in the Qur'an.
السحر الكلامي (siḥr al-kalāmī): Subtlety and delicacy in speech that occurs in multiple levels and methods, unlike i'jaz.
البَلاغَة (al-balāghah): Eloquence; the quality of speech that conveys meaning effectively and beautifully.
الفَصَاحَة (al-faṣāḥah): Clarity and purity of expression; a component of eloquence.
الهَدَب (al-hu'dab): Fringes of a garment; metaphorical for the multiple weak strands of magic (sihr).
العُرْوَة (al-'urwah): Handle of a ewer; metaphorical for the singular strong grip of i'jaz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the essential condition for i'jaz of speech?
A) It must be more eloquent than all other speech.
B) It must be from Allah.
C) No one can oppose it or produce its like.
D) It must have a subtle source.

Key Takeaway
I'jaz is defined by the impossibility of opposition and is a singular fixed limit, unlike sihr which is multiple and imitable.

The Two Investigations: Unity of I'jaz Across Levels
Two investigations and their resolutions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN the two investigations regarding i'jaz and STATE the author's resolutions that i'jaz is unified regardless of level.

Core Idea
I'jaz is one fixed limit; even if the level of eloquence varies, it remains unopposable.

The passage continues by raising two important investigations (bahthan) that refine the definition of i'jaz. The first investigation asks whether being more eloquent than all speech is sufficient for i'jaz without the condition of impossibility. The second questions whether i'jaz would be multiple if it can occur at different levels of eloquence. The author provides clear answers, preserving the unity of i'jaz and distinguishing it further from sihr.

Guided Path
1
State the first investigation
If being more eloquent than all existing and potential speech is required, then even Allah could produce a like of the Qur'an, so is being more eloquent sufficient?
The investigation queries the necessity of the impossibility condition.
2
State the answer to the first investigation
I'jaz is only in Allah's speech; being more eloquent implies impossibility of imitation because no non-divine speech can match it.
The answer ties i'jaz exclusively to divine speech.
3
State the second investigation
If there are different levels of eloquence that humans cannot reach (the highest and near-highest), then i'jaz would be multiple based on the level.
This challenges the previous claim of singularity.
4
State the answer to the second investigation
I'jaz is a fixed limit (hadd) that is the most eloquent; whether at the highest level or close to it, it is still that one limit that cannot be crossed. Unlike sihr, it has no multiple levels.
The answer reaffirms the unity of i'jaz.

بِالبَلاغَةِ بَل هُوَ عِبَارَة عَن كَونِ الكَلامِ بِحَيثُ لَا يُمكِنُ مُعَارَضَتْهُ وَالإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ مِن أَعجَرْتُهُ إِذَا جَعَلته عَاجِرًا وَلِهَذَا اختَلَفُوا فِي جِهَةِ إعجاز القرآن مَعَ الاتِّفَاقِ عَلَى كَونِهِ مُعجِزًا فَقِيلَ إِنَّهُ بِبَلاغَتِهِ وَقِيلَ بِإِحْبَارِهِ عَن المَغِيْبَاتِ وَقِيلَ بِأُسَلُوبِهِ الغَرِيبِ وَقِيلَ بصَرفِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى العُقُولَ عَن المُعَارَضَةِ بَلِ المُرَادُ أَنَّ إعْجَازَ كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِهَذَا الطَّرِيقِ وَهُوَ كَونُهُ فِى غَايَةِ البَلَاغَةِ وَنِهَايَةِ الفَصَاحَةِ عَلَى مَا هُوَ الرَّأى الصَّحِيحُ فَبِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ يُشتَرَطُ فِى إعجازِ الكَلامِ كُونُهُ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ يَكُونُ وَاحِدًا لَا تَعَدُّدَ فِيهِ بِخِلَافِ سِحرِ الكَلَامِ فَإِنَّهُ عِبَارَةٌ عَن دِقَّتِهِ وَلُطفِ مَا خَذِهِ وَهَذَا يَقَعُ عَلَى طُرُقٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ وَمَرَاتِبَ مُختَلِفَةٍ فَلِهَذَا قَالَ أَهْدَابُ السِّحرِ بِلَفظِ الجَمع وَعُرَوَةُ الإِعْجَازِ بِلَفظ المُفرَدِ وَهُدَبُ الثّوبِ مَا عَلَى أَطْرَافِهِ وَعُرَوَةُ الكوز كُليَّتُهُ الَّذِى تُؤحَدٌ عِندَ أَخْذِهِ وَهِىَ أقوَى مِن الهُدَبِ فَخَصَّهَا بِالإِعجاز الَّذِي هُوَ أَوثَقُ مِن السِّحرِ وَفِى الصَّحَاحِ السّحرُ الأخذَةُ وَكُلُّ مَا لَطْف مَاخَذُهُ وَدَقَّ فَهُوَ سِحرٌ وَمَعَنَى تَمَسُّكِهِ بِذَلِكَ مُبَالَغَتْهُ فِي تَلْطِيفِ الكَلَامِ وَتَادِيَةِ المَعَانِي بِالعِبَارَاتِ اللَّايُقَةِ الفَايْقَةِ حَتَّى كَأَنَّهُ يَتَقَرَّبُ إِلَى السِّحْرِ وَالإِعْجَازِ وَهَاهُنَا بَحثَانِ الأَوَّلُ أَنْ كَونَ طَرِيقِ تَـادِيَة المَعنى أبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ مِن الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ المَوجُودَةِ غَيْرُ كَافٍ فِى الإعجازِ بَل لَا بُدَّ مِن العَجزِ عَن مُعَارَضَتِهِ وَالإِنْيَان بِمِثْلِهِ وَمِنَ الطُّرُقِ المُحَقَّقَةِ وَالمُقَدَّرَةِ حَتَّى لَا يُمكِنَ الإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوطٍ ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَادِرٌ عَلَى الإِنيَانِ بِمِثْلِ القُرآنِ مَعَ كَونِهِ مُعَجِزًا فَمَا مَعَنَىٰ قَولِهِ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ وَالثَّانِي أَنَّ الطَّرَف الأعلَى مِن البَلاغَةِ وَمَا يَقرُبُ مِنهُ مِن المَرَاتِبِ العَلِيَّةِ الَّتِى لَا يُمكِنُ لِلبَشَرِ الإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ كَلاهُمَا مُعجز عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِى المفتاح وَنِهَايَةِ الإعجاز وَحِينَيْد يَتَعَدَّدُ طَرِيقُ الإعجازِ أَيْضًا بِأَن يَكُونَ عَلَى الطَّرَفِ الأعلى أو عَلَى بَعضِ المَرَاتِبِ القَرِيبَةِ مِنْهُ وَالجَوَابُ عَنِ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّ الإِعْجَازَ لَيسَ إلَّا فِي كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَمَعَنَى كَونِهِ أَبْلَغَ مِن جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ أَنَّهُ أَبْلَغُ مِن كُلِّ مَا هُوَ غَيْرُ كَلامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مُحَقَّفًا اَوْمُقَدَّرًا حَتَّى لَا يُمكِنَ لِلْغَيْرِ الْإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ وَعَنِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ الإِعْجَازَ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ فِي الطَّرَفِ الأعلى أو فِيمَا يَقرُبُ مِنهُ مُتَّحِدٌ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ حَدٌ من الكَلامِ هُوَ أَبْلَعُ مِمَّا عَدَاهُ بِمَعنَى أَنَّهُ لَا يُمكِنُ لِلغَيرِ مُعَارَضَتْهُ وَالإِنْيَانُ بِمِثْلِهِ بِخِلَافِ سِحرِ الكَلَامِ فَإِنَّهُ لَيسَ لَهُ حَدٌ يَصْبِطُهُ
His statement: 'I'jaz in speech is that the meaning is conveyed by a method that is more eloquent than all other methods' is not an explanation of the concept of i'jaz of speech; because it is not necessary that it be through eloquence. Rather, it is an expression of the speech being such that it cannot be opposed nor can one produce its like, derived from a'jartuhu when you make someone incapable. For this reason, they disagreed about the aspect of the i'jaz of the Qur'an, despite agreement that it is a miracle. It was said it is due to its eloquence, and said due to its informing of the unseen, and said due to its strange style, and said due to Allah turning minds away from opposition. Rather, the intended meaning is that the i'jaz of Allah's speech is only by this method, and it is its being at the utmost of eloquence and the peak of clarity, according to the correct view. By considering that it is required in i'jaz of speech that it be more eloquent than all others, it becomes singular with no multiplicity, unlike the magic of speech, for it is an expression of its subtlety and delicacy of its source, and this occurs in multiple ways and different levels. For this reason, he said 'hu'dab of magic' in the plural and 'urwah of i'jaz' in the singular. Hu'dab of a garment are its fringes; the 'urwah of a ewer is its handle by which it is grasped. And it is stronger than the fringes, so he specified it for i'jaz which is more reliable than magic. In al-Sihah: 'Good magic is a trick, and everything whose source is subtle and delicate is magic.' And the meaning of his clinging to that is his exaggeration in refining speech and conveying meanings with appropriate and excellent expressions until he seems to draw near to magic and i'jaz. And here are two investigations: First, that the method of conveying meaning being more eloquent than all other verified existing methods is not sufficient for i'jaz; rather, inability to oppose it and produce its like is necessary, and from the verified and estimated methods, so that inability to produce its like is not conditional? Because Allah is able to produce the like of the Qur'an despite its being a miracle. So what is the meaning of his statement 'more eloquent than all others'? Second, that the highest level of eloquence and what is close to it among the high levels that humans cannot produce their like, both are miraculous according to what is mentioned in al-Miftah and Nihayat al-I'jaz. Then the method of i'jaz would also be multiple by being at the highest level or at some of the levels close to it. The answer to the first: that i'jaz is only in Allah's speech, and the meaning of its being more eloquent than all others is that it is more eloquent than everything that is not Allah's speech, whether actual or estimated, so that no other can produce its like. And regarding the second: that i'jaz, whether at the highest level or what is close to it, is unified in consideration that it is a limit of speech that is more eloquent than what is other than it, meaning that no other can oppose it or produce its like, unlike the magic of speech for it has no fixed limit.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage defines i'jaz (inimitability/miracle) of the Qur'an in the Hanafi usul context. The author first clarifies a common misconception: i'jaz is not simply about the speech being extremely eloquent (balaghah) in conveying meaning; rather, it refers to the speech being such that no one can oppose it (mu'āraḍah) or produce something like it (ityān bi-mithlihī). The root is 'ajaza (to be unable). Despite agreement that the Qur'an is a miracle, scholars differed on the exact aspect: some said eloquence, some said predictions of the unseen, some said unique style, some said Allah turned people away from opposing. The author prefers eloquence at the highest degree. Then he distinguishes i'jaz from sihr al-kalām (magic of speech): i'jaz is singular and fixed (one level that cannot be matched), whereas sihr is subtle and can occur in multiple levels and methods. The metaphor of hu'dab (fringes) for magic vs. 'urwah (handle) for i'jaz illustrates that i'jaz is stronger and more reliable. Finally, two investigations are resolved: (1) Is being more eloquent than all other speech sufficient for i'jaz? Answer: Yes, but only because i'jaz is specifically in Allah's speech, and being more eloquent than all other speech implies inability to produce its like. (2) Can i'jaz be both at the highest level and near it? Answer: Yes, but it remains unified as a fixed limit that none can cross, unlike sihr which has no fixed limit.

Key Terms
الإعجاز (al-iʿjāz): The quality of speech that makes it impossible for others to oppose or produce its like, specifically in the Qur'an.
السحر الكلامي (siḥr al-kalāmī): Subtlety and delicacy in speech that occurs in multiple levels and methods, unlike i'jaz.
الحد (al-ḥadd): A fixed limit or boundary; used here to describe i'jaz as a single, unbreachable standard.
البحثان (al-baḥthān): The two investigations or scholarly inquiries raised to refine the definition.

Key Takeaway

Defining 'Asl' and the Conditions of Nominal Definitions
Definition and critique of 'asl'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul distinction between real and nominal definitions and apply the conditions of tard and aks to evaluate a definition of 'asl'.

Core Idea
A correct nominal definition must include everything it names and exclude what it does not name.

The term 'asl' (origin/foundation) is central to usul al-fiqh. This passage explains how to define it correctly, distinguishing between real definitions of actual essences and nominal definitions of conventional terms. It then tests a candidate definition using the logical conditions of tard (universality) and aks (converse) and finds it wanting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two approaches to defining usul al-fiqh
The passage notes two methods: defining the phrase 'usul al-fiqh' as a construct (idafa) which requires defining each part, or as a title for a specific science. Focus here is on the construct approach, specifically on defining 'asl'.
The construct definition is the immediate concern.
2
Distinguish real vs nominal definitions
The author explains that definitions can be real (haqiqi) for actual essences, or nominal (ismi) for conventional terms like 'asl'. The definition of 'asl' is nominal because it is a term we coin for a composite idea.
This distinction is crucial for understanding what conditions apply.
3
Apply the conditions: tard and aks
For any definition, especially nominal, two conditions are necessary: tard (universality) means every instance of the definition is an instance of the defined; aks (converse) means every instance of the defined is an instance of the definition. The passage gives examples of failing each.
Tard ensures no over-inclusion; aks ensures no under-inclusion.
4
Critique the definition from al-Mahsul
The author states that Imam al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed' (al-muhtaj ilayh). But this definition fails tard because it includes efficient causes, formal causes, final causes, and conditions (like tools) — none of which are called 'asl' in Arabic. Hence the definition is invalid.
This critique uses the tool of falsification through counterexample.

أُصُولُ الفِقهِ أَى هَذَا أُصُولُ الفِقهِ أَو أُصُولُ الفِقهِ مَا هِيَ فَتُعَرِّفُهَا أَوَّلًا بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِضَافَةِ وَثَانِيَا بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ لَقَـبْ لِعِلمٍ مَخصُوصِ أَمَّا تَعرِيفُهَا بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِضَافَةِ فَيَحتَاجُ إلَى تَعرِيفِ المُضَافِ وَالمُصَافِ إِلَيهِ فَقَالَ الْأَصْلُ مَا يُبْتَنَى عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَالِابْتِنَاءُ شَامِلٌ لِلابْتِنَاءِ الحِسَى وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ وَالابْتِنَاءِ العَقلِي وَهُوَ تَرَتُبُ الحُكمِ عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ وَتَعرِيفُهُ بِالمُحتاجِ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَطَّرِدُ وَقَد عَرَّفَهُ الإِمَامُ فِي المَحصُولِ بِهَذَا وَاعلَم أَنَّ التَّعرِيفَ إِمَّا حَقِيقِيٌّ كَتَعرِيفِ المَاهِيَّاتِ الحَقِيقِيَّةِ وَإِمَّا اسْمِيٌّ كَتَعرِيفِ المَاهِيَّاتِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ كَمَا إِذَا رَكَّبَنَا شَيْئًا مِن أُمُورٍ هِيَ أَجْزَاؤُهُ بِاعْتِبَارِ تَركِيبِنَا ثُمَّ وَضَعْنَا لِهَذَا المُرَكَّبِ اسمًا كَالأصلِ وَالفِقهِ وَالجِنسِ وَالنَّوعِ وَنَحوِهَا فَالتَّعرِيفُ الاسمِيُّ هُوَ تَبيينُ أَنَّ هَذَا الاسمَ لِأَيِّ شَيْءٍ وُضِعَ وَشْرِطَ لِكَلا التَّعْرِيفَينِ الطَّرِدُ أَى كُلُّ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيهِ الحَدُّ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ المَحدُودُ وَالعَكسُ أَى كُلُّ مَا صَدَقَ مَا عَلَيْهِ المَحدُودُ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الحَدُّ فَإِذَا قِيلَ فِى تَعرِيفِ الْإِنسَانِ : إِنَّهُ حَيَوَانٌ مَاشِ لَا يَطَّرِدُ وَلَو قِيلَ حَيَوَانٌ كَاتِبٌ بِالفِعلِ لَا يَنعَكِسُ وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّ تَعْرِيفَ الْأَصْلِ تعريف اسمى أى بَيَانُ أَنَّ لَفظَ الأَصل لأيِّ شَيْءٍ وُضِعَ فَالتَّعْرِيفَ الَّذِي ذُكِرَ في المحصُولِ لَا يَطْرِدُ لأنه أى الأصل لا يُطلَقُ عَلَى الفَاعِلِ أَى العِلَّةِ الفَاعِلِيَّةِ وَالصُّورَةِ أى العِلَّةِ الصُّورِيَّةِ وَالغَايَةِ أَى العِلَّةِ الغَايْبَةِ وَالشُّرُوطِ كَأَدَوَاتِ الصَّنَاعَةِ مَثَلًا فَعْلِمَ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفَ صَادِقَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ لِكُونِهَا مُحتَاجَةً إِلَيهَا وَالمَحدُودُ لَا يَصدُقُ عَلَيْهَا ؛ لأنَّ شَيْئًا مِن هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ لَا يُسَمَّى أصلا فَلا يَصِحُ هَذَا التَّعرِيف الاسمى .
Usul al-fiqh: i.e., what is usul al-fiqh? Or what is usul al-fiqh? So define it firstly by consideration of construct (idafa) and secondly by consideration that it is a title for a specific science. As for its definition by consideration of construct, it requires defining the first part (mudaf) and the second part (mudaf ilayh). So he said: al-asl is that upon which something else is built. So 'building' (ibtina') includes physical building, which is apparent, and intellectual building, which is the effect of a ruling on its evidence. And its definition as 'that which is needed' is not universal (la yattarid). Imam [al-Razi] in al-Mahsul defined it with this. And know that the definition is either real (haqiqi) like the definition of real essences, or nominal (ismi) like the definition of conventional essences, as when we compose something from matters that are its parts by virtue of our composition, then we put a name for this composite, like 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins', 'naw', and the like. The nominal definition is explaining for what thing this name was placed. And for both definitions, the condition is universality (tard), i.e., everything to which the definition applies, the defined applies to it; and the converse (aks), i.e., everything to which the defined applies, the definition applies to it. So if it is said in the definition of human: 'It is a walking animal', it is not universal (la yattarid); and if it is said 'an animal that actually writes', it does not converse (la yan'akis). And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is a nominal definition, i.e., an explanation of for what thing the word 'asl' was placed. So the definition mentioned in al-Mahsul is not universal because 'asl' is not applied to the agent (i.e., efficient cause), form (formal cause), end (final cause), and conditions like the tools of a craft, for example. Thus, it is known that this definition applies to these things because they are needed for them, but the defined does not apply to them, because none of these things is called 'asl'. Therefore, this nominal definition is not valid.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'asl' within usul al-fiqh. It distinguishes two approaches to defining usul al-fiqh: as a construct (idafa) and as a science. For the construct, 'asl' is defined as 'that upon which something else is built' (ma yubtana 'alayhi ghayruhu). This covers both physical foundations (e.g., a wall on a foundation) and intellectual foundations (e.g., a ruling based on its evidence). The author critiques the alternative definition 'that which is needed' (al-muhtaj ilayh) because it is not universal (tard): it would include efficient, formal, and final causes as well as conditions (e.g., tools of a craft), none of which are called 'asl' in Arabic. The discussion then explains real vs. nominal definitions. Since 'asl' is a conventional term, its definition is nominal, requiring both tard (universality) and aks (converse). The definition from al-Mahsul fails tard because it applies to things not called 'asl', and is therefore invalid.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): That upon which something else is built; a foundational source or principle.
الطرد (al-tard): Universality: every individual that falls under the definition must be included.
العكس (al-aks): Converse: every individual of the defined must be covered by the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the definition of 'al-asl' as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed) not correct?
A) Because it fails the condition of aks (converse).
B) Because it fails the condition of tard (universality) by including things not called 'asl'.
C) Because it is a real definition, but 'asl' requires a nominal definition.
D) Because it defines 'asl' in terms of 'fiqh', which is circular.

Key Takeaway
A correct nominal definition of a conventional term like 'asl' must pass both tard and aks; the definition accepted in Hanafi usul is 'that upon which something else is built'.
