Defining 'Asl' and the Two Approaches to Definition
Defining 'asl' and introducing the types of definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of 'asl' according to Hanafi usul and distinguish between real (ḥaqīqī) and nominal (ismī) definitions.

Core Idea
'Asl' is that upon which something else is built—physically or intellectually.

This passage introduces the foundational term 'asl' (origin/root) in usul al-fiqh. It explains that defining usul al-fiqh can be done by analyzing its construct (idafa) or by treating it as a technical term. The focus here is on defining 'asl', which is crucial for understanding how proofs and rulings are built. The passage also distinguishes between definitions of real essences and definitions of conventional concepts like 'asl'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two approaches to defining usul al-fiqh
The author states that usul al-fiqh can be defined by way of construct (idafa) — defining its two parts 'usul' and 'fiqh' — or as a technical term for a specific science. Focus on the first approach.
2
Extract the definition of 'asl'
The passage defines 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built' (mā yubnā ʿalayhi ghayruh). Note that building includes physical building (like a foundation) and intellectual building (like a ruling depending on its evidence).
3
Distinguish between real and nominal definitions
Ḥaqīqī definitions capture real essences; ismī definitions explain the coinage of a term for a conventional concept. 'Asl' falls under ismī definition because it is a composite concept made from parts by our own composition.
The example given: 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins', 'naw' are all nominal definitions.
4
Note the condition for nominal definitions
Both types require ṭard and 'aks, but this section only introduces the distinction. The next lesson covers the conditions in detail.

التَّعْرِيفَينِ الطَّرِدُ أَى كُلُّ مَا صَدَقَ عَلَيهِ الحَدُّ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ المَحدُودُ وَالعَكسُ أَى كُلُّ مَا صَدَقَ مَا عَلَيْهِ المَحدُودُ صَدَقَ عَلَيْهِ الحَدُّ فَإِذَا قِيلَ فِى تَعرِيفِ الْإِنسَانِ : إِنَّهُ حَيَوَانٌ مَاشِ لَا يَطَّرِدُ وَلَو قِيلَ حَيَوَانٌ كَاتِبٌ بِالفِعلِ لَا يَنعَكِسُ وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّ تَعْرِيفَ الْأَصْلِ تعريف اسمى أى بَيَانُ أَنَّ لَفظَ الأَصل لأيِّ شَيْءٍ وُضِعَ فَالتَّعْرِيفَ الَّذِي ذُكِرَ في المحصُولِ لَا يَطْرِدُ لأنه أى الأصل لا يُطلَقُ عَلَى الفَاعِلِ أَى العِلَّةِ الفَاعِلِيَّةِ وَالصُّورَةِ أى العِلَّةِ الصُّورِيَّةِ وَالغَايَةِ أَى العِلَّةِ الغَايْبَةِ وَالشُّرُوطِ كَأَدَوَاتِ الصَّنَاعَةِ مَثَلًا فَعْلِمَ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفَ صَادِقَ عَلَى هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ لِكُونِهَا مُحتَاجَةً إِلَيهَا وَالمَحدُودُ لَا يَصدُقُ عَلَيْهَا ؛ لأنَّ شَيْئًا مِن هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ لَا يُسَمَّى أصلا فَلا يَصِحُ هَذَا التَّعرِيف الاسمى .تر یعنی یہ اصول فقہ ہے یا اصول فقہ کیا ہے؟ پس ہم تعریف کریں گے اس کی اولا اضافت کے اعتبار سے اور ثانیا اس اعتبار سے کہ وہ لقب ہے مخصوص علم کا ۔ اور بہر حال اس کی تعریف اضافت کے اعتبار سے پس و محتاج ہوتی ہے مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف پس فرمایا " اصل وہ ہے کہ جس پر غیر کی بنیاد رکھی جائے۔ پس ابتناء شامل ہے۔ ابتناء حس کو اور وہ ظاہر ہے اور ابتنا عقلی کو اور وہ حکم کا مرتب ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل پر۔ اور اس کی تعریف کرنا محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ وہ نمرد نہیں ہے۔ اور تحقیق تعریف کی اس (اصل) کی امام رازی نے محصول میں اسی کے ساتھ ۔ اور جان لیجیے کے بے شک تعریف یا تو حقیقی ہے جیسے ماھیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف اور یا تعریف امی ہے جیسے ماھیات اعتبار یہ کی تعریف جیسے ہم مرکب کریں کسی شے کو ایسے امور سے کہ وہ اس کے اجزاء ہوں ہمارے مرکب کرنے کے اعتبار سے پھر ہم نے وضع کیا ہے اس مرکب کے لیے ایک نام مثل لفظ اصل کے اور فقہ اور جنس اور نوع اور اس جیسی مثالوں کے۔ پس تعریف اسمی وہ بیان کرنا ہے یہ کہ : شک اسم کون سی مٹی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے ( اور شرط لگائی گئی ہے دونوں کے لیے طرد کی ) یعنی وہ چیز کہ صادق آئے اس پر حد تو صادق آئے اس پر محدود اور ( شرط لگائی گئی ہے عکس طرد کی ) یعنی ہر وہ چیز کہ صادق آئے اس پر محدود تو صادق آئے اس پر حد بھی ۔ پس جب کہا جائے انسان کی تعریف میں کہ وہ بے شک وہ حیوان ماشی ہے تو اس میں طرد نہیں ہے اور اگر کہا جائے کہ حیوان کا تب بالفعل ہے تو یہ تعریف منعکس نہیں ہے۔ (اور نہیں ہے کوئی شک اس میں کہ بے شک اصل کی تعریف تعریف امی ہے ) یعنی بیان کرنا ہے اس کا کہ بے شک لفظ اصل کون سی چیز کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ پس وہ تعریف جو ذکر کی گئی ہے۔ محصول میں وہ مطرد نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ وہ ) یعنی اصل ( کہ نہیں اطلاق کیا جاتا اس کا فاعل پر ) یعنی علت فاعلیہ پر ( اور صورت پر ) یعنی علت صور یہ پر ( اور غایت پر ) یعنی علت غائیہ پر ( اور شرط پر ) جیسے ادوات صناعت ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تعریف صادق ہے ان اشیاء پر بوجہ ہونے ان کے محتاج الیہ اور محدود نہیں صادق آتا ان پر اس لیے کہ ان اشیاء میں سے کسی شے کا نام نہیں رکھا جاتا ہے اصل ۔ پس یہ تعریف اسمی درست نہیں ہے۔
Usul al-fiqh: i.e., 'This is usul al-fiqh' or 'What is usul al-fiqh?' So we define it firstly by way of construct (idafa) and secondly by way of it being a title for a specific science. As for its definition by way of construct, it requires the definition of the first term and the second term. So he said: 'Al-asl (the root/origin) is that upon which something else is built.' So 'al-ibnā' (building) includes physical building, which is apparent, and intellectual building, which is the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence. Defining it as 'that which is needed by something else' does not meet the condition of tarid (comprehensiveness). Imam al-Razi in al-Mahsul defined it this way. And know that definition is either haqiqi (real), like the definition of real essences, or ismi (nominal), like the definition of conventional essences, as when we compose something from matters that are its parts by virtue of our composition, then we coin a name for this composite, like 'asl' and 'fiqh' and 'jins' and 'naw' and the like. So the ismi definition is an explanation of what this name was coined for. Both types of definition require tarid, i.e., every time the definition applies, the defined term applies; and 'aks (converse), i.e., every time the defined term applies, the definition applies. So if one says in the definition of 'insan' (human) that it is 'a walking animal', it does not meet tarid; and if one says 'animal that actually writes', it does not meet 'aks. And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is an ismi definition, i.e., an explanation of for what thing the word 'asl' was coined. So the definition mentioned in al-Mahsul does not meet tarid, because 'asl' (i.e., the term) is not applied to the agent (i.e., the efficient cause), nor to the form (i.e., the formal cause), nor to the end (i.e., the final cause), nor to conditions like the tools of an art, for example. Thus it becomes known that this definition applies to these things because they are needed by something else, but the defined term does not apply to them, because none of these things are called 'asl'. So this nominal definition is invalid. [Urdu translation and elaboration]
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses the definition of usul al-fiqh and the term 'asl' (origin/foundation). The author first explains that defining usul al-fiqh can be approached in two ways: by considering the construct (idafa) of the two words 'usul' and 'fiqh', or by treating it as a technical term for a specific science. For the first approach, one must define each part: 'asl' and 'fiqh'. Here they focus on 'asl' and provide a definition: 'that upon which something else is built,' covering both literal building (like a foundation) and intellectual building (like a ruling depending on its proof). The author notes that defining 'asl' as 'that which is needed by something else' is not comprehensive (ṭārid), contrary to Imam al-Razi's definition in al-Mahsul. The passage then distinguishes between real (ḥaqīqī) definitions, which capture the essence of real entities, and nominal (ismī) definitions, which explain the coinage of a term for a conceptual construct (like 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins'). For a valid definition, two conditions are required: ṭard (the definition applies to every instance of the defined term) and ‘aks (the defined term applies to every instance of the definition). The author gives examples: 'walking animal' for human is too broad (includes animals that walk), so it lacks ṭard; 'animal that actually writes' is too narrow, lacking ‘aks. Applying this to 'asl', al-Razi's definition (something needed by another) fails ṭard because it applies to agents, forms, ends, and conditions, which are needed but not called 'asl'. Therefore, the definition is invalid. This critique reflects a Hanafi emphasis on precise, bidirectional definitions in usul methodology.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): That upon which something else is built; the origin or foundation.
تعريف حقيقي (taʿrīf ḥaqīqī): Real definition that captures the essence of an entity.
تعريف اسمي (taʿrīf ismī): Nominal definition that explains for what thing a term was coined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) That upon which something else is built
C) The first part of a construct
D) A ruling from the Quran

Key Takeaway
The term 'asl' is defined nominally as 'that upon which something else is built', distinguishing it from al-Razi's definition and emphasizing its foundational role in usul.

Conditions of Valid Definition: Ṭard and ʿAks
Critiquing al-Razi's definition using ṭard and ʿaks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of ṭard (comprehensiveness) and ʿaks (exclusivity) to evaluate the validity of a nominal definition, and explain why al-Razi's definition of 'asl' fails ṭard.

Core Idea
A valid nominal definition must cover all instances of the defined term (ṭard) and only those instances (ʿaks).

This lesson delves into the two essential conditions for any valid definition, particularly nominal definitions: ṭard and ʿaks. The passage illustrates these conditions using examples like 'walking animal' and 'actually writing animal', then applies them to critique al-Razi's definition of 'asl'. Understanding these criteria is crucial for evaluating definitions in usul al-fiqh and avoiding over- or under-inclusivity.

Guided Path
1
Define ṭard and ʿaks
Ṭard means that every time the definition applies, the defined term applies (comprehensiveness). ʿAks means that every time the defined term applies, the definition applies (exclusivity). Together, they ensure equivalence.
The passage literally says: 'al-ṭard wa al-ʿaks' and examples follow.
2
Analyze the examples given
If 'human' is defined as 'walking animal', it fails ṭard because not all walking animals are humans. If defined as 'animal that actually writes', it fails ʿaks because not all humans are actually writing at all times.
These examples clarify why both conditions are needed.
3
Identify the critique of al-Razi's definition of 'asl'
Al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed by another'. This definition applies to efficient causes, formal causes, final causes, and conditions (e.g., tools) because they are all needed by something else. Yet, none of these are called 'asl' in legal terminology. Thus, the definition fails ṭard (it is too broad).
The passage then concludes the nominal definition is invalid.
4
Reflect on why this matters for usul al-fiqh
Ensuring definitions are precise prevents confusion in legal reasoning. If 'asl' were defined too broadly, it could misidentify the foundation in qiyas or other usul operations.

Usul al-fiqh: i.e., 'This is usul al-fiqh' or 'What is usul al-fiqh?' So we define it firstly by way of construct (idafa) and secondly by way of it being a title for a specific science. As for its definition by way of construct, it requires the definition of the first term and the second term. So he said: 'Al-asl (the root/origin) is that upon which something else is built.' So 'al-ibnā' (building) includes physical building, which is apparent, and intellectual building, which is the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence. Defining it as 'that which is needed by something else' does not meet the condition of tarid (comprehensiveness). Imam al-Razi in al-Mahsul defined it this way. And know that definition is either haqiqi (real), like the definition of real essences, or ismi (nominal), like the definition of conventional essences, as when we compose something from matters that are its parts by virtue of our composition, then we coin a name for this composite, like 'asl' and 'fiqh' and 'jins' and 'naw' and the like. So the ismi definition is an explanation of what this name was coined for. Both types of definition require tarid, i.e., every time the definition applies, the defined term applies; and 'aks (converse), i.e., every time the defined term applies, the definition applies. So if one says in the definition of 'insan' (human) that it is 'a walking animal', it does not meet tarid; and if one says 'animal that actually writes', it does not meet 'aks. And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is an ismi definition, i.e., an explanation of for what thing the word 'asl' was coined. So the definition mentioned in al-Mahsul does not meet tarid, because 'asl' (i.e., the term) is not applied to the agent (i.e., the efficient cause), nor to the form (i.e., the formal cause), nor to the end (i.e., the final cause), nor to conditions like the tools of an art, for example. Thus it becomes known that this definition applies to these things because they are needed by something else, but the defined term does not apply to them, because none of these things are called 'asl'. So this nominal definition is invalid. [Urdu translation and elaboration]
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses the definition of usul al-fiqh and the term 'asl' (origin/foundation). The author first explains that defining usul al-fiqh can be approached in two ways: by considering the construct (idafa) of the two words 'usul' and 'fiqh', or by treating it as a technical term for a specific science. For the first approach, one must define each part: 'asl' and 'fiqh'. Here they focus on 'asl' and provide a definition: 'that upon which something else is built,' covering both literal building (like a foundation) and intellectual building (like a ruling depending on its proof). The author notes that defining 'asl' as 'that which is needed by something else' is not comprehensive (ṭārid), contrary to Imam al-Razi's definition in al-Mahsul. The passage then distinguishes between real (ḥaqīqī) definitions, which capture the essence of real entities, and nominal (ismī) definitions, which explain the coinage of a term for a conceptual construct (like 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins'). For a valid definition, two conditions are required: ṭard (the definition applies to every instance of the defined term) and ‘aks (the defined term applies to every instance of the definition). The author gives examples: 'walking animal' for human is too broad (includes animals that walk), so it lacks ṭard; 'animal that actually writes' is too narrow, lacking ‘aks. Applying this to 'asl', al-Razi's definition (something needed by another) fails ṭard because it applies to agents, forms, ends, and conditions, which are needed but not called 'asl'. Therefore, the definition is invalid. This critique reflects a Hanafi emphasis on precise, bidirectional definitions in usul methodology.

Key Terms
اطراد (ṭard): Comprehensiveness: every instance of the definition is an instance of the defined term.
عكس (ʿaks): Exclusivity: every instance of the defined term is an instance of the definition.
علة فاعلة (ʿilla fāʿila): Efficient cause; the agent that produces an effect.
علة صورية (ʿilla ṣūriyya): Formal cause; the form that defines a thing’s essence.
علة غائية (ʿilla ghāʾiyya): Final cause; the purpose or end for which something is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is al-Razi's definition of 'asl' considered invalid?
A) It fails ʿaks because not all things called 'asl' are needed.
B) It fails ṭard because it applies to efficient causes, formal causes, etc., which are not called 'asl'.
C) It is not a nominal definition.
D) It is too narrow.

Key Takeaway
A valid nominal definition must satisfy both ṭard (comprehensiveness) and ʿaks (exclusivity); al-Razi's definition of 'asl' fails ṭard and is therefore invalid.

Defining 'Asl' and the Two Types of Definitions (Haqiqi and Ismi)
Definition and critique of 'asl' with types of definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions, apply the conditions of tard and aks al-tard to evaluate definitions, and explain why Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' is inadequate in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A valid definition of a technical term must be co-extensive (tard and aks) and appropriate to its conventional nature.

How do we define the foundational terms of Usul al-Fiqh? This passage introduces the definition of 'asl' (the singular of 'usul') and the key distinction between real definitions (haqiqi) of essences and nominal definitions (ismi) of conventional terms. You will see how the Hanafi tradition rigorously tests definitions for logical completeness using the conditions of tard (inclusion) and aks al-tard (converse). We will also examine why a famous definition by Imam al-Razi in al-Mahsul fails this test.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Aspects of Defining Usul al-Fiqh
Recognize that Usul al-Fiqh can be defined either as a construct (mudaf-mudaf ilayh) or as a title for a specific science. The passage focuses on the construct aspect, first defining 'asl'.
The two aspects are hadd idafi (definition by construction) and hadd laqabi (definition by title).
2
Extract the Hanafi Definition of 'Asl'
State the definition given: 'al-asl ma tubna 'alayhi ghayruh' (the asl is that upon which something else is built). Note that this includes both sensory and rational foundations.
Examples: wall for roof (sensory), evidence for ruling (rational).
3
Distinguish Between Haqiqi and Ismi Definitions
Understand that haqiqi definitions define real essences (e.g., man = rational animal), while ismi definitions define conventional terms coined for particular meanings (e.g., 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins'). The definition of 'asl' is ismi.
The passage insists that for conventional terms, an ismi definition is appropriate and must satisfy the conditions of tard and aks al-tard.
4
Apply the Conditions of Tard and Aks al-Tard
Tard means the definition applies to everything the defined term applies to; aks al-tard means the defined term applies to everything the definition applies to. Together they ensure co-extensiveness.
Example: If 'asl' is defined as 'that which is needed', the definition applies to causes, forms, ends, conditions (all are needed), but the term 'asl' does not apply to them, so the definition lacks aks al-tard (fails converse).
5
Critique Imam al-Razi's Definition
Identify the flaw: Imam al-Razi in al-Mahsul defined 'asl' as 'ma yuhtaju ilayh' (that which is needed). The passage argues this is not muttard because it applies to entities (e.g., efficient cause, formal cause, final cause, condition) that are needed but not called 'asl'. Thus it fails the ismi definition criteria.
This critique shows the precision expected in Hanafi usul; a definition must match conventional usage exactly.

تر یعنی یہ اصول فقہ ہے یا اصول فقہ کیا ہے؟ پس ہم تعریف کریں گے اس کی اولا اضافت کے اعتبار سے اور ثانیا اس اعتبار سے کہ وہ لقب ہے مخصوص علم کا ۔ اور بہر حال اس کی تعریف اضافت کے اعتبار سے پس و محتاج ہوتی ہے مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف پس فرمایا " اصل وہ ہے کہ جس پر غیر کی بنیاد رکھی جائے۔ پس ابتناء شامل ہے۔ ابتناء حس کو اور وہ ظاہر ہے اور ابتنا عقلی کو اور وہ حکم کا مرتب ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل پر۔ اور اس کی تعریف کرنا محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ وہ نمرد نہیں ہے۔ اور تحقیق تعریف کی اس (اصل) کی امام رازی نے محصول میں اسی کے ساتھ ۔ اور جان لیجیے کے بے شک تعریف یا تو حقیقی ہے جیسے ماھیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف اور یا تعریف امی ہے جیسے ماھیات اعتبار یہ کی تعریف جیسے ہم مرکب کریں کسی شے کو ایسے امور سے کہ وہ اس کے اجزاء ہوں ہمارے مرکب کرنے کے اعتبار سے پھر ہم نے وضع کیا ہے اس مرکب کے لیے ایک نام مثل لفظ اصل کے اور فقہ اور جنس اور نوع اور اس جیسی مثالوں کے۔ پس تعریف اسمی وہ بیان کرنا ہے یہ کہ : شک اسم کون سی مٹی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے ( اور شرط لگائی گئی ہے دونوں کے لیے طرد کی ) یعنی وہ چیز کہ صادق آئے اس پر حد تو صادق آئے اس پر محدود اور ( شرط لگائی گئی ہے عکس طرد کی ) یعنی ہر وہ چیز کہ صادق آئے اس پر محدود تو صادق آئے اس پر حد بھی ۔ پس جب کہا جائے انسان کی تعریف میں کہ وہ بے شک وہ حیوان ماشی ہے تو اس میں طرد نہیں ہے اور اگر کہا جائے کہ حیوان کا تب بالفعل ہے تو یہ تعریف منعکس نہیں ہے۔ (اور نہیں ہے کوئی شک اس میں کہ بے شک اصل کی تعریف تعریف امی ہے ) یعنی بیان کرنا ہے اس کا کہ بے شک لفظ اصل کون سی چیز کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ پس وہ تعریف جو ذکر کی گئی ہے۔ محصول میں وہ مطرد نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ وہ ) یعنی اصل ( کہ نہیں اطلاق کیا جاتا اس کا فاعل پر ) یعنی علت فاعلیہ پر ( اور صورت پر ) یعنی علت صور یہ پر ( اور غایت پر ) یعنی علت غائیہ پر ( اور شرط پر ) جیسے ادوات صناعت ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تعریف صادق ہے ان اشیاء پر بوجہ ہونے ان کے محتاج الیہ اور محدود نہیں صادق آتا ان پر اس لیے کہ ان اشیاء میں سے کسی شے کا نام نہیں رکھا جاتا ہے اصل ۔ پس یہ تعریف اسمی درست نہیں ہے۔
تشریح ۔ اصول الفقہ :۔ اس کی ترکیب میں دو احتمال ہیں۔ (۱) یہ خبر ہے مبتدا محذوف کی اصل عبارت یہ ہوگی ۔ ”ھذہ اصول الفقہ“ ۔ (۲) اصول الفقہ مبتداء ہے اور اس کی خبر ماھی محذوف ہے۔
اصول فقہ کی دو حیثیتیں
فتعرفھا:۔ یہاں سے بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ کی دوحیشیتیں ہیں۔(۱) لفظی (۲) معنوی۔ لفظوں کے اعتبار سے یہ مضاف مضاف الیہ ہیں۔ اور معنی و مفہوم کے اعتبار سے یہ ایک خاص فن کا لقب ہے دونوں اعتبار سے اصول فقہ کی تعریف ہوگی۔ لفظوں کے اعتبار سے جو تعریف ہوگی وہ حد اضافی کہلاتی ہے۔ اور معنی کے لحاظ سے جو تعریف ہوگی وہ حد لقمی کہلاتی ہے تو پہلے ہم حد اضافی کو بیان کریں گے ۔ خداضافی کے اعتبار سے مضاف کی تعریف علیحدہ اور مضاف الیہ کی تعریف علیحدہ ہوگی ۔ سب سے پہلے مضاف یعنی اصول کی تعریف ہوگی۔ اصول جمع ہے اصل کی۔
اصل حسی و عقلی دونوں کو شامل ہے
الاصل ما تبنی علیہ غیرہ :۔ اصل وہ ہے جس پر غیر کی بنیاد رکھی جائے۔ تو منی کو فرع اور مبنی علیہ کو اصل کہتے ہیں اور یہاں ابتنا ء ابتغاء کی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے یعنی ابتنا حسی کو بھی اور ابنا عقلی کو بھی ۔
ابتاء حسی: ابتکاء جسی کہتے ہیں کہ بنی اور مینی علیہ دونوں کا اور اک حواس ظاہرہ کے ساتھ کیا جاسکے جیسے چھت مینی اور دیوار مبنی علیہ ہے۔
ابتنا عقلی : ابتاء علی کہتے ہیں جس کا اور اک حواس ظاہرہ نہ کرسکیں بلکہ حواس باطنہ کریں جیسے حکم مبنی ہے اور دلیل منی علیہ ہے۔ امام رازی کی تردید
و تعريفه بالمحتاج اليه لا يطرد : ۔ یہاں سے مصنف نے امام فخر الدین رازی کا رد کیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ امام نے اپنی کتاب محصول میں اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کیا ہے ۔ کہ اصل وہ ہے جو محتاج الیہ ہو ۔ ماتن فرماتے ہیں یہ تعریف درست نہیں۔ درست کیوں نہیں ہے؟ اس کا سمجھنا تین مقدموں پر موقوف ہے۔ مقدمہ اولی: تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) تعریف حقیقی ۔ (۲) تعریف امی ۔ (۱) تعریف حقیقی یہ ہے کہ ماھیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف کی جائے۔ (۲) تعریف امی یہ ہے کہ ماھیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف کی جائے۔ ماعیت کی تعریف: ماهیت کہتے ہیں شے کے ان اجزاء کو جن سے مل کر شے بنے ۔ پھر اگر ماهیت خارج میں پائی جائے کسی معتبر کے اعتبار کرنے سے یا فارض کے فرض کرنے سے تو یہ ماهیت اعتبار یہ ہے ۔ اور اگرشی کی ماہیت خارج میں معتبر کے اعتبار اور فارض کے فرض کرنے کے بغیر پائی جائے تو یہ ماهیت حقیقیقہ ہے ۔ ماهیت حقیقیہ کی مثال یہ ہے کہ انسان کی تعریف کی جائے حیوان ناطق کے ساتھ اور ماھیت اعتباریہ کی مثال یہ ہے کہ ہم کسی چیز کو مرکب کریں ایسے امور کے ساتھ جو
That is, this is Usul al-Fiqh or what is Usul al-Fiqh? So we will define it: first according to its construction (idafa) and second according to its being a title for a specific science. In any case, its definition according to construction requires defining the mudaf and mudaf ilayh. So he said: 'Al-Asl is that upon which something else is built.' Hence, 'ibna' (building) includes: sensory building, which is apparent, and rational building, which is the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence. And defining it with 'ma yuhtaju ilayh' (what is needed) is not inclusive. And Imam al-Razi researched and defined it (al-asl) in his book al-Mahsul with that. And know that definition is either haqiqi (real), like the definition of real essences, or ismi (nominal), like the definition of conventional essences: such as when we compose a thing from matters that are its parts by virtue of our composition, then we assign a name to that composite, like the word 'asl' and 'fiqh' and 'jins' and 'naw' and similar examples. So ismi definition is to explain that: for what meaning the name is coined. And the condition for both is tard (mutual inclusion) — i.e., whatever the definition applies to, the defined also applies; and the condition is 'aks al-tard' (converse) — i.e., whatever the defined applies to, the definition also applies. So when it is said in the definition of man: 'He is a walking animal', it lacks tard; and if it is said 'an animal that actually speaks', that definition is not converse. (And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is an ismi definition) — i.e., it is to explain that the word 'asl' is coined for what thing. So the definition mentioned in al-Mahsul is not inclusive (mutard), because (asl) is not applied to the agent (efficient cause), nor to form (formal cause), nor to end (final cause), nor to condition — like tools of the craft. So it is known that this definition applies to those things because they are needed, but the defined does not apply to them because none of those things is named 'asl'. So this ismi definition is not correct.
Explanation: Usul al-Fiqh: In its construction there are two possibilities: (1) It is the predicate of a deleted subject, the original phrase being 'Hadha usul al-fiqh'. (2) 'Usul al-Fiqh' is the subject and its predicate 'ma hiya' is deleted.
The two aspects of Usul al-Fiqh
'Fa tu'arrifuha': From here he explains that Usul al-Fiqh has two aspects: (1) literal (lafzi) and (2) conceptual (ma'nawi). In terms of words, it is mudaf-mudaf ilayh, and in terms of meaning and significance, it is the title of a specific art. According to both aspects, Usul al-Fiqh is defined. The definition according to words is called hadd idafi (definition by construction), and the definition according to meaning is called hadd laqabi (definition by title). So first we will mention the hadd idafi. According to hadd idafi, the definition of the mudaf is separate and the definition of the mudaf ilayh is separate. First is the definition of the mudaf, i.e., 'usul'. 'Usul' is the plural of 'asl'.
'Asl' includes both sensory and rational
'Al-Asl is that upon which something else is built': So the built thing is called far' and the foundation is called asl, and here 'ibna' includes both types: sensory building and rational building.
Sensory building: Sensory building is that where the built and the foundation can both be perceived by the external senses, like the roof is built and the wall is the foundation.
Rational building: Rational building is that which cannot be perceived by external senses but by internal senses, like the ruling is built and the evidence is the foundation.
Refutation of Imam al-Razi
'And his definition with 'al-muhtaj ilayh' does not have tard (is not inclusive)': From here the author refutes Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The gist is that the Imam defined 'asl' in his book al-Mahsul with 'ma yuhtaju ilayh' — that 'asl' is that which is needed. The author says this definition is not correct. Why is it not correct? Understanding this depends on three premises. First premise: There are two types of definition: (1) real (haqiqi) definition and (2) nominal (ismi) definition. (1) Real definition is the definition of real essences. (2) Nominal definition is the definition of conventional essences. Definition of essence (mahiyya): Mahiyya refers to the parts of a thing from which the thing is composed. Then if the essence is found in external reality by the consideration of a considerer or the assumption of an assumer, it is a conventional essence. And if the thing's essence exists externally without the consideration or assumption, it is a real essence. Example of real essence: defining man as 'rational animal'. Example of conventional essence: when we compose a thing from matters that it...

Commentary
This passage is a definitional study of the term 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The author explains that we can define it from two angles: the grammatical structure (idafi) and the technical meaning (laqabi). The main focus is on defining the word 'asl' (plural: usul). The author gives a functional definition: 'asl is that upon which something else is built.' This includes both sensory foundations (like a wall for a roof) and rational foundations (like evidence for a ruling). The author then critiques Imam al-Razi's definition in al-Mahsul, where he defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed' (al-muhtaj ilayh). The problem is that this definition is too broad: it applies to things that are needed but not called 'asl', like efficient causes, forms, ends, and conditions. Therefore, the definition fails the condition of tard (co-extensiveness). The author distinguishes between real definitions (of real essences) and nominal definitions (of conventional terms). Since 'asl' is a coined term, its definition is nominal, and thus it must precisely match its conventional usage. Imam al-Razi's definition does not meet this standard. The passage then transitions to the two aspects of Usul al-Fiqh and prepares to define each part separately. The teacher should note that this is a typical Hanafi usul approach: meticulous about definitional precision and critical of definitions that are not co-extensive.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): That upon which something else is built (sensory or rational).
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): Definition of a real essence, such as defining man as 'rational animal'.
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): Definition explaining the conventional coinage of a term for a meaning.
طرد (tard): The condition that the definition applies to everything the defined term applies to.
عكس طرد (aks al-tard): The converse condition that everything the defined term applies to, the definition applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'ma yuhtaju ilayh' (that which is needed) incorrect?
A) Because it is a haqiqi definition, not an ismi one.
B) Because it does not include sensory foundations.
C) Because it applies to things that are needed but are not called 'asl', so it lacks aks al-tard.
D) Because it is a definition of a conventional term.

Key Takeaway
A precise ismi definition must be mutually inclusive (tard and aks al-tard) with the term's conventional usage; otherwise it fails as a valid definition in Hanafi usul.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Necessity of Definition and Subject in Usul al-Fiqh
Providing a rational proof for the essentiality of definition and subject matter and explaining the matn phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rational proof for the necessity of knowing a science's definition and subject matter to identify why the Hanafi school requires foundational study of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Without knowing a science's definition and subject, its issues become either impossible or confused — knowledge requires both conception and affirmation.

Why must a student of usul al-fiqh begin by learning its definition and subject matter? This lesson presents a rational argument (dalil aqli) that clarifies that without a regulating aspect (jihah), the issues of any science become either infinite (inconceivable) or finite but mixed with non-issues. Understanding this foundational point will help you appreciate the structure of Hanafi usul texts and the importance of proper conceptualization before deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
The passage argues that knowing the definition and subject matter of a science is necessary for any seeker. Locate this claim in the text.
The claim is stated explicitly: 'تعریف، موضوع کا جاننا کیوں ضروری ہے؟'
2
Understand the Preamble on Regulating Aspects
The passage explains that words have infinite states, but they are grouped by specific aspects (jihah) into separate sciences, like morphology (sarf) and syntax (nahw). This shows that a science is a regulated multitude of issues from one aspect.
This analogy sets up the proof: without the regulating aspect, the issues lose structure.
3
Trace the Rational Proof
The proof proceeds: if the seeker does not know the regulating aspect, the issues are either infinite (impossible to conceive) or finite but mixed with non-issues, leading to confusion. Therefore, conception (tasawwur) and affirmation (tasdiq) require that aspect.
Note the key terms: 'غیر متناہی' (infinite) and 'اختلاط' (mixing).
4
Distinguish Definition and Subject
The passage clarifies: definition (ta'rif) distinguishes the science in the seeker's mind, while subject matter (mawdu') distinguishes it externally. Both are necessary.
Hanafi usul: the mawdu' of usul al-fiqh is the proofs of fiqh in their capacity as proofs.
5
Analyze the Matn Explanation
The commentator explains that the matn author anticipated the seeker's eagerness to define 'usul al-fiqh' and thus said 'Hadhihi usul al-fiqh' or posed the question himself. This illustrates a pedagogical device.
This shows how classical texts embed the answer to the student's expected question.

پہلے بطور تمہید کے مقدمہ سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔ مقدمہ:۔ لفظ کے بہت سارے احوال ہوتے ہیں۔ جو غیر متناہی ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن ان احوال کی ایک جماعت ایک جہت سے منضبط ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری جماعت دوسری جہت سے منضبط اسی طرح تیسری جماعت تیسری جہت سے منضبط ہوتی ہے۔ اور لفظ کے احوال کا ایک طائفہ جو ایک جہت سے منضبط ہو وہ مستقل علم اور فن ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا لفظ مفرد کے اشتقاق اور تصریف کے بہت سے جو مسائل منضبط ہیں وہ مستقل علم ہیں۔ اور ان کا نام صرف ہے۔ اور لفظ کے اعراب کے اعتبار سے جو مسائل منضبط ہیں وہ مستقل علم ہیں اور ان کا نام علم نحو ہے۔ پس جو بھی علم ہے۔ وہ ایسے مسائل کثیرہ کا نام ہے جو ایک خاص جہت سے منضبط ہوں ۔ دلیل:۔ اب جو بھی کسی کثرت مضبوطہ کا طالب ہوگا۔ ( کسی علم کا طالب ہو گا ) اس کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ ان مسائل کو اسی جہت خاص سے جانے تا کہ اس کو مسائل کے تصور بوجہ ما سے ان کی تصدیق حاصل ہو جائے اور اس تصور کو معرفت اور تعریف کہتے ہیں۔ اگر وہ مسائل کو اسی جہت خاص سے نہیں جانے گا تو مسائل دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہوں گے ۔ (۱) غیر متناہی ہونگے (۲) یا متناہی ہوں گے ۔ اگر غیر متناہی ہوں گے تو ان کا تصور بھی نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ چہ جائیکہ تصدیق حاصل ہو جب تصدیق حاصل نہیں ہوگی تو علم ہی حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ علم نام ہے تصدیق کا ۔ اور اگر مسائل ملتا ہی ہوں گے تو بہر حال مطلوب کا غیر مطلوب میں اختلاط ہو جائے گا۔ تو کبھی مقصود کو حاصل کرے گا اور کبھی غیر مقصود کو حاصل کرے گا ۔ اس لیے طالب کو اس جہت خاص کے ساتھ ان مسائل کا جاننا ضروری ہے ۔ تا کہ وہ مسائل غیر مقصودہ سے مسائل مقصودہ کوممتاز کر سکے۔ اور موضوع کو جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ تعریف کے ساتھ تو علم ، طالب کے ہاں ممتاز ہوتا ہے اور موضوع کے ساتھ ایک علم دوسرے علم سے نفس الامر ( خارج ) میں ممتاز ہوتا ہے۔ فحسین تشوقت:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آٹھواں حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے۔ کہ ماتن نے لفظ " اصول الفقہ" کی دو ترکیبیں ذکر کی تھیں۔ ان کی وضاحت فرمارہے ہیں۔ فرمایا کہ جب تعریف کا جانا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ تعریف سے علم طالب کے ہاں ممتاز ہو جاتا ہے تو طالب کو شوق پیدا ہوا کہ اس علم کی تعریف معلوم ہوتی کہ قریب تھا کہ سامع سوال کردے۔ ماتن نے اس کو سوال سے چپ رکھنے کے لیے فرمایا " هذا الاصول الفقہ " یہ اصول الفقہ ہے۔ یا طالب علم کو سائل کے مرتبے میں اتار کر خود ماتن نے ہی اس کی طرف سے اپنی زبان سے سوال کیا ہے۔ کہ "اصول نتہ ماھی پھر اس کی تعریف میں شروع ہو گئے۔
Why is it necessary to know the definition and subject? 'Because it is the right of the seeker': This is the seventh part of the commentary. From here, the proof is given for why it is necessary to know the definition and subject in the preface. Before understanding the proof, it is necessary to understand the preface as a preamble. Preface: Words have many states, which are infinite. But one group of these states is regulated from one aspect, another group from another aspect, and a third group from a third aspect. And a group of word states regulated from one aspect constitutes an independent science and art. For example, the many issues of derivation and conjugation of a single word that are regulated constitute an independent science, and its name is morphology. And the issues regulated with respect to vowel endings constitute an independent science, and its name is syntax. So any science is a name for a multitude of issues regulated from a particular aspect. Proof: Now anyone who seeks any regulated multitude (i.e., seeks any science) must know those issues from that particular aspect so that he obtains a conception of the issues and then their affirmation. This conception is called knowledge and definition. If he does not know the issues from that particular aspect, the issues will inevitably be either infinite or finite. If they are infinite, their conception is impossible, let alone affirmation. When affirmation is not obtained, knowledge itself is not obtained, because knowledge is the name of affirmation. And if the issues are finite, then in any case there will be mixing of the sought with the non-sought. So sometimes he will obtain the intended and sometimes the unintended. Therefore it is necessary for the seeker to know those issues with that particular aspect so that he can distinguish the intended issues from the unintended. And it is necessary to know the subject because by definition the science is distinguished for the seeker, and by the subject one science is distinguished from another in reality (externally). 'So when he longed': This is the eighth part of the commentary. In this phrase, the commentator explains the text: that the matn author mentioned two constructions of the word 'usul al-fiqh'. He explains them. He said that when knowledge of the definition is necessary because by definition the science is distinguished for the seeker, the seeker becomes eager to know the definition of this science, so much so that the listener was about to ask a question. To keep him silent from questioning, the matn author said, 'Hadhihi usul al-fiqh' (This is usul al-fiqh). Or, placing the seeker in the position of the questioner, the matn author himself asked from his side: 'What is usul?' then he began its definition.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage provides a rational argument (dalil aqli) for why a student of any science must first know its definition and subject matter. It uses the analogy of language sciences: words have infinite possible states, but they are regulated from specific aspects, giving rise to distinct sciences like morphology and syntax. Similarly, the seeker of a science must approach its issues from the correct aspect to obtain proper conception and affirmation; otherwise, the issues become either infinite (inconceivable) or finite but mixed (causing confusion). The subject matter further distinguishes sciences externally. The commentator then explains that the matn author anticipated a student's eagerness to define 'usul al-fiqh' and immediately said 'This is usul al-fiqh' or posed the question himself to introduce the definition. This reflects a pedagogical technique in Hanafi matn writing.

Key Terms
تعریف (ta'rif): The definition of a science, which provides a conceptual distinction for the seeker
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science, which distinguishes it from other sciences in external reality
جہت (jihah): The particular aspect from which a set of issues is regulated, forming a distinct science
تصدیق (tasdiq): Affirmation or judgment about a conception, which constitutes knowledge (ilm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Knowing the definition and subject matter of a science is essential for proper conception and affirmation, as without them the issues become impossible or confused.

The Organization of Knowledge by Perspective
Explaining that each science is defined by a unique perspective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the concept of jiha (perspective) and explain how a science is defined by its subject matter and perspective.

Core Idea
Each science is a body of issues regulated by a unique perspective; without perspective, knowledge is chaotic.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text lays the foundational principle that every discipline, including usul al-fiqh, is defined by a specific perspective (jiha) that organizes its issues. Understanding this helps us distinguish between sciences and grasp the structure of knowledge, which is essential for systematic learning and teaching.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key concepts
Read the passage and mark the terms 'jiha', 'ahwal al-lafz', and 'ilm'. Note how they relate: words have many states (ahwal), but these are grouped by different perspectives (jihaat) to form separate sciences (ulum).
These terms are foundational in Hanafi classification of sciences.
2
Understand the organizing principle
The passage states that a group of word states regulated by one perspective becomes an independent science. Examples: Sarf (morphology) from the perspective of derivation and conjugation; Nahw (syntax) from the perspective of declension (i'rab). Grasp that the perspective is what makes a collection of issues a coherent science.
In usul al-fiqh, the perspective is how rulings are derived from dalils.
3
Analyze the rational proof (dalil)
The author proves that a student must know the specific perspective of a science. Without it, the issues become either infinite (impossible to conceive) or finite but intermingled with other issues, leading to confusion. Therefore, knowing the perspective is necessary for distinguishing intended from unintended knowledge.
This is a logical argument (talil) using the impossibility of mastering infinite issues.
4
Apply the distinction between tasawwur and tasdiq
The passage mentions that through the perspective, the student obtains tasawwur (conception) of the issues and then tasdiq (assent). 'Ilm is defined as tasdiq. Recognize that without the perspective, tasawwur is impossible (if issues infinite) or faulty (if mixed), blocking the attainment of knowledge.
This connects to Hanafi epistemology: 'ilm is certain knowledge (yaqin).
5
Distinguish internal vs external differentiation of sciences
The passage concludes that sciences are distinguished in the mind of the student by their definition (ta'rif), but in external reality (nafs al-amr) by their subject matter (mawdu'). Note that the subject gives objective distinctness between sciences.
This principle helps in defining usul al-fiqh and separating it from other shar'i sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمہ:۔ لفظ کے بہت سارے احوال ہوتے ہیں۔ جو غیر متناہی ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن ان احوال کی ایک جماعت ایک جہت سے منضبط ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری جماعت دوسری جہت سے منضبط اسی طرح تیسری جماعت تیسری جہت سے منضبط ہوتی ہے۔ اور لفظ کے احوال کا ایک طائفہ جو ایک جہت سے منضبط ہو وہ مستقل علم اور فن ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا لفظ مفرد کے اشتقاق اور تصریف کے بہت سے جو مسائل منضبط ہیں وہ مستقل علم ہیں۔ اور ان کا نام صرف ہے۔ اور لفظ کے اعراب کے اعتبار سے جو مسائل منضبط ہیں وہ مستقل علم ہیں اور ان کا نام علم نحو ہے۔ پس جو بھی علم ہے۔ وہ ایسے مسائل کثیرہ کا نام ہے جو ایک خاص جہت سے منضبط ہوں ۔
دلیل:۔ اب جو بھی کسی کثرت مضبوطہ کا طالب ہوگا۔ ( کسی علم کا طالب ہو گا ) اس کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ ان مسائل کو اسی جہت خاص سے جانے تا کہ اس کو مسائل کے تصور بوجہ ما سے ان کی تصدیق حاصل ہو جائے اور اس تصور کو معرفت اور تعریف کہتے ہیں۔ اگر وہ مسائل کو اسی جہت خاص سے نہیں جانے گا تو مسائل دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہوں گے ۔ (۱) غیر متناہی ہونگے (۲) یا متناہی ہوں گے ۔ اگر غیر متناہی ہوں گے تو ان کا تصور بھی نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ چہ جائیکہ تصدیق حاصل ہو جب تصدیق حاصل نہیں ہوگی تو علم ہی حاصل نہیں ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ علم نام ہے تصدیق کا ۔ اور اگر مسائل ملتا ہی ہوں گے تو بہر حال مطلوب کا غیر مطلوب میں اختلاط ہو جائے گا۔ تو کبھی مقصود کو حاصل کرے گا اور کبھی غیر مقصود کو حاصل کرے گا ۔ اس لیے طالب کو اس جہت خاص کے ساتھ ان مسائل کا جاننا ضروری ہے ۔ تا کہ وہ مسائل غیر مقصودہ سے مسائل مقصودہ کوممتاز کر سکے۔ اور موضوع کو جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ تعریف کے ساتھ تو علم ، طالب کے ہاں ممتاز ہوتا ہے اور موضوع کے ساتھ ایک علم دوسرے علم سے نفس الامر ( خارج ) میں ممتاز ہوتا ہے۔
Introduction: Words have many states that are infinite. But a group of these states is regulated by one perspective; another group by a second perspective; similarly a third group by a third perspective. And a collection of word states regulated by one perspective is an independent science and art. For example, the many issues regarding derivation and morphology of a single word are regulated into an independent science called Sarf. And the issues regarding the declension of words are regulated into an independent science called Nahw. So any science is a name for a multitude of issues regulated by one specific perspective. Proof: Whoever seeks any organized multitude (i.e., seeks a science) must know those issues from that specific perspective so that he can obtain tasawwur (conception) of the issues regarding how they are, and then their tasdiq (assent). This tasawwur is called ma'rifah and ta'rif. If he does not know them from that specific perspective, the issues will be either infinite or finite. If infinite, their tasawwur is impossible, let alone tasdiq. Without tasdiq, knowledge is not attained because knowledge is named as tasdiq. If they are finite, the desired (issues) will intermingle with the undesired, sometimes attaining the objective and sometimes not. Therefore, it is necessary for the student to know these issues with that specific perspective so that he can distinguish intended issues from unintended ones. And knowing the subject is necessary because through definition the science is distinguished for the student, and through the subject one science is distinguished from another externally (in reality).
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the nature of sciences and their organization. The author explains that words have numerous states (ahwal), but these states can be grouped from different perspectives (jihaat). Each group of states, when collected and organized from one perspective, forms an independent science (fann). For example, the science of Sarf (morphology) collects issues related to derivation and conjugation of a word, while Nahw (syntax) collects issues related to the declension of words. Thus, any science is essentially a body of issues (masa'il) that are regulated by a specific perspective. The author then provides a rational proof (dalil) for why a student must know these issues from that specific perspective. Without recognizing the unifying perspective, the issues remain either infinite (and thus impossible to conceive) or finite but confused with other issues. In the latter case, the student may accidentally obtain some intended knowledge but cannot reliably distinguish it from unintended knowledge. Hence, knowing the perspective is necessary for proper distinction. Additionally, the subject matter (mawdu') of a science distinguishes it from other sciences externally, while the definition distinguishes it in the mind of the student. This foundational concept is crucial in Hanafi usul al-fiqh because the discipline of usul al-fiqh is itself defined by its own specific perspective and subject matter.

Key Terms
جہت (jiha): A specific viewpoint or aspect from which a collection of issues is organized and regulated in a science.
احوال لفظ (ahwal al-lafz): The various states of a word, such as its derivation, morphology, and declension, which are infinite in number.
علم ('ilm): A body of numerous issues regulated by a specific perspective, also defined as tasdiq (assent) of conceptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what distinguishes one science from another externally (in reality)?
A) The definition (ta'rif)
B) The subject matter (mawdu')
C) The number of issues
D) The name of the science

Key Takeaway
Every science is defined by a unique perspective (jiha) that organizes its issues; knowing this perspective is essential for systematic learning and distinguishes the science internally by definition and externally by subject matter.

Prioritizing Additive vs. Titular Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh
Dispute over prioritizing definitions of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the additive (idafi) and titular (laqabi) definitions of usul al-fiqh, and evaluate the arguments for prioritizing one over the other.

Core Idea
The additive definition takes precedence over the titular to avoid repetition in defining the discipline.

This passage presents a key methodological debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: should we define 'usul al-fiqh' by its parts (additive) or as a title (laqabi)? The commentator explains both positions and the logic behind the author's choice to prioritize the additive. Understanding this helps grasp how Hanafi scholars structure their definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of usul al-fiqh
In the source, usul al-fiqh has two aspects: verbal (compound of 'usul' and 'fiqh') and meaning (a title for the discipline). From these derive the additive and titular definitions.
2
Understand arguments for prioritizing titular definition
Some scholars give two arguments: (1) The titular definition concerns the intended meaning (the discipline), and the intended prevails over the unintended. (2) The titular definition treats the term as a simple, and simple precedes compound.
3
Understand arguments for prioritizing additive definition
The author gives two counterarguments: (1) The additive definition is the origin (manqul 'anhu), and the origin precedes the derived. (2) Prioritizing the titular leads to repetition: fiqh must be defined in both definitions.
4
Analyze the repetition argument
The author argues that if the titular definition is presented first, fiqh is defined there, then again in the additive definition. This is redundant. By presenting additive first, fiqh is defined once.
5
Conclude the preferred approach
In Hanafi tradition, the additive definition is typically presented first to avoid repetition and maintain logical flow in teaching usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعریف اضافی و لقبی کا پس منظر
واصول الفقہ :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ نہم ہے۔ تاریخ اصول فقہ کی دو تعریفوں کا پس منظر بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں۔ (۱) لفظی (۲) معنوی لفظوں کے اعتبار سے یہ مرکب اضافی ہے۔ لیکن معنوی حیثیت یہ ہے کہ مرکب اضافی سے منقول ہو کر اس علم کا لقب ہو چکا ہے۔ اب ہر حیثیت سے اس کی تعریف ہوگی ۔ منقول عنہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے تعریف اضافی ہوگی اور منقول ہونے کے اعتبار سے تعریف لقمی ہوگی۔

علماء کے طریق کار کے اختلاف پر دلائل
قدم بعضہم :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا حصہ دہم ہے۔ غرض اس میں علماء کے طریق کار کے اختلاف پر دلائل ذکر کرنا ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے حدیقی کو مقدم کیا ہے اور مصنف نے حد اضافی کو مقدم کیا ہے۔ دونوں حضرات کی دو دو دلیلیں ہیں۔ تاریخ نے دونوں کی دلیلوں کو بیان کیا ہے۔ بعض کی دلیل اول: کہ تعریف لقمی معنی علمی کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ اور اعلام میں مقصود معنی علمی ہوتا ہے۔ تو معنی علمی یعنی اضافی کے اعتبار سے مقصود ہوا اور معنی اضافی غیر مقصود اور ضابطہ ہے کہ مقصود غیر مقصود پر مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے حد لقمی حد اضافی پر مقدم ہونی چاہیے۔ دلیل ثانی: اصول الفقہ حدیقی کے اعتبار سے بمنزلہ مفرد اور بسیط کے ہے۔ اور تعریف اضافی کے اعتبار سے بمنزل مرکب اسے نمول مرکب کے ہے ۔ لفظ اصول اور فقہ سے۔ اور بسیط مقدم ہوتا ہے مرکب سے اس لیے تعریف لھی کومقدم ہونا چاہیے۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ کی دو دلیلیں۔ دلیل (۱):- تعریف اضافی منقول عنہ ہے اور تعریف لقمی منقول ہے۔ اور منقول عنہ مقدم ہوتا ہے منقول سے اس لیے تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا۔
ولیل (۲) اگر لقی کو تعریف اضافی پر مقدم کریں تو اس میں تکرار محض لازم آتا ہے۔ وہ اس طرح کہ تعریف لھی میں فقہ کی قید موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ اصول فقہ کی حد قمی یہ ہے۔ ھو العلم بالقواعد التی توصل بھا الی الفقہ ۔ اور کامل تعریف وہ ہوتی ہے کہ تعریف سے اس کے اجزاء کی معرفت بھی معلوم ہو جائے ۔ اور یہاں چونکہ فقہ جز ہے۔ اس لیے اس کی تعریف کرنا پڑے گی۔ پھر حد اضافی میں مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کے دوبارہ تعریف کرنی پڑے گی۔ ورنہ تعریف اضافی متحقق نہیں ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر تعریف
اضافی کو مقدم کریں جیسا کہ مصنف نے کیا ہے تو فقہ کی تعریف معلوم ہو جائے گی اور خدا لقمی میں دوبارہ اس کی تعریف کرنے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں پڑے گی۔ اس طرح تکرار لازم نہیں آئے گا۔
Background of additive and titular definitions. And usul al-fiqh: This is the ninth part of the commentary's text. It explains the background of the two definitions of usul al-fiqh, that usul al-fiqh has two aspects: (1) verbal (2) meaning. In terms of words, it is an additive compound. But in terms of meaning, it has been transferred from an additive compound to become a title of this knowledge. Now it will be defined from each aspect. In terms of being that from which it is transferred, the definition will be additive, and in terms of being transferred, the definition will be titular. Arguments on the difference of scholars' methods. Some presented: This is the tenth part of the commentary's text. The purpose is to mention arguments on the difference of scholars' methods. Some scholars gave priority to the titular definition, and the author gave priority to the additive definition. Both have two arguments each. The author has stated both arguments. First argument of some: The titular definition is in terms of the meaning of the knowledge. And in proper names, the intended meaning is the knowledge meaning. So the meaning of knowledge, i.e., additive, is intended, and the additive meaning is unintentional, and the rule is that the intended takes precedence over the unintended. Therefore, the titular definition should take precedence over the additive definition. Second argument: Usul al-fiqh in terms of the titular definition is like a simple and singular thing. And in terms of the additive definition, it is like a compound, like a compound from the words usul and fiqh. The simple takes precedence over the compound, so the titular definition should take precedence. Two arguments of the author (may Allah have mercy on him). First argument: The additive definition is that from which transfer occurs, and the titular definition is transferred. That from which transfer occurs takes precedence over that which is transferred, so the additive definition is given priority. Second argument: If the titular definition is given priority over the additive definition, then pure repetition becomes necessary. In the following way: The titular definition contains the restriction of fiqh, because the titular definition of usul al-fiqh is: It is knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh. And a complete definition is one that gives knowledge of its parts. And here, since fiqh is a part, it will have to be defined. Then in the additive definition, the second part (fiqh) will have to be defined again. Otherwise, the additive definition will not be realized. But if the additive definition is given priority, as the author did, then the definition of fiqh will be known, and in the titular definition there will be no need to define it again. Thus repetition will not occur.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute about which definition of usul al-fiqh should be presented first: the additive (idafi) definition or the titular (laqabi) definition. The commentator explains that usul al-fiqh has two aspects: verbally it is a compound of 'usul' and 'fiqh', but it has become a title for the discipline. Therefore, it can be defined in two ways: by its parts (idafi) or as a title (laqabi). Some scholars argue that the titular definition should be prioritized because it relates to the meaning of the discipline, which is what is intended, and because a simple definition takes precedence over a compound one. The author (al-Musannif) argues that the additive definition should be prioritized because it is the original meaning from which the title is derived, and because prioritizing the titular would lead to repetition: the titular definition requires defining fiqh, and then the additive definition would require defining it again, causing unnecessary repetition. By prioritizing the additive, fiqh is defined first, and the titular can refer back to it. This is a methodological dispute within Hanafi usul al-fiqh about how to properly define a discipline that has both a compositional and a transferred meaning.

Key Terms
تعريف اضافي (ta'rif idafi): Definition of usul al-fiqh by considering it as a compound of 'usul' and 'fiqh'.
تعريف لقبي (ta'rif laqabi): Definition of usul al-fiqh by considering it as a title for the discipline.
منقول (manqul): That which is transferred (the titular definition is transferred from the additive meaning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (al-Musannif), what problem arises if the titular definition is given priority over the additive definition?
A) It contradicts the rules of Arabic grammar.
B) It leads to unnecessary repetition in defining 'fiqh'.
C) It makes usul al-fiqh difficult to understand.
D) It ignores the importance of the word 'usul'.

Key Takeaway
In defining usul al-fiqh, the additive (idafi) definition should be presented before the titular (laqabi) to avoid redundancy.

Defining Uṣūl al-Fiqh: The Meaning of Aṣl and the Role of Iḍāfah
Explaining the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh by iḍāfah and the linguistic meaning of aṣl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define uṣūl al-fiqh by analyzing its components (aṣl and fiqh) and the iḍāfah, and evaluate the Hanafi position that retains the linguistic meaning of 'aṣl' over the customary 'dalīl'.

Core Idea
Aṣl linguistically means 'that upon which something is built', but only from the perspective of being built upon.

Defining a compound term like 'uṣūl al-fiqh' requires defining each part and the relationship between them. The key component is 'aṣl', which has a rich linguistic meaning that, with the right restriction, perfectly captures what we mean by the foundations of fiqh. In this lesson, we will see why the Hanafi school insists on staying with the original meaning rather than switching to the narrower technical term 'dalīl'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
Recognize that defining uṣūl al-fiqh by iḍāfah means defining the muḍāf (uṣūl), the muḍāf ilayh (fiqh), and the iḍāfah itself. The passage notes that scholars often omit defining the iḍāfah because it is well-known.
The iḍāfah acts as a formal part of the compound.
2
Understand the linguistic meaning of 'aṣl'
Linguistically, 'aṣl' is 'that upon which something is built' (mā yubtana ʿalayhi al-shayʾ). Critically, it comes with an implicit restriction: min ḥaythu annahu yubtana ʿalayhi – from the perspective that it is built upon. Without this restriction, anything that serves as a foundation in any context could be called aṣl, causing confusion.
The restriction (qayd al-ḥaythiyyah) is essential for relational terms.
3
Apply the restriction to exclude extraneous foundations
For example, the proofs of fiqh themselves are built upon the science of tawḥīd. But when defining uṣūl al-fiqh, we do not consider that perspective. The restriction ensures that only the direct foundation of fiqh (the proofs) is intended, not further back.
This prevents the term from becoming too broad.
4
Analyze the dispute over the customary meaning
Some scholars argued that in the term 'uṣūl al-fiqh', 'aṣl' has been transferred in custom (ʿurf) to mean 'dalīl' (proof). The author (al-Tawḍīḥ) counters that there is no need to deviate from the linguistic sense, because it already includes intellectual building, which covers proofs. By adding 'fiqh' (an intellectual matter), the intellectual aspect is specified.
The Hanafi principle: stay with the original meaning unless a clear necessity to transfer.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi definition
Thus, uṣūl al-fiqh is 'that upon which fiqh is built and to which it relies' – i.e., the proofs of fiqh. The linguistic meaning with the restriction suffices, and the customary sense is not needed.
This definition preserves the broad yet precise scope of the term.

التَّوْحِيدِ فَإِنَّهَا بِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ فُرُوعٌ لَا أُصُولٌ وَقَيدُ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْإِضَافِيَّاتِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ كَثِيرًا مَا يُحْذَفَ لِشُهْرَةِ أَمْرِهِ ، ثُمَّ نُقِلَ الْأَصْلُ فِي الْعُرْفِ إِلَى مَعَانِ أُخَرَ ، مِثْلُ الرَّاحِحِ وَالْقَاعِدَةِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ وَالدَّلِيلِ فَذَهَبَ بَعْضُهُمُ إلَى أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ هَاهُنَا الدَّلِيلُ وَأَشَارَ الْمُصَنِّفُ إلَى أَنَّ التَّقْلَ خِلاف الأَصْلِ وَلَا ضَرُورَةَ فِي الْعُدُولِ إِلَيْهِ ؛ لأنَّ الِابْتِنَاء كَمَا يَشْمَلُ الْحِسْيَّ كَابْتِنَاء السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجُدْرَانِ وَابْتِنَاء أَعَالِي الْجُدْرَانِ عَلَى أَسَاسِهِ وَأَغْصَانِ الشَّجَرِةِ عَلَى دَوْحَتِهِ كَذَلِكَ يَشْمَلُ الابْتِنَاء الْعَقْلِى كَابْتِنَاءِ الْحُكُم عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ فَهَهُنَا يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِى وَبِالْإِضَافَةِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ الَّذِي هُوَ مَعْنِّى عَقْلِيٌّ يُعْلَمُ أَنَّ الابْتِنَاءَ هُنَا عَقْلِيٌّ فَيَكُونُ أُصُولُ الْفِقْهِ مَا يُبْتَنى هُوَ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسْتَنَدُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا مَعْنَى لِمُسْتَنَدِ الْعِلْمِ وَمُبْتَنَاهُ إِلَّا دَلِيلُهُ وَبِهَذَا يَنْدَفِعُ مَا يُقَالُ إِنَّ الْمَعْنَى الْعُرْفِيَّ أَعْنِي الدَّلِيلَ مُرَادٌ قَطعًا فَأَيُّ حَاجَةٍ إِلَى جَعْلِهِ بِالْمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِلْمَقْصُودِ وَغَيْرِهِ فَإِن قُلْتَ : ابْتِنَاء الشَّيْء عَلَى الشَّيْء إِضَافَةٌ بَيْنَهُمَا ، وَهُوَ أَمْرٌ عَقْلِيٌّ قَطعًا قُلْتُ أَرَادَ بِالابْتِنَاءِ الْحِسَى كَوْنَ الشَّيْئَيْنِ مَحْسُوسَيْنِ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ مِثْلُ ابْتِنَاء السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجِدَارِ وَابْتِنَاءِ الْمُشْتَقَ عَلَى الْمُشْتَقِّ مِنْهُ كَالْفِعْلِ عَلَ
As for its definition by way of iḍāfah, it requires the definition of the muḍāf, which is al-uṣūl, and the muḍāf ilayh, which is al-fiqh, because the definition of a compound requires the definition of its components. The non-evident [parts] due to the necessity of knowledge of the whole depending on knowledge of its parts, and it also requires the definition of the iḍāfah itself, because it is like a formal part, except that they did not address it, because it is known that the meaning of the iḍāfah of a derived term and what is in its meaning is the specification of the muḍāf ilayh by the concept of the muḍāf. For example, 'the proof of the issue' is what is specific to it by virtue of being a proof upon it. So 'aṣl al-fiqh' is what is specific to it from the perspective that it is built upon it and relies upon it. So al-uṣūl is the plural of 'aṣl', and in language it is that upon which something is built, from the perspective that it is built upon it. With this restriction, for example, the proofs of fiqh are excluded from the perspective that they are built upon the science of tawḥīd, for in this regard they are branches, not principles. And the restriction of al-ḥaythiyyah is necessary in the definition of relational terms, except that it is often omitted due to its notoriety. Then 'aṣl' was transferred in custom to other meanings, such as the preponderant, the universal principle, and the proof. So some held that what is intended here is the proof. The author indicated that adherence to the literal meaning is contrary to the principle and there is no necessity to deviate to it, because 'ibtināʾ' (building) as it includes physical building, like the building of a roof on walls, the building of the upper parts of walls on their foundation, and the branches of a tree on its trunk, similarly it includes intellectual building, like the building of a ruling on its proof. So here it is taken in the linguistic sense, and by its addition to fiqh, which is an intellectual meaning, it is known that the building here is intellectual. So uṣūl al-fiqh is that upon which it is built and to which it relies, and there is no meaning of the foundation of knowledge and its basis except its proof. And by this is repelled what is said: 'Indeed the customary meaning, i.e., the proof, is intended definitively, so what need is there to make it carry the linguistic meaning that includes the intended and other than it?' If you say: 'The building of one thing upon another is a relationship between them, and it is definitively an intellectual matter', I say: 'He intended by physical building the two things being sensible, and then it includes like the building of the roof on the wall and the building of the derived term on its derivation, like the verb on...'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed definition of 'uṣūl al-fiqh' as a compound term (by iḍāfah). The commentator explains that we must define both parts: 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh', and also the iḍāfah itself, although scholars often omit the latter due to its obviousness. The key point is the linguistic meaning of 'aṣl' as 'that upon which something is built', but with the crucial restriction (qayd) of 'min ḥaythu annahu yubtana ʿalayhi' — i.e., considered from the perspective of being built upon. Without this restriction, any underlying layer could be considered a 'principle', for example, fiqh proofs are built on tawḥīd, but they are not 'uṣūl al-fiqh' in this sense. The passage then addresses a dispute: some argue that 'aṣl' here means 'dalīl' (proof) in its customary usage. The author rejects this, arguing that the linguistic sense of 'ibtināʾ' covers both physical and intellectual building, and by iḍāfah to 'fiqh' (an intellectual concept), it is clear that intellectual building is intended. Thus, 'uṣūl al-fiqh' are the proofs upon which fiqh rulings are based, and we need not switch to the customary meaning. The passage ends with a counter-objection and response about the nature of 'ibtināʾ'.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): Linguistically: that upon which something is built, with the restriction of al-ḥaythiyyah (perspective). In urf: sometimes used for preponderant, universal principle, or proof.
إضافة (iḍāfah): The grammatical construct linking muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh; in definition, it acts as a formal part of the compound.
حيظية (ḥaythiyyah): The restriction indicating the specific perspective from which something is considered; essential in defining relational terms.
ابتناء (ibtināʾ): Building, including both physical (sensible) and intellectual (mental) construction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the restriction 'min ḥaythu yubtana ʿalayhi' in the definition of 'aṣl'?
A) To exclude physical building from the definition.
B) To ensure that only intellectual building is considered, not physical.
C) To exclude cases where something is a foundation for something else in a different category (e.g., fiqh proofs being built on tawḥīd).
D) To include both physical and intellectual building.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of uṣūl al-fiqh retains the linguistic meaning of 'aṣl' with the perspective restriction, affirming that it refers to the proofs on which fiqh is built, without needing the customary transfer to 'dalīl'.

Defining Usul al-Fiqh: The Necessity of Defining Its Components
Analyzing the definition of usul al-fiqh and the importance of defining its parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the compound nature of 'usul al-fiqh' and explain why defining its parts (usul, fiqh, and idafa) is necessary for a proper definition of the discipline.

Core Idea
A compound term's definition requires defining each non-obvious part — usul al-fiqh is no exception.

In this passage, the commentator of Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih explains that to define 'usul al-fiqh' properly, one must define its constituent parts: 'usul' and 'fiqh', as well as the idafa (construct phrase) that links them. This is because a compound (murakkab) is known only through its parts. The passage also addresses a potential objection about the need to define idafa, showing that it is a formal part but is left undefined due to its obvious meaning. By understanding this definitional method, you will grasp the foundational concept of usul al-fiqh as the discipline that provides the evidence upon which fiqh is based.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound term
Recognize that 'usul al-fiqh' is a compound (murakkab) consisting of 'usul' and 'fiqh' connected by idafa. Note that compounds require definition of their parts.
2
Recall the rule for defining compounds
The commentator states that defining a compound depends on defining its non-obvious (ghayr bayyin) parts. 'Usul' and 'fiqh' are non-obvious because their technical meanings are not immediately clear.
3
Recognize the role of idafa
The idafa (construct) itself is a formal part of the compound, but the commentator explains it is not defined separately because its meaning is well-known: it indicates specification (ikhtisas) of the first term by the second.
4
Apply to the definition of usul al-fiqh
Thus, defining 'usul al-fiqh' requires defining 'usul' (as foundations/evidence) and 'fiqh' (as knowledge of practical rulings), and understanding that the idafa indicates a rational foundation (ibtina' 'aqli).
5
Refute a common objection
The passage refutes the idea that one could simply take 'asl' in its customary meaning (as 'evidence') and avoid defining parts. The commentator argues that the literal meaning (foundation) includes both sensory and rational, and the rational foundation (ruling on evidence) is the intended meaning here, so the idafa to fiqh makes it clear.
