أَرَادَ مَا هُوَ الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِى الْعُرْفِ مِنْ أَنَّ ابْتِنَاءَ السَّقْفِ عَلَى الْجِدَارِ بِمَعْنَى كَوْنِهِ مَبْنِيًّا عَلَيْهِ وَمَوْضُوعًا فَوْقَهُ مِمَّا يُدْرَكَ بِالْحِس وَحِينَئِذٍ يَخْرُجُ مِثْلُ ابْتِنَاءِ الْفِعْلِ عَلَى الْمَصْدَرِ مِنْ الْحِسَى وَلَا يَدْخُلُ فِي الْعَقْلِي بِتَفْسِيرِهِ وَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ تَرَتَّبَ الْحُكْمِ عَلَى دَلِيلِهِ لَا يَصْلُحُ تَفْسِيرًا لِلابْتِنَاء الْعَقْلِي ، وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ مِثَالٌ لَهُ لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّ ابْتِنَاء الْمَجَازِ عَلَى الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ عَلَى الْقَوَاعِدِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولَاتِ عَلَى عِلَيْهَا وَالأفْعَالِ عَلَى الْمَصَادِر وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ ابْتِنَاءٌ عَقْلِيٌّ
ترجمہ: قولہ اما تعریبا الخ بہر حال اسکی تعریف اضافت کیسا تھ پر محتاج ہوگی مضاف کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اور وہ سول ہے اور مضاف الیہ کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف اور وہ فقہ ہے اسلیئے کہ مرکب کی تعریف محتاج ہوتی ہے اپنے مفردات غیر بینہ کی تعریف کی طرف بوجہ بدیہی ہونے کل کی معرفت کے موقوف ہونے کے اپنے اجزاء کی معرفت پر اور محتاج ہوگی اضافت کی تعریف کرنے کی طرف بھی اسلیئے کہ وہ بمنزلہ جزو صوری کے ہے مگر بے شک وہ نہیں در پے ہوئے اسکی طرف بوجہ معلوم ہونے اس کے کہ مشتق اور اسکے ہم معنی کی اضافت کا مطلب مضاف کا خاص ہوتا ہے مضاف الیہ کے ساتھ مضاف کے مفہوم کے اعتبار سے مثلاً دلیل المسئلہ وہ ہے کہ مختص ہو اس کے ساتھ اس کے دلیل ہونے کے اعتبار سے اس پر ۔ پس فقہ کی اصل وہ ہے کہ جو شخص ہو اس فقہ کے ساتھ اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک منی ہو فقہ اس پر اور منسوب ہو اسکی طرف۔ پس اصول جمع ہے اصل کی اور و و لغت میں وہ ہے کہ مبنی ہو اس پر کوئی تھی اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ پینی ہے اس پر اور اس قید کے ساتھ نکل جائیں گی ادلتہ فقہ مثلاً اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ مبنی ہوں علم تو حید پر پس وہ اس اعتبار کے ساتھ فرع ہیں نہ کہ اصول۔ اور حیثیت کی قید ضروری ہے اضافیات کی تعریف میں مگر بے شک کثرت سے اس کو حذف کیا جاتا ہے اس کے امر کی شہرت کی وجہ سے پھر نقل کیا گیا ہے اصل کو عرف میں دوسرے معانی کی طرف مثل راج قاعدہ کلیہ اور دلیل پس چلے گئے ان میں سے بعض اس بات کی طرف کہ بیشک مراد اس کے ساتھ یہاں دلیل ہے اور اشارہ کیا مصنف نے اس بات کی طرف کہ بے شک نقل خلاف اصل ہے اور نہیں ہے کوئی ضرورت عدول کرنے میں اسکی طرف اس لئے کہ ابتاء جس طرح مشتمل ہوتی ہے حسی کو جیسے چھت کا بنی ہونا دیواروں پر اور دیواروں کے اوپر والے حصوں کا مبنی ہونا اسکی بنیادوں پر اور درخت کی شاخوں کا اس کے تنے پر اسی طرح شامل ہوتا ہے ابتائے عقلی کو جیسے حکم کا بنی ہونا اس کی دلیل پر پس یہاں محمول کیا جائے گا معنی اموی پر اور اضافت کرنے کے ساتھ اس کی فقہ کی طرف جو معنی عقلی ہے معلوم ہو جاتا ہے کہ بے شک اجتماء یہاں عقلی ہے۔ پس اصول فقہ وہ ہے جس پر فقہ مبنی
ہو اور منسوب ہو اسکی طرف اور نہیں ہے کوئی معنی کسی علم کے منسوب الیہ اور بنی علیہ بننے کے لئے مگر اس کی دلیل ، اور اسی کے ساتھ مندفع ہو جائے گا۔ وہ جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ بیشک معنی عرفی مراد لیتا ہوں میں دلیل کو مراد ہے قطعا۔ پس کونسی حاجت ہے اس کے پھیرنے کی معنی لغوی کی طرف جو شامل ہونے والا ہے مقصود کو اور اس کے غیر کو ۔ پس اگر تو کہے کہ شی کا مبنی ہو ناشی پر یہ کو۔ اضافت ہے ان دونوں کے درمیان اور وہ امر عقلی ہے قطعاً۔ میں کہوں گا کہ مراد ابنتنا حسی کے ساتھ دو چیزوں کا محسوس ہوتا ہے اور اس وقت داخل ہوگا اس میں سقف کے مینی ہونے کی مثل دیواروں پر اور مشتق کا مبنی ہونا مشتق منہ پر جیسے فعل کا ابتناء مصدر پر یا ارادہ کیا اس کا کہ جس کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے عرف میں اس بات سے کہ بیشک چھت کا بنی ہونا دیواروں پر اس معنی کے ساتھ کہ وہ پینی ہے اس پر اور اسکے اوپر رکھی ہوئی ہے ان اشیاء میں سے ہے جنکا ادراک کیا جاتا ہے جس کے ساتھ اور اس وقت نکل جائے گا فعل کے مبنی ہونے کی مثل مصدر پر حسی سے اور نہیں داخل ہو گا عقلی میں اسکی ( ماتن ) تفسیر کے مطابق اور حق بات یہ ہے کہ حکم کا مرتب ہونا اسکی دلیل پر نہیں صلاحیت رکھتا ابتناء عقلی کی تفسیر کی اور سوائے اسکے نہیں ہے وہ مگر ایک مثال ہے اس کے لیئے بوجہ یقینی ہونے اس بات کے کہ مجاز عقلی کا بنی ہونا حقیقت پر اور احکام جزئیہ کا بنی ہونا قواعد کلیہ پر اور معلولات کا مبنی ہونا انکی عمل پر اور افعال کا بنی ہونا مصادر پر اور جو اسکے مشابہ ہیں یہ سب ابتناء عقلی ہیں۔
مرکبات کی تعریف کیلئے اس کے مفردات غیر بینہ کی تعریف ضروری ہے قوله اما تعریفها باعتبار الاضافہ :۔ یہ شرح کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارع یہاں سے ماتن کے دعویٰ کی دلیل بیان کرنا ہے ماتن نے یہ دعویٰ کیا تھا کہ تعریف اضافی میں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ مرکب ہے اور ضابطہ ہے کہ مرکب کی تعریف کیلئے اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ کی تعریف ضروری ہوتی ہے تو چونکہ اصول فقہ مرکب ہے اور اصول اور فقہ اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ ہیں اس لئے انکی تعریف ضروری ہوگی یعنی جس طرح کل کی معرفت موقوف ہے اجزا کی معرفت پر اسی طرح مرکب کی تعریف موقوف ہے مفردات کی معرفت پر ۔
ويحتاج الى تعريف الاضافہ ایضاً :- یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے سوال:۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ مرکب اضافی کی معرفت اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے اور مرکب اضافی کے مفردات اور اجزاء میں جس طرح مضاف مضاف الیہ داخل ہیں اسی طرح اضافت بھی داخل ہے کیونکہ صورۃ یہ بھی مرکب کا جزو ہے اور غیر مبینہ ہے لہذا اسکی بھی تعریف کرنی چاہیے تھی حالانکہ اسکی تعریف نہیں کی اسکی کیا وجہ ہے
He intended what is considered in customary usage, that the roof's being built upon the wall means it is constructed upon it and placed above it — something perceived by sense. In that case, examples like the action's being based on its verbal noun come out from the sensory meaning and do not enter into the rational according to his interpretation. The truth is that the ordering of a ruling upon its evidence is not valid as an interpretation of rational foundation; rather, it is an example of it, due to certainty that metaphorical meaning's being based on literal meaning, particular rulings on universal principles, effects on their causes, actions on their verbal nouns, and similar things — all these are rational foundations. Translation: Regarding his statement 'but definition of its...' in any case, its definition by way of idafa requires defining the mudaf (the first term) — which is usul — and defining the mudaf ilayh (the second term) — which is fiqh. This is because the definition of a compound needs the definition of its non-obvious parts, due to the obvious fact that knowledge of the whole depends on knowledge of its parts. It also requires defining the idafa because it is like a formal part, but they did not bother to define it due to its being well-known: the meaning of idafa for derivatives and their synonyms is that the mudaf is specific to the mudaf ilayh with respect to the mudaf's meaning. For example, 'dalil al-mas'alah' is that specific to it in terms of being evidence for it. Thus 'asl al-fiqh' is that which is such with respect to fiqh, so that fiqh is based on it and attributed to it. So usul is the plural of asl, which in language means something upon which something else is built, with the condition that it is based on it. With this condition, the evidences of fiqh (for example, being based on tawhid) are excluded; they are branches, not principles. The condition of aspect (haythiyya) is necessary in definitions of relational terms, but it is often omitted due to notoriety. Then 'asl' was transferred customarily to other meanings such as the predominant universal principle and the evidence. Some went so far as to say that what is meant here is 'evidence', and the author indicated that the transfer is against the literal meaning and there is no need to deviate to it, because foundation includes the sensory (like a roof on walls, upper parts on foundations, branches on a trunk) and includes the rational (like a ruling on its evidence). So here it will be interpreted in the rational meaning, and by its idafa to fiqh it becomes clear that the connection here is rational. Thus usul al-fiqh is that upon which fiqh is based and to which it is attributed. There is no meaning of a science being attributed and based upon except its evidence. With this the objection is refuted: 'It is said that the customary meaning is intended, meaning evidence decisively; then what need is there to revert to the literal meaning which includes both intended and other?' Then if you say: 'A thing's being based on something is a relation between them, and it is a rational matter absolutely,' I would say: 'Sensory foundation means the sensory perception of two things; then it includes the roof on walls and the derivative on its source (action on verbal noun). Or it is intended what is considered in custom: the roof on walls meaning it is built upon and placed above — these are things perceived by sense. Then the action's being based on its verbal noun would exit from the sensory and not enter the rational according to the matn's interpretation. The truth is that the ordering of the ruling on its evidence is not valid as an interpretation of rational foundation; rather, it is an example of it, due to certainty that rational foundation includes metaphorical on literal, particular rulings on universal principles, effects on their causes, actions on their verbal nouns, etc.' For the definition of compounds, the definition of its non-obvious parts is necessary. The statement 'But its definition with regard to idafa' — this is the first part of the commentary. The commentator's purpose here is to provide evidence for the matn's claim. The matn claimed that in the definition by idafa, knowledge of the mudaf and mudaf ilayh is necessary. The evidence is that usul al-fiqh is a compound, and the rule is that for defining a compound, defining its non-obvious parts is necessary. Since usul al-fiqh is a compound and usul and fiqh are its non-obvious parts, their definition is necessary — just as knowledge of the whole depends on knowledge of the parts, so too does the definition of a compound depend on the definition of its parts. 'And it also needs the definition of idafa' — this is the second part of the commentary. Here the answer to a potential question is given. The question: 'You stated that knowledge of the compound idafa depends on knowledge of its non-obvious parts, and among the parts of the compound idafa, just as the mudaf and mudaf ilayh are included, so too is the idafa itself included, because it is a formal part and is non-obvious; so it should also have been defined, yet it was not defined. What is the reason?'
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) is explaining the definition of usul al-fiqh. The author begins by clarifying the nature of 'foundation' (ibtina'), distinguishing between sensory (hissi) and rational ('aqli) foundation. Sensory foundation is physically perceptible, like a roof on a wall. Rational foundation is conceptual, like a ruling being based on its evidence. The passage then moves to the central issue: defining the compound term 'usul al-fiqh' requires defining its parts: 'usul' (foundations) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence). The commentator argues that since usul al-fiqh is a compound (murakkab), its definition depends on defining its non-obvious (ghair bayyin) parts. Therefore, one must define both 'usul' and 'fiqh'. Additionally, the idafa (construct phrase) itself is like a formal part, but it is not separately defined because its meaning is well-known: it indicates specification of the first term by the second. The passage also discusses the linguistic and customary usage of the word 'asl' (root/foundation), noting that it is often transferred to mean 'evidence' (dalil). The commentator refutes the objection that one could simply take 'asl' in its customary meaning and avoid defining its parts. The key insight is that the basis of a science is its evidence, and that rational foundation is the relevant type here. The passage concludes by showing the logical necessity of defining the parts, especially in response to the objection that if idafa is also a part, it should be defined. The commentator explains that idafa is not explicitly defined because its meaning is self-evident within the context of derivatives and their constructions.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): In language, that upon which something else is built; in technical usage, it is the foundation or evidence (dalil) of a discipline.
ابتناء (ibtina'): To be based or founded upon something; it can be sensory (hissi) or rational ('aqli).
اضافة (idafa): The construct phrase linking mudaf and mudaf ilayh; in definition, it indicates specification (ikhtisas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the idafa in 'usul al-fiqh' not separately defined?
A) Because it is not a real part of the compound.
B) Because its meaning is well-known among scholars of usul.
C) Because the matn forgot to define it.
D) Because idafa is not part of the definition.

Key Takeaway
Defining usul al-fiqh requires defining its components 'usul' and 'fiqh' and understanding the idafa as a rational foundation, ensuring conceptual precision.

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
Types of Ibnā' in Usul al-Fiqh: Rational vs. Sensory Building
Clarifying the meaning of 'ibnā' between sensory and rational

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sensory (ḥissī) and rational (ʿaqlī) building in Hanafi usul, and apply the correct interpretation to the relationship between a ruling and its evidence.

Core Idea
The dependency of a ruling on its evidence is rational building, not sensory – a key distinction in Hanafi usul.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the term 'ibnā'' (building) as it is used in usul al-fiqh. A common misconception is that this refers to physical support, like a roof on walls. The commentator argues that when we say a ruling is 'built upon' its evidence, we mean a rational, conceptual dependency, not a physical one. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its ambiguity
Recognize that the Arabic word 'ibnā'' can be interpreted in multiple ways: sensory (ḥissī), customary (ʿurfī), linguistic (lughawī), or rational (ʿaqlī).
The passage addresses a potential objection that interprets it sensorily.
2
Analyze the objection
The imaginary opponent argues that building is a relationship between two physical things (e.g., roof on walls) and is therefore sensory. Consider why this interpretation is problematic for usul.
The objection confuses physical dependency with conceptual dependency.
3
Understand the commentator's response
The commentator clarifies that the intended meaning in usul is rational building – a conceptual relationship like a ruling depending on its evidence, metaphor built on reality, or actions on their sources.
Examples are given to illustrate rational building.
4
List examples of rational building
From the passage: (1) rational metaphor on reality, (2) particular rulings on universal principles, (3) effects on causes, (4) actions on their sources. All these are rational, not sensory.
These examples reinforce that the relationship is conceptual.
5
Conclude the proper interpretation
Synthesize: In usul al-fiqh, when we say 'al-hukm mabniyyun 'ala al-dalīl' (the ruling is built upon the evidence), we mean rational dependency, not physical support.
This distinction prevents misinterpretation of usul terminology.

هو اور منسوب ہو اسکی طرف اور نہیں ہے کوئی معنی کسی علم کے منسوب الیہ اور بنی علیہ بننے کے لئے مگر اس کی دلیل ، اور اسی کے ساتھ مندفع ہو جائے گا۔ وہ جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ بیشک معنی عرفی مراد لیتا ہوں میں دلیل کو مراد ہے قطعا۔ پس کونسی حاجت ہے اس کے پھیرنے کی معنی لغوی کی طرف جو شامل ہونے والا ہے مقصود کو اور اس کے غیر کو ۔ پس اگر تو کہے کہ شی کا مبنی ہو ناشی پر یہ کو۔ اضافت ہے ان دونوں کے درمیان اور وہ امر عقلی ہے قطعاً۔ میں کہوں گا کہ مراد ابنتنا حسی کے ساتھ دو چیزوں کا محسوس ہوتا ہے اور اس وقت داخل ہوگا اس میں سقف کے مینی ہونے کی مثل دیواروں پر اور مشتق کا مبنی ہونا مشتق منہ پر جیسے فعل کا ابتناء مصدر پر یا ارادہ کیا اس کا کہ جس کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے عرف میں اس بات سے کہ بیشک چھت کا بنی ہونا دیواروں پر اس معنی کے ساتھ کہ وہ پینی ہے اس پر اور اسکے اوپر رکھی ہوئی ہے ان اشیاء میں سے ہے جنکا ادراک کیا جاتا ہے جس کے ساتھ اور اس وقت نکل جائے گا فعل کے مبنی ہونے کی مثل مصدر پر حسی سے اور نہیں داخل ہو گا عقلی میں اسکی ( ماتن ) تفسیر کے مطابق اور حق بات یہ ہے کہ حکم کا مرتب ہونا اسکی دلیل پر نہیں صلاحیت رکھتا ابتناء عقلی کی تفسیر کی اور سوائے اسکے نہیں ہے وہ مگر ایک مثال ہے اس کے لیئے بوجہ یقینی ہونے اس بات کے کہ مجاز عقلی کا بنی ہونا حقیقت پر اور احکام جزئیہ کا بنی ہونا قواعد کلیہ پر اور معلولات کا مبنی ہونا انکی عمل پر اور افعال کا بنی ہونا مصادر پر اور جو اسکے مشابہ ہیں یہ سب ابتناء عقلی ہیں۔
He and attributed to him, and there is no meaning of any knowledge that is attributed to and built upon except its proof, and with it the objection will be repelled. What is said: 'Indeed, I intend the customary meaning, intending the proof absolutely.' So what need is there to turn it to the linguistic meaning which includes the intended and other than it? So if you say: 'The thing's being built upon what arises is an addition between the two, and it is a rational matter absolutely.' I would say: What is meant by sensory building is two things being perceived, and then it will include in it the like of the roof being built on walls, and the derived term being built upon its root, like the verb's building on the infinitive, or it is intended which is considered customary that the roof's building on walls in the sense that it is standing [قائم] on it and placed upon it, and it is among things that are perceived with it. And then the like of the verb's building on the infinitive will exit from the sensory and will not enter into the rational according to the interpretation of the matn. And the truth is that the ruling's being dependent on its proof does not have the capacity to be interpreted as rational building, and it is nothing but an example for it due to the certainty that the building of rational metaphor on reality, and the building of particular rulings on universal principles, and the building of effects on their causes, and the building of actions on their sources, and what resembles them, all of these are rational buildings.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a detailed clarification of the concept of 'ibnā'' (building) as it applies in usul al-fiqh. The commentator addresses a potential objection: when it is said that a ruling is 'built upon' its evidence, the term 'ibnā'' could be interpreted linguistically (sensory building, like a roof on walls) or customarily (which is still sensory) but the rational interpretation is the correct one. The author argues that the dependency of a ruling on its evidence is not sensory but rational, because the evidence does not physically support the ruling. Examples given include: rational metaphor built on reality, particular rulings on universal principles, effects on causes, and actions on their sources. All these are rational relationships. The passage also distinguishes between sensory building (which requires perception) and rational building (which is conceptual). The matn's interpretation is upheld: the phrase 'the ruling is built on its evidence' must be understood in a rational sense.

Key Terms
ابتناء (ibnā'): The dependency or relationship of one thing upon another, either sensory (حسی) or rational (عقلی).
عقلی (ʿaqlī): Rational, conceptual, not physically observable.
حسی (ḥissī): Sensory, physically perceptible.
عرفی (ʿurfī): Customary, based on common usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what kind of 'ibnā'' is the dependency of a ruling on its evidence?
A) Sensory building (حسی)
B) Customary building (عرفی)
C) Rational building (عقلی)
D) Linguistic building (لغوی)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the relationship between a ruling and its evidence is a conceptual dependency (rational building), not a physical one.

Method of Learning

Defining the Components of Uṣūl al-Fiqh
Methodology of defining compound terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of defining compound terms by identifying non-obvious parts (mufradāt ghayr mubayyana) and explaining the role of iḍāfah as a formal part.

Core Idea
A compound's definition requires defining its non-obvious parts and the relation that binds them.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, terms like 'uṣūl al-fiqh' are compound (murakkab). To define such a compound, we must first define its non-obvious parts. This lesson unpacks that methodology: we identify 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh' as the core components, and we examine why the genitive relation (iḍāfah) is a formal part that may or may not require explicit definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound term and its parts
Locate the term 'uṣūl al-fiqh' and list its apparent components: 'uṣūl' (foundations) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence). Note that the iḍāfah (addition/genitive) is a third, non-obvious part.
In Arabic, iḍāfah is the relation between mudaf and mudaf ilayh.
2
Distinguish obvious vs non-obvious parts
A part is 'non-obvious' (ghayr mubayyan) if its meaning is not immediately clear without further definition. Here, 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh' are considered non-obvious because their technical usages differ from everyday language.
The passage calls them 'mufradāt ghayr mubayyana'.
3
Recognize iḍāfah as a formal part
The iḍāfah is a formal part (juzʾ ṣūrī) because it gives the compound its structure and specific meaning. The commentator calls it 'like a formal part' (bimanzilat juzʾ ṣūrī) due to its concealment in writing.
Formal part does not require physical visibility; it is essential for the compound's existence (qawām).
4
Understand why iḍāfah may be omitted if well-known
The matn did not define iḍāfah because it is well-known (badīhī). However, the commentator still defines it because some intuitive concepts have hidden aspects (khafāʾ).
This shows the commentator's thoroughness: even well-known parts may need clarification if they can be misunderstood.
5
Apply the lexical and customary meaning of aṣl
The passage gives the lexical meaning of aṣl as 'that upon which another is built' and its customary meanings (evidence, analogical basis, universal principle). These multiple meanings affect how 'uṣūl al-fiqh' is understood.
Context determines which meaning is operative in a given ruling.

مرکبات کی تعریف کیلئے اس کے مفردات غیر بینہ کی تعریف ضروری ہے قوله اما تعریفها باعتبار الاضافہ :۔ یہ شرح کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارع یہاں سے ماتن کے دعویٰ کی دلیل بیان کرنا ہے ماتن نے یہ دعویٰ کیا تھا کہ تعریف اضافی میں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ مرکب ہے اور ضابطہ ہے کہ مرکب کی تعریف کیلئے اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ کی تعریف ضروری ہوتی ہے تو چونکہ اصول فقہ مرکب ہے اور اصول اور فقہ اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ ہیں اس لئے انکی تعریف ضروری ہوگی یعنی جس طرح کل کی معرفت موقوف ہے اجزا کی معرفت پر اسی طرح مرکب کی تعریف موقوف ہے مفردات کی معرفت پر ۔

ويحتاج الى تعريف الاضافہ ایضاً :- یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے سوال:۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ مرکب اضافی کی معرفت اس کے مفردات غیر مبینہ کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے اور مرکب اضافی کے مفردات اور اجزاء میں جس طرح مضاف مضاف الیہ داخل ہیں اسی طرح اضافت بھی داخل ہے کیونکہ صورۃ یہ بھی مرکب کا جزو ہے اور غیر مبینہ ہے لہذا اسکی بھی تعریف کرنی چاہیے تھی حالانکہ اسکی تعریف نہیں کی اسکی کیا وجہ ہے

جواب:۔ اضافت کی تعریف مشہور تھی اسلئے اس کو ذکر نہیں کیا مشہور اس طرح تھی کہ مشتق اور معنی مشتق کی اضافت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مضاف اپنے مفہوم کے اعتبار سے خاص ہو مضاف الیہ کیسا تھ مثلا دلیل المسئلہ میں دلیل مضاف ہے اور المسئلہ مضاف الیہ ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دلیل اس مسئلہ کے ساتھ مختص ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ وہ اس مسئلہ کی دلیل ہے اب اصول فقہ کا معنی ہوگا کہ ایسی چیزیں جو فقہ کے ساتھ منی علیہ ہونے کی حیثیت سے اور منسوب الیہ ہونے کی حیثیت سے مختص ہوں۔ اضافت کے جزو صوری ہونے کا مطلب

سوال (1): یہاں سے شاریخ نے اضافت کو بمنزلہ جز صوری کے کہا مطلقا جز صوری کیوں نہیں کہا؟ جواب (۱): جزء صوری اجسام میں پایا جاتا ہے (وہ نظر آتا ہے) اور مرکب اضافی اجسام کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے اس لئے بمنزل جزء صوری کے کہا۔

جواب (۲):۔ پہلا جواب درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ جز صوری کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ وہ نظر بھی آئے بلکہ جز صوری وہ ہے جس کی وجہ سے شئی کا قوام ہو اور مرکب اضافی بھی اضافت کی وجہ سے قائم ہے باقی بمنزل جزء صوری کے اس لئے کہا کہ لفظوں میں اضافت نظر نہیں آتی اس میں خفا ہے اور مصنفین کی عادت ہے جس چیز میں خفا ہو اسکو بمنزل سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں وگرنہ یہ حقیقت میں جزء صوری ہے۔

۱ (۲) ۔ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے کہا کہ اضافت کی تعریف بدیہی ہے تو پھر شارع نے اسکی تعریف کیوں کی؟ لیئے کہ بعض چیزوں میں بد یہی ہونے کے باوجود خفا ہوتا ہے اور بدیہی ہونے کا یہ مطلب نہیں کہ اسکی تعریف ہی جائز نہیں بلکہ ۔ یہ ہے کہ اسکی تعریف کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی ۔

اصل کا لغوی اور عرفی معنی اور ان کے نظائر

فالاصول جمع اصل یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ یہاں سے شاریخ نے اصول کا لغوی اور عرفی معنی بیان کیا ہے۔

لغوی معنی: ما يبتنى عليه غيره من حيث انه يبتنی علیہ یعنی اصل وہ چیز ہے کہ جس پر غیر کی بنیاد ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ غیر کیلئے منی علیہ اور بنیاد ہو۔

عرف: کے اعتبار سے کئی معانی ہیں مثلا راج دلیل مقیس علیہ قاعدہ کلیہ وغیرہ۔
For the definition of compounds, it is necessary to define its non-obvious parts. He said: 'As for its definition by way of addition...' This is the first part of the commentary. The purpose of the commentator from here is to present a proof for the claim of the matn. The matn claimed that in an additive definition, knowing the mudaf and mudaf ilayh is necessary. The proof is that uṣūl al-fiqh is a compound, and the rule is that for defining a compound, defining its non-obvious parts is necessary. So since uṣūl al-fiqh is a compound and uṣūl and fiqh are its non-obvious parts, their definition is necessary. That is, just as knowledge of the whole depends on knowledge of the parts, similarly defining a compound depends on knowledge of the parts.

And he also needs to define al-iḍāfah: This is the second part of the commentary. Here a hypothetical question is answered. Question: You said that knowledge of the additive compound depends on knowledge of its non-obvious parts, and in the parts of the additive compound, just as mudaf and mudaf ilayh are included, similarly iḍāfah is also included because formally it is also a part of the compound and is non-obvious. Therefore, it should have been defined as well, but it was not defined; what is the reason?

Answer: The definition of iḍāfah was well-known, so it was not mentioned. It was well-known in this way: The iḍāfah of the derivative and the meaning of the derivative means that the mudaf becomes specific in terms of its meaning with respect to the mudaf ilayh. For example, in 'dalīl al-mas'alah', dalīl is mudaf and al-mas'alah is mudaf ilayh. This means that the evidence is specific to this issue in the sense that it is the evidence for this issue. Now the meaning of uṣūl al-fiqh will be: things that are specific to fiqh in terms of being built upon it and being attributed to it.

The meaning of iḍāfah being a formal part:

Question (1): Here the commentator said that iḍāfah is like a formal part (bimanzilat juz' ṣūrī). Why did he not say it is absolutely a formal part? Answer (1): A formal part is found in bodies (it is visible), and the additive compound is not of the category of bodies, so he said 'like a formal part.'

Answer (2): The first answer is not correct because a formal part does not mean that it is visible; rather, a formal part is that by which the thing's essence is established (qawām). The additive compound is also established by iḍāfah. Nevertheless, he said 'like a formal part' because iḍāfah is not visible in words; there is concealment in it. And it is the habit of authors to use 'like' (bimanzilat) for things that have concealment. Otherwise, it is in reality a formal part.

Question (2): It happens that you said that the definition of iḍāfah is intuitive (badīhī), so why did the commentator define it? Answer: Because some things have concealment despite being intuitive, and being intuitive does not mean that its definition is not permissible; rather, it means that its definition is not needed.

The lexical and customary meanings of aṣl and their parallels.

Fa-al-uṣūl is the plural of aṣl. This is the third part of the commentary. Here the commentator explains the lexical and customary meanings of uṣūl.

Lexical meaning: ما يبتنى عليه غيره من حيث انه يبتنی علیہ, i.e., aṣl is the thing upon which another is built in the sense that it is a foundation and basis for the other.

Customary: It has several meanings, such as the preponderant (rājiḥ), evidence (dalīl), the analogized-upon (maqīs 'alayh), a universal principle (qā'ida kulliyya), etc.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how to define a compound term like 'uṣūl al-fiqh'. The commentator, following the matn, argues that to define a compound, one must first define its non-obvious parts. Since 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh' are non-obvious components, they are defined separately. Additionally, the iḍāfah (genitive relation) is a formal part of the compound, but it was not defined in the matn because it is well-known. The commentator addresses objections: why iḍāfah is called 'like a formal part' (due to concealment in words) and why it is defined despite being intuitive (because some intuitive things have hidden aspects). Finally, the lexical meaning of 'aṣl' is given as 'that upon which another is built', and its customary meanings include evidence, analogical basis, universal principle, etc.

Key Terms
مرکب (murakkab): A compound term consisting of multiple parts.
مفرد غیر مبین (mufrad ghayr mubayyan): A non-obvious part of a compound that requires definition.
اضافت (iḍāfah): The genitive construction that specifies the mudaf by the mudaf ilayh.
اصل (aṣl): Lexically: that upon which another is built. Customarily: evidence, analogical basis, universal principle.
جزو صوری (juz' ṣūrī): A formal part that gives a thing its essential structure, even if not physically visible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the commentator call the iḍāfah 'like a formal part' (bimanzilat juzʾ ṣūrī) instead of simply 'a formal part'?
A) Because iḍāfah is not a real part of the compound.
B) Because iḍāfah is not visible in the written form, and authors use 'like' for things with concealment.
C) Because formal parts only exist in physical bodies.
D) Because the matn did not define iḍāfah.

Key Takeaway
To define a compound term in Hanafi usul, you must define all non-obvious parts, including the relation (iḍāfah), though well-known parts may be omitted if no concealment exists.

Definition and Division of Ibtina' into Hissi and 'Aqli
Defining and dividing ibtina' with a critical objection and resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hissi and 'aqli ibtina' in usul al-fiqh and apply the correct definition to examples of rational ordering.

Core Idea
Ibtina' is not a relation but a placement: sensible if termini are physical, rational if intellectual.

This passage from a sharh on usul al-fiqh tackles the precise definition of 'ibtina'' (dependency or leaning) and its division into two types. The commentator first offers two definitions, then faces an objection regarding the derivation of verbs. Understanding this resolution is crucial for correctly analyzing how rulings and concepts depend on their sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposed definitions
The first definition is based on the perceptibility of the two termini (the built thing and the base). The second is based on whether the placement is visible (sensible) or not.
Both definitions aim to classify ibtina' but differ in criteria.
2
Test the first definition with the verb derivation example
Apply the first definition to the relationship between a derived verb and its masdar. The verb's 'hearing' is sensible, so the ibtina' would be hissi, which contradicts the intended 'aqli classification.
This exposes a weakness in the first definition.
3
Analyze the objection and the response
The critic argues that the first definition leads to an incorrect classification. The responder clarifies that the matn author's phrase 'order of a ruling upon its evidence' is merely an example, not the full definition of 'aqli ibtina'.
The proper definition is broader: any ordering according to reason.
4
Apply the corrected definition
Now, the derivation of a verb from its source is clearly 'aqli ibtina' because the relationship is intellectual, not physical.
This aligns with the second answer and resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت الجواب الاول: ابتداء کی یہ تعریف نہیں جو آپ کہہ رہے ہیں کہ نسبت بین الشیمین کا نام ہے بلکہ ابتناء کی تعریف طرفین کے اعتبار سے ہے اگر طرفین یعنی مینی اور مبنی علیہ دونوں محسوس ہوں جیسے چھت کا ابتنا ء دیواروں پر تو یہ ابتنا حسی ہے اور اگر طرفین غیر محسوس ہوں تو ابتغاء عقلی ہے جیسے ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ پس ابتاء کی تقسیم درست ہے۔ الجواب الثانی: ابتناء کا عرفی معنی مراد ہے یعنی مینی کا مبنی علیہ کے اوپر رکھا ہوا ہونا اور کبھی یہ رکھا ہوا نظر آتا ہے اور کبھی نہیں پہلے اعتبار سے حسی ہے اور دوسرے اعتبار سے عقلی ہے۔
وحينئذ يخرج مثل ابتاء الفعل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ایک سوال ذکر کر کے والحق سے اسکا جواب دیا ہے۔
اعتراض: پہلا جواب کمزور ہے کیونکہ اس میں یہ مذکور ہے کہ اگر طرفین دونوں محسوس ہوں تو یہ بنتا حسی ہے اب فعل مشتق ہے مصدر سے جیسے ضَرَبَ ضَرْبًا سے مشتق ہے اگر یہ بولیں تو کان سنتے ہیں اور کان حواس ظاہرہ میں سے ہیں تو ابتناء المشتق علی المشتق منہ ابتنا حسی میں داخل ہو جائیگی حالانکہ یہ ابتنا عقلی ہے حسی نہیں ہے اور دوسرے جواب کے ذریعے ابناء الفعل علی المصدر ابنتا حسی سے نکل جاتا ہے کیونکہ فعل کا مصدر پر رکھا ہوا ہوتا محسوس نہیں ہوتا لیکن عقلی میں داخل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مصنف کے نزدیک ابتا عقلی کی تعریف ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ ہے۔
جواب:۔ ماتن کا قول ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ ابتا عقلی کی تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک مثال ہے لہذا ترتب المشتق على المشتق منہ ابتنا عقلی میں سے ہے باقی ابتناء عقلی کی تعریف یہ ہے ترتب الشئی علی الشئی بحسب العقل یعنی ایک شئی کا ترتب ہو دوسری شئے پر عقل کے اعتبار سے اور یہ عام ہے اس میں حکم کا ترتب دلیل پر بھی داخل ہوگا اور افعال کا ترتب مصادر پر بھی داخل ہوگا۔
I said the first answer: The definition of ibtina' is not what you say, that it is the name of a relation between two things, but rather the definition of ibtina' is based on the two termini. If both termini, i.e. the built thing and that upon which it is built, are sensible, like the roof's leaning on walls, then this ibtina' is hissi (sensible). And if the two termini are non-sensible, then ibtina' is 'aqli (rational), like the order of a ruling upon its evidence. Thus the division of ibtina' is correct. The second answer: The customary meaning of ibtina' is intended, i.e. the built thing being placed upon that upon which it is built. Sometimes this placement is visible and sometimes not. From the first perspective it is hissi, and from the second it is 'aqli. And in that case, like ibtina' of the verb (upon its source) is excluded. This is the last part of the sharh's expression. In short, the commentators mention a question and then answer it with 'and the truth is'. Objection: The first answer is weak because it mentions that if both termini are sensible then it is hissi ibtina'. Now the verb is derived from the source, like ضَرَبَ derived from ضَرْبًا. If we say this, then 'hearing' is heard and 'hearing' is among the external senses, so the ibtina' of the derived upon that from which it is derived would enter into hissi ibtina', whereas it is 'aqli, not hissi. And by the second answer, the ibtina' of the verb upon the source is removed from hissi ibtina' because the verb's being placed upon the source is not sensible, but it does not enter into 'aqli according to the author's definition of 'aqli ibtina' as the order of a ruling upon its evidence. Answer: The matn author's statement 'order of a ruling upon its evidence' is not the definition of 'aqli ibtina' but rather an example. Hence the order of a derived term upon its source is part of 'aqli ibtina'. The remaining definition of 'aqli ibtina' is: the order of a thing upon another thing according to reason, i.e. a thing being ordered upon another thing from the perspective of reason. And this is general, including the order of a ruling upon its evidence and the order of verbs upon their sources.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion in the sharh about the definition and division of 'ibtina'' (building/leaning). The commentator first gives two answers to a question about how ibtina' is defined. The first answer defines ibtina' based on the two termini: if both are physical, it is hissi (sensible); if both are non-physical, it is 'aqli (rational). The second answer defines it based on whether the placement is visible (hissi) or not ('aqli). An objection is raised against the first answer: the derivation of a verb from its masdar (e.g., ضَرَبَ from ضَرْبًا) would then be considered hissi because 'hearing' is a sensible thing, but it is actually 'aqli. The commentator responds by clarifying that the matn author's statement 'order of a ruling upon its evidence' is just an example of 'aqli ibtina', not its definition. The true definition is 'the order of a thing upon another thing according to reason', which encompasses both rulings on evidence and verbs on sources. This passage highlights the importance of precise definitions in usul al-fiqh and shows how objections are resolved by refining the understanding of terms.

Key Terms
الابتناء (al-ibtinā’): The state of one thing being built or leaning upon another; a relationship of dependence.
حسی (ḥissī): Pertaining to the senses; perceptible by physical faculties.
عقلی (‘aqlī): Pertaining to the intellect; rational, non-sensible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected definition in the passage, which of the following is an example of 'aqli ibtina'?
A) A roof leaning on walls.
B) The derivation of the verb ضَرَبَ from the masdar ضَرْبًا.
C) A ruling being ordered upon its evidence.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
In usul al-fiqh, the definition of terms must be precise; 'aqli ibtina' includes any rational dependence, not only rulings on evidence.

Distinction Between Real and Nominal Definitions (Ta'rif Haqiqi wa Ismi)
Defining and differentiating real and nominal definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi), identify their conditions, and apply the distinction to legal terms in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A real definition describes a thing's essence; a nominal definition only clarifies its name's meaning.

In usul al-fiqh, definitions are not all the same. Some terms refer to real essences (like 'human'), while others are mere legal constructs (like 'ownership'). The classical Hanafi scholars distinguished between ta'rif haqiqi (real definition), which explains the quiddity itself, and ta'rif ismi (nominal definition), which only clarifies what a name means. This lesson unpacks that distinction from a foundational usul text, showing you when each type applies and why it matters for legal analysis.

Guided Path
1
Understand the preamble on quiddities
The author first sets up a framework: some quiddities (mahiyyat) are real (haqiqiyyah) and exist independently; others are i'tibariyyah (considered/constructed) and exist only in the mind. You must grasp this distinction to understand what a definition can describe.
Real quiddities have necessary parts; i'tibari quiddities do not.
2
Identify the two types of definitions
From the preamble, the author derives two kinds of definition: ta'rif haqiqi (real definition) describes the real quiddity itself, using essential (dhatiyyat) or accidental ('aradiyyat) properties. Ta'rif ismi (nominal definition) clarifies the meaning of a name without describing an essence.
Nominal definition works even when no real quiddity exists.
3
Analyze the conditions for each definition
A real definition requires the thing to have a real quiddity (thubut fi nafs al-amr). A nominal definition only requires that a name was put (wad') for a conceived meaning. Real definition produces a mental picture (taswir) of the essence; nominal definition clarifies (tubayyin) the name's reference.
The text gives two ways for nominal definition: using a more famous word (lafz ashhar) or expanding the summary indication (tafsil al-mujmal).
4
Apply the distinction to existent vs. non-existent things
Non-existent things (ma'dumat) have no reality, so only nominal definition is possible. Existent things (mawjudat) can be defined both ways, because they have both a concept and a reality.
This is a key test: if a thing has no extra-mental existence, any definition must be nominal.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul practice
Many legal terms in usul (like 'asl', 'fiqh', 'mujtahid') are i'tibari concepts. Their definitions are typically nominal, clarifying the meaning as put by the language or the legal tradition. Recognizing this avoids confusion when seeking the 'essence' of a legal concept.
Example: The definition 'al-asl ma yubna 'alayhi ghayruhu' is nominal because 'asl' has no real quiddity apart from its relational function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْمَسَائِلِ الْمَخْصُوصَةِ وَالْجِنسِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاء الْكُلِّيِّ الْمَقُولِ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالنَّوْعِ الْمَوْضُوعِ بِإِزَاء الْكُلِّيِّ الْمَقُولِ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ وَالتَّمْثِيلُ بِالْمُرَكَّبَةِ مِنْ عِدَّةٍ أُمُورٍ لَا يُنَافِي كَوْنَ بَعْضِ الْمَاهِيَّاتِ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةِ بَسَائِطَ عَلَى أَنَّ الْحَقَّ أَنَّهَا إِنَّمَا يُقَالُ لَهَا الْأُمُورُ الْاعْتِبَارِيَّةُ لَا الْمَاهِيَّاتُ الاعْتِبَارِيَّةُ إِذَا تُمُهَدَ هَذَا فَتَقُولُ مَا يَتَعَقَّلُهُ الْوَاضِعُ لِيَضَعَ بِإِزَائِهِ اسْمًا إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ مَاهِيَّةٌ حَقِيقِيَّةٌ أَوْ لَا وَعَلَى الْأَوَّلِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مُتَعَقَّلُهُ نَفْسَ حَقِيقَةِ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء أَوْ وُجُوهًا وَاعْتِبَارَاتٍ مِنْهُ فَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ لِمُسَمَّى بِهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا مَاهِيَّةٌ حَقِيقِيَّةٌ تَعْرِيفٌ حَقِيقِيٌّ يُفِيدُ تَصَوُّرَ الْمَاهِيَّةِ فِي الذَّهَنِ بِالذَّاتِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا أَوْ بَعْضِهَا أَوْ بِالْعَرَضِيَّاتِ أَوْ بِالْمُرَكَّبِ مِنْهُمَا وَتَعْرِيفُ مَفْهُومِ الِاسْمِ وَمَا تَعَقَّلَهُ الْوَاضِعُ فَوَضَعَ الِاسْمَ بِإِزَائِهِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسْمِيٌّ يُفِيدُ تَبَيُّنَ مَا وُضِعَ الِاسْمُ بِإِزَائِهِ بِلَفْظٍ أَشْهَرَ كَقَوْلِنَا الْغَضَفَرُ الْأَسَدُ أَوْ بِلَفْظٍ يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى تَفْصِيلِ مَا دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ الِاسْمُ إِجْمَالًا كَقَوْلِنَا الْأَصْلُ مَا يُبْتَنَى عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ فَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَعْدُومَاتِ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا اسْمِيًّا إِذْ لَا حَقَائِقَ لَهَا بَلْ مَفْهُومَاتٌ وَتَعْرِيفُ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ قَدْ يَكُونُ اسْمِيًّا وَقَدْ يَكُونُ حَقِيقِيًّا إِذْ لَهَا مَفْهُومَاتٌ وَحَقَائِقُ
The specific matters, and the genus (jins) placed for the universal predicated over many differing realities, and the species (naw') placed for the universal predicated over many agreeing realities in answer to 'what is it', and the example with composite things composed of several matters does not negate the possibility of some i'tibari (considered) quiddities being simple. Indeed the truth is that they are called 'i'tibari matters' not 'i'tibari quiddities'. When this preamble is set, then we say: that which the putter (wadi') conceives in order to put a name for it either has a real quiddity (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah) or not. On the first, either his conception is the very reality of that thing, or aspects and considerations from it. So the definition of the real quiddity for a named thing, from the aspect that it is a real quiddity, is a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi). It benefits the picturing of the quiddity in the mind with all of its essential properties (dhatiyyat) or some of them, or with accidental properties ('aradiyyat), or with a composite of both. And the definition of the meaning of the name and that which the putter conceived and placed the name for is a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi). It benefits the clarification of that for which the name was placed, with a more famous word like our saying 'al-ghadafar (a lion) is the lion', or with a word that includes a detailed explanation of what the name indicates in summary, like our saying 'al-asl (the root) is that upon which something else is built'. Therefore the definition of non-existent things can only be nominal, since they have no realities, but only concepts. And the definition of existent things may be nominal or real, since they have both concepts and realities.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage, from a commentary (sharh) on a matn in usul al-fiqh, explains the distinction between two types of definition: real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi). The author first sets up a preamble about quiddities (mahiyyat). He explains that what the language-putter (wadi') conceives to name either has a real quiddity (existing independently of mental consideration) or not. If it has a real quiddity, the conception may be of the essence itself or of its aspects. A real definition describes the quiddity itself, either through its essential or accidental properties, giving a mental picture. A nominal definition, on the other hand, clarifies the meaning of a name by using a more famous word or by expanding on what the name implies. For non-existent things, only a nominal definition is possible because they have no reality. For existent things, both types are possible. The Urdu commentary further explains that a real quiddity (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah) has real existence and its parts necessarily depend on each other if composite, whereas an i'tibari quiddity is merely a mental construct where the putter selects aspects without necessary interdependence. Examples include 'asl' (foundation) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence) as nominal definitions. The distinction is crucial in usul al-fiqh for understanding how terms are defined and how legal concepts are explained.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that describes the real quiddity (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah) of a thing, benefiting a mental picture of that quiddity.
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A definition that clarifies the meaning of a name (mafhum al-ism) without necessarily depicting the essence.
ماهية حقيقية (mahiyyah haqiqiyyah): A quiddity that has real existence (thubut) independent of mental consideration; its parts (if composite) necessarily depend on each other.
ماهية اعتبارية (mahiyyah i'tibariyyah): A quiddity that exists only by mental consideration (i'tibar); its parts do not necessarily depend on each other; also called 'umur i'tibariyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of definition (ta'rif) is possible for non-existent things (ma'dumat)?
A) Only real definition (ta'rif haqiqi)
B) Only nominal definition (ta'rif ismi)
C) Both real and nominal definitions
D) Neither real nor nominal definitions are possible

Key Takeaway
The key takeaway is that a real definition depicts an essence, while a nominal definition clarifies a name; legal terms in usul are often i'tibari and therefore defined nominally.

Real Definition vs Nominal Definition
Explaining that real essences can have both haqiqi and ismi definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) and a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) and explain why a real essence can be defined in both ways according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A real essence can be defined either as it exists in reality (haqiqi) or as a conceptual meaning (ismi) – the aspect determines the type.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, defining terms is a crucial step before deriving rulings. This passage clarifies that real essences (like 'triangle') are not confined to a single type of definition; they can be defined both really and nominally depending on the perspective. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion when analyzing legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definition types
Recognize that haqiqi describes the essence as it is in reality, while ismi explains the meaning as conceived by the coiner (wadi').
Both types can apply to the same thing from different aspects.
2
Understand the objection from the matn
The apparent wording of the original text suggests that real essences always have real definitions and conventional essences always have nominal definitions — implying exclusivity.
This is the prima facie understanding that the commentator addresses.
3
Analyze the two responses
The first response uses ta'wil (interpretation) to reconcile the matn; the second insists that a literal reading would contradict tahqiq (verification) because real essences have two aspects.
The second response is considered more accurate in Hanafi methodology.
4
Apply to the triangle example
The definition 'a figure enclosed by three sides' is ismi before existence is known; after confirming that such a figure exists, it becomes a haqiqi definition.
This illustrates the shift from nominal to real once existence is established.

Source Text

يُحِيطُ بِهِ ثَلاثَةُ أَضْلاعِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسْمِيٌّ وَبَعْدَ الدَّلَالَةِ عَلَى وُجُودِهِ يَصِيرُ هُوَ بِعَيْنِهِ تَعْرِيفًا حَقِيقِيًّا
ترجمہ: پس اگر تو اعتراض کرتا ہے کہ اس (ماتن) کی عبارت کا ظاہر مشعر ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف تعریف اسمی ہوتی ہے یقینی طور پر تو میں کہتا ہوں کہ ظاہر العبارة سے عدول کرنے میں وسعت ہے مگر بیشک تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بیشک ماہیات حقیقیہ بھی لی جاتی ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ اسم کے مسمی کی حقیقت ہے اور وہ ایسی ماہیت ہے جو ثابت ہے نفس الامر میں اور اس ( ماہیت حقیقیہ ) کی تعریف اس اعتبار سے تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر اس لئے کہ بیشک وہ جواب ہے اس ماہ کیلئے جو حقیقت کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے وہ مؤخر ہوتی ہے ھل بسیطہ سے جو طلب کرنے والا ہے شی متاخرہ کے وجود کیلئے اس ما سے جو اسم کی تفسیر کو طلب کرنے کے لیے اور اس کے مفہوم کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ کبھی لیا جاتا ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بیشک وہ اسم کا مفہوم ہے اور واضع کا تعقل ہے اسم کے وضع کرنے کے وقت اور اس کا تعریف کرنا اس اعتبار سے اسی ہے یقینا اس لیے کہ وہ جواب ہے اس ما کا جو اسم کے مفہوم کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے اور واضع کے تعقل کیلئے ہے اور یہ تعریف کبھی ہوتی ہے اس شی کی نفس حقیقت بایں طور کہ ہوگا واضع کا تعقل نفس حقیقت اور کبھی ہوتا ہے اس کے علاوہ سے اسی وجہ سے تصریح کی ہے انہوں نے بائیں طور کہ کبھی متحد ہوتی ہے تعریف اسمی اور تعریف حقیقی مگر بے شک وہ مٹی کے وجود کے علم سے پہلے ہمی ہوتی ہے اور وجود کے علم کے بعد تبدیل ہو جاتی ہے حقیقی سے مثال کے طور پر مثلث کی تعریف مبادی ہندسہ میں ایسی شکل کے ساتھ جس کا احاطہ کریں اضلاع ثلاث تعریف آسی ہے اور دلالت کرنے کے بعد اس کے وجود پر ہو جائے گی وہ ( تعریف آسی ) بعینہ تعریف حقیقی
ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوتی ہے اور کبھی حقیقی ہوتی ہے
فان قلت :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت کی ایک اعتراض نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- شارخ پر اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ کی کلام سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیت حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوگی اور کبھی حقیقی لیکن ماتن کی کلام سے یہ ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ حقیقی ہوگی جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ اسکی ہوتی ہے اور وجہ ظہور یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے تعریف حقیقی کو ماہیات حقیقیہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور تعریف اسمی کو ماہیات اعتباریہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف صرف امی ہی ہوتی ہے لھذا اس تقابل سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف بھی صرف حقیقی ہوگی اسمی نہیں ہوگی۔
قلت في العدول عن ظاہر العبارة سعة :- یہاں سے شاریخ نے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔
جواب :(۱) ۔ اگر چہ مصنف کی عبارت کے ظاہر سے یہی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہی ہوتی ہے لیکن تاویل کر کے ظاہر سے عدول کیا جاسکتا ہے وہ اسطرح کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں حیثیت کی قید معتبر ہے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی تعريف الماهية الحقيقية من حيث انها المساهمية الحقيقية لهذا اب تعارض ختم ہو گیا کیونکہ مصنف کی عبارت کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی تب ہوگی جب انکی ماہیات حقیقیہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے کی جائے اگر تعریف مفہومات کے اعتبار سے کی جائے تو وہ تعریف آئی ہوگی دوسری تاویل یوں کی جاسکتی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف اکثر طور پر تعریف حقیقی ہوتی ہے تقدیری عبارت ہوگی کتعریف الماہیتہ الحقیقیة من حیث الاکثر تیسری تاویل یوں بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ کتعریف الماہیات الحقیقیہ کہہ کر تعریف حقیقی کی مثال بیان کی ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف تعریف حقیقی پر بند ہے۔ جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ اگر مصنف کی عبارت کو ظاہر سے نہ ہٹایا جائے تو یہ عبارت تحقیق کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی بھی ہوگی اور تعریف اسمی بھی ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں دو اعتبار ہیں۔ (1) ماہیت حقیقیہ کا اعتبار کیا جائے۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ ماہیت حقیقیہ ہے اس اعتبار سے جو تعریف ہوگی وہ تعریف حقیقی ہوگی اور اس ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں جو سوال ہوگا وہ ماتحقیقیہ کے ذریعے ہوگا۔ (۲) ماہیت حقیقیہ میں یہ لحاظ کیا جائے یہ اسم مسمی کا مفہوم ہے واضح کا متعتقل متصور ہونے کے اعتبار سے ۔اس اعتبار سے تعریف امی ہوگی اس لئے کہ جب ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں سوال کیا ہے تو ما شارجہ کے ذریعہ سوال ہوگا جو ما حقیقیہ سے دو درجے مؤخر ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ آلات طلب مختلف ہیں لھذا ان کے جوابات بھی مختلف ہوں گے۔
روور
آلات طلب میں ترتیب
ڈائندہ :۔ آلات طلب میں ترتیب یہ ہے کہ سب سے پہلے درجہ ما شارجہ کا ہے ماشارحہ کے ذریعہ اسم کے مفہوم کے متعلق سوال ہو گا اور دوسرا درجہ مل بسیطہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعے وجودشی کو طلب کیا جاتا ہے تیسرا درجہ ما حقیقیہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعہ شی کی ماہیت اور حقیقت کا سوال ہوگا اور چونی درجہ بل مرکبہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعہ شی کی صفات کے متعلق سوال ہوگا تو ہل بسینہ ما شارجہ اور ما حقیقیہ کے درمیان میں ہے اور ما حقیقیہ بل بسیطہ اور بل مرکبہ کے درمیان میں ہے۔
It is surrounded by three sides: a nominal definition, and after indicating its existence, it becomes itself a real definition. Translation: So if you object that the apparent meaning of the author's words indicates that the definition of real essences will definitely be real, just as the definition of conventional essences is definitely nominal, then I say that there is leeway in departing from the apparent wording, but indeed the investigation is that real essences are also taken in the sense that they are the reality of the named thing and are an essence established in reality; and its definition from this aspect will definitely be a real definition, because it is the answer to the 'ma' that seeks reality, which is posterior to the simple 'hal' that seeks the existence of a contingent thing, and to the 'ma' that seeks the interpretation of the name and its meaning. Sometimes it is taken in the sense that it is the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner at the time of coining, and its definition from this aspect is nominal, because it is the answer to the 'ma' that seeks the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner. And this definition sometimes is of the essence itself in that the coiner's conception is of the essence itself, and sometimes it is from something else. Therefore they stated that sometimes the nominal definition and the real definition coincide, but indeed it is nominal before the knowledge of the existence of the essence, and after the knowledge of existence it changes to a real definition. For example, the definition of a triangle in geometry as a figure encompassed by three sides is a nominal definition, and after indicating its existence, it becomes itself a real definition. The definition of real essences is sometimes nominal and sometimes real. If you say: This is the seventh part of the commentary's text. The purpose is to transmit an objection and answer it. Objection: The objection to the commentator is that from your speech it is understood that the definition of a real essence is sometimes nominal and sometimes real, but from the author's speech it appears that the definition of real essences is always real, just as the definition of conventional essences is always nominal. The reason for this appearance is that the author mentioned the real definition in contrast to real essences, and the nominal definition in contrast to conventional essences, and the definition of conventional essences is only nominal; therefore from this contrast it is understood that the definition of real essences is also only real, not nominal. I say: There is leeway in departing from the apparent wording. From here the commentator gives two answers. Answer (1): Although the apparent meaning of the author's wording indicates that the definition of real essences is always real, it can be departed from through interpretation, such that a qualification of aspect is considered in real essences. The estimated wording would be: 'the definition of the real essence in terms of being the real essence for this'. Then the conflict is resolved because the author's meaning is also that the definition of real essences is real only when it is made in terms of their being real essences. If the definition is made in terms of meanings, then it would be nominal. A second interpretation can be that the definition of real essences is mostly real; the estimated wording would be 'the definition of real essences for the most part'. A third interpretation is that by saying 'the definition of real essences' he gave an example of a real definition; from this it does not necessitate that the definition of real essences is confined to real definition. Answer (2): This is that if the author's wording is not departed from its apparent meaning, then this wording is contrary to the investigation, because the investigation is that the definition of real essences can be both real and nominal. This is because real essences have two aspects: (1) the real essence is considered in terms of being a real essence; the definition from this aspect will be real, and the question about this real essence will be through 'ma haqiqiyyah'. (2) The real essence is considered in terms of being the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner; the definition from this aspect will be nominal, because when a question is asked about the real essence through 'ma sharhah', which is two degrees posterior to 'ma haqiqiyyah', so it is known that the tools of inquiry are different, therefore their answers will also be different. The order of the tools of inquiry: The first rank is 'ma sharhah'; through it the question is about the meaning of the name. The second rank is 'hal basitah'; through it the existence of a thing is sought. The third rank is 'ma haqiqiyyah'; through it the essence and reality of a thing are sought. The fourth rank is 'hal murakkabah'; through it the attributes of a thing are sought. So 'hal basitah' is between 'ma sharhah' and 'ma haqiqiyyah', and 'ma haqiqiyyah' is between 'hal basitah' and 'hal murakkabah'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the classification of definitions (ta'rif) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by defining the two types: ta'rif ismi (nominal definition) and ta'rif haqiqi (real definition). A nominal definition explains the meaning of a term (what the coiner intended), while a real definition describes the essence itself as it exists in reality. The core issue is whether a real essence (mahiyya haqiqiyya) can only have a real definition or also a nominal one. The objection is based on the matn (original text) which seems to contrast real definitions with real essences and nominal definitions with conventional essences, implying exclusivity. The commentator (sharh) provides two answers. The first allows interpretation (ta'wil) of the matn's wording to reconcile, suggesting qualifications or that the matn gave an example. The second answer insists that if taken literally, the matn would contradict the truth (tahqiq), because real essences indeed have two aspects: as essences in themselves (yielding real definition) and as meanings conceived by the coiner (yielding nominal definition). The passage also explains the hierarchy of interrogative tools (alat al-talab): ma sharhah (asking for interpretation of a name), hal basitah (asking for existence), ma haqiqiyyah (asking for essence/haqiqa), and hal murakkabah (asking for attributes). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul for proper conceptual analysis before deriving rulings.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that describes the essence (mahiyya) as it exists in the external reality (nafs al-amr), revealing its constitutive parts.
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A definition that explains the conceptual meaning (mafhum) of a term as intended by its coiner (wadi'), without necessarily revealing the thing's external reality.
ما حقيقية (ma haqiqiyyah): An interrogative particle used to ask about the essence and reality of a thing, corresponding to 'what is it in reality?'
ما شارجة (ma sharhah): An interrogative particle asking for the interpretation or explanation (sharh) of a name, i.e., 'what does this name mean?'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi) from a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi) of a real essence?
A) Real definition describes the essence in reality; nominal definition describes the coiner's conception.
B) Real definition is always given after nominal definition.
C) Real definition uses 'ma sharhah'; nominal definition uses 'ma haqiqiyyah'.
D) Real definition is only for conventional essences.

Key Takeaway
Real essences can be defined both really (haqiqi) and nominally (ismi) depending on whether the definition captures the essence in reality or the coiner's conceptual meaning.

Method of Learning

The Hierarchy of Interrogative Tools (Alat al-Talab)
Explaining the hierarchy of interrogative tools used to arrive at real and nominal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of interrogative tools (ma sharhah, hal basitah, ma haqiqiyyah, hal murakkabah) and state their order and purpose in Hanafi conceptual analysis.

Core Idea
The tools of inquiry in usul have a strict hierarchy: first ask the meaning (ma sharhah), then existence (hal basitah), then essence (ma haqiqiyyah), then attributes (hal murakkabah).

To properly define a term in usul al-fiqh, one must follow the correct order of questioning. This passage outlines the four alat al-talab that guide the process from simple name interpretation to full real definition. Knowing this order prevents confusion when distinguishing between nominal and real definitions.

Guided Path
1
List the four tools in order
From the passage, identify the sequence: ma sharhah, hal basitah, ma haqiqiyyah, hal murakkabah.
This order is fixed; each tool builds on the previous.
2
Understand the function of each tool
Ma sharhah asks for lexical meaning; hal basitah asks for existence; ma haqiqiyyah asks for essence; hal murakkabah asks for attributes.
Each tool answers a different type of question about the thing under study.
3
See the relationships between the tools
Hal basitah lies between ma sharhah and ma haqiqiyyah; ma haqiqiyyah lies between hal basitah and hal murakkabah. This shows that existence is confirmed before essence, and essence before attributes.
The order is logical: you must know the meaning before asking if it exists; then know the essence before asking about its attributes.
4
Connect to definitions
A nominal definition answers ma sharhah; a real definition answers ma haqiqiyyah after existence is confirmed by hal basitah.
This clarifies why the same definition can be nominal before existence and real after — the tool changes.

يُحِيطُ بِهِ ثَلاثَةُ أَضْلاعِ تَعْرِيفٌ اسْمِيٌّ وَبَعْدَ الدَّلَالَةِ عَلَى وُجُودِهِ يَصِيرُ هُوَ بِعَيْنِهِ تَعْرِيفًا حَقِيقِيًّا
ترجمہ: پس اگر تو اعتراض کرتا ہے کہ اس (ماتن) کی عبارت کا ظاہر مشعر ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف تعریف اسمی ہوتی ہے یقینی طور پر تو میں کہتا ہوں کہ ظاہر العبارة سے عدول کرنے میں وسعت ہے مگر بیشک تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بیشک ماہیات حقیقیہ بھی لی جاتی ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ اسم کے مسمی کی حقیقت ہے اور وہ ایسی ماہیت ہے جو ثابت ہے نفس الامر میں اور اس ( ماہیت حقیقیہ ) کی تعریف اس اعتبار سے تعریف حقیقی ہوگی یقینی طور پر اس لئے کہ بیشک وہ جواب ہے اس ماہ کیلئے جو حقیقت کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے وہ مؤخر ہوتی ہے ھل بسیطہ سے جو طلب کرنے والا ہے شی متاخرہ کے وجود کیلئے اس ما سے جو اسم کی تفسیر کو طلب کرنے کے لیے اور اس کے مفہوم کو بیان کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ کبھی لیا جاتا ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ بیشک وہ اسم کا مفہوم ہے اور واضع کا تعقل ہے اسم کے وضع کرنے کے وقت اور اس کا تعریف کرنا اس اعتبار سے اسی ہے یقینا اس لیے کہ وہ جواب ہے اس ما کا جو اسم کے مفہوم کو طلب کرنے کیلئے ہے اور واضع کے تعقل کیلئے ہے اور یہ تعریف کبھی ہوتی ہے اس شی کی نفس حقیقت بایں طور کہ ہوگا واضع کا تعقل نفس حقیقت اور کبھی ہوتا ہے اس کے علاوہ سے اسی وجہ سے تصریح کی ہے انہوں نے بائیں طور کہ کبھی متحد ہوتی ہے تعریف اسمی اور تعریف حقیقی مگر بے شک وہ مٹی کے وجود کے علم سے پہلے ہمی ہوتی ہے اور وجود کے علم کے بعد تبدیل ہو جاتی ہے حقیقی سے مثال کے طور پر مثلث کی تعریف مبادی ہندسہ میں ایسی شکل کے ساتھ جس کا احاطہ کریں اضلاع ثلاث تعریف آسی ہے اور دلالت کرنے کے بعد اس کے وجود پر ہو جائے گی وہ ( تعریف آسی ) بعینہ تعریف حقیقی
ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوتی ہے اور کبھی حقیقی ہوتی ہے
فان قلت :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض اس عبارت کی ایک اعتراض نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔ اعتراض:- شارخ پر اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آپ کی کلام سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیت حقیقیہ کی تعریف کبھی اسمی ہوگی اور کبھی حقیقی لیکن ماتن کی کلام سے یہ ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ حقیقی ہوگی جیسا کہ ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف ہمیشہ اسکی ہوتی ہے اور وجہ ظہور یہ ہے کہ ماتن نے تعریف حقیقی کو ماہیات حقیقیہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور تعریف اسمی کو ماہیات اعتباریہ کے مقابلے میں ذکر کیا ہے اور ماہیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف صرف امی ہی ہوتی ہے لھذا اس تقابل سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف بھی صرف حقیقی ہوگی اسمی نہیں ہوگی۔
قلت في العدول عن ظاہر العبارة سعة :- یہاں سے شاریخ نے دو جواب دیے ہیں۔
جواب :(۱) ۔ اگر چہ مصنف کی عبارت کے ظاہر سے یہی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی ہی ہوتی ہے لیکن تاویل کر کے ظاہر سے عدول کیا جاسکتا ہے وہ اسطرح کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں حیثیت کی قید معتبر ہے تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی تعريف الماهية الحقيقية من حيث انها المساهمية الحقيقية لهذا اب تعارض ختم ہو گیا کیونکہ مصنف کی عبارت کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی تب ہوگی جب انکی ماہیات حقیقیہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے کی جائے اگر تعریف مفہومات کے اعتبار سے کی جائے تو وہ تعریف آئی ہوگی دوسری تاویل یوں کی جاسکتی ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف اکثر طور پر تعریف حقیقی ہوتی ہے تقدیری عبارت ہوگی کتعریف الماہیتہ الحقیقیة من حیث الاکثر تیسری تاویل یوں بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ کتعریف الماہیات الحقیقیہ کہہ کر تعریف حقیقی کی مثال بیان کی ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف تعریف حقیقی پر بند ہے۔ جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ اگر مصنف کی عبارت کو ظاہر سے نہ ہٹایا جائے تو یہ عبارت تحقیق کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ کی تعریف حقیقی بھی ہوگی اور تعریف اسمی بھی ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ میں دو اعتبار ہیں۔ (1) ماہیت حقیقیہ کا اعتبار کیا جائے۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ یہ ماہیت حقیقیہ ہے اس اعتبار سے جو تعریف ہوگی وہ تعریف حقیقی ہوگی اور اس ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں جو سوال ہوگا وہ ماتحقیقیہ کے ذریعے ہوگا۔ (۲) ماہیت حقیقیہ میں یہ لحاظ کیا جائے یہ اسم مسمی کا مفہوم ہے واضح کا متعتقل متصور ہونے کے اعتبار سے ۔اس اعتبار سے تعریف امی ہوگی اس لئے کہ جب ماہیت حقیقیہ کے بارہ میں سوال کیا ہے تو ما شارجہ کے ذریعہ سوال ہوگا جو ما حقیقیہ سے دو درجے مؤخر ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ آلات طلب مختلف ہیں لھذا ان کے جوابات بھی مختلف ہوں گے۔
روور
آلات طلب میں ترتیب
ڈائندہ :۔ آلات طلب میں ترتیب یہ ہے کہ سب سے پہلے درجہ ما شارجہ کا ہے ماشارحہ کے ذریعہ اسم کے مفہوم کے متعلق سوال ہو گا اور دوسرا درجہ مل بسیطہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعے وجودشی کو طلب کیا جاتا ہے تیسرا درجہ ما حقیقیہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعہ شی کی ماہیت اور حقیقت کا سوال ہوگا اور چونی درجہ بل مرکبہ کا ہے اس کے ذریعہ شی کی صفات کے متعلق سوال ہوگا تو ہل بسینہ ما شارجہ اور ما حقیقیہ کے درمیان میں ہے اور ما حقیقیہ بل بسیطہ اور بل مرکبہ کے درمیان میں ہے۔
It is surrounded by three sides: a nominal definition, and after indicating its existence, it becomes itself a real definition. Translation: So if you object that the apparent meaning of the author's words indicates that the definition of real essences will definitely be real, just as the definition of conventional essences is definitely nominal, then I say that there is leeway in departing from the apparent wording, but indeed the investigation is that real essences are also taken in the sense that they are the reality of the named thing and are an essence established in reality; and its definition from this aspect will definitely be a real definition, because it is the answer to the 'ma' that seeks reality, which is posterior to the simple 'hal' that seeks the existence of a contingent thing, and to the 'ma' that seeks the interpretation of the name and its meaning. Sometimes it is taken in the sense that it is the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner at the time of coining, and its definition from this aspect is nominal, because it is the answer to the 'ma' that seeks the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner. And this definition sometimes is of the essence itself in that the coiner's conception is of the essence itself, and sometimes it is from something else. Therefore they stated that sometimes the nominal definition and the real definition coincide, but indeed it is nominal before the knowledge of the existence of the essence, and after the knowledge of existence it changes to a real definition. For example, the definition of a triangle in geometry as a figure encompassed by three sides is a nominal definition, and after indicating its existence, it becomes itself a real definition. The definition of real essences is sometimes nominal and sometimes real. If you say: This is the seventh part of the commentary's text. The purpose is to transmit an objection and answer it. Objection: The objection to the commentator is that from your speech it is understood that the definition of a real essence is sometimes nominal and sometimes real, but from the author's speech it appears that the definition of real essences is always real, just as the definition of conventional essences is always nominal. The reason for this appearance is that the author mentioned the real definition in contrast to real essences, and the nominal definition in contrast to conventional essences, and the definition of conventional essences is only nominal; therefore from this contrast it is understood that the definition of real essences is also only real, not nominal. I say: There is leeway in departing from the apparent wording. From here the commentator gives two answers. Answer (1): Although the apparent meaning of the author's wording indicates that the definition of real essences is always real, it can be departed from through interpretation, such that a qualification of aspect is considered in real essences. The estimated wording would be: 'the definition of the real essence in terms of being the real essence for this'. Then the conflict is resolved because the author's meaning is also that the definition of real essences is real only when it is made in terms of their being real essences. If the definition is made in terms of meanings, then it would be nominal. A second interpretation can be that the definition of real essences is mostly real; the estimated wording would be 'the definition of real essences for the most part'. A third interpretation is that by saying 'the definition of real essences' he gave an example of a real definition; from this it does not necessitate that the definition of real essences is confined to real definition. Answer (2): This is that if the author's wording is not departed from its apparent meaning, then this wording is contrary to the investigation, because the investigation is that the definition of real essences can be both real and nominal. This is because real essences have two aspects: (1) the real essence is considered in terms of being a real essence; the definition from this aspect will be real, and the question about this real essence will be through 'ma haqiqiyyah'. (2) The real essence is considered in terms of being the meaning of the name and the conception of the coiner; the definition from this aspect will be nominal, because when a question is asked about the real essence through 'ma sharhah', which is two degrees posterior to 'ma haqiqiyyah', so it is known that the tools of inquiry are different, therefore their answers will also be different. The order of the tools of inquiry: The first rank is 'ma sharhah'; through it the question is about the meaning of the name. The second rank is 'hal basitah'; through it the existence of a thing is sought. The third rank is 'ma haqiqiyyah'; through it the essence and reality of a thing are sought. The fourth rank is 'hal murakkabah'; through it the attributes of a thing are sought. So 'hal basitah' is between 'ma sharhah' and 'ma haqiqiyyah', and 'ma haqiqiyyah' is between 'hal basitah' and 'hal murakkabah'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the classification of definitions (ta'rif) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by defining the two types: ta'rif ismi (nominal definition) and ta'rif haqiqi (real definition). A nominal definition explains the meaning of a term (what the coiner intended), while a real definition describes the essence itself as it exists in reality. The core issue is whether a real essence (mahiyya haqiqiyya) can only have a real definition or also a nominal one. The objection is based on the matn (original text) which seems to contrast real definitions with real essences and nominal definitions with conventional essences, implying exclusivity. The commentator (sharh) provides two answers. The first allows interpretation (ta'wil) of the matn's wording to reconcile, suggesting qualifications or that the matn gave an example. The second answer insists that if taken literally, the matn would contradict the truth (tahqiq), because real essences indeed have two aspects: as essences in themselves (yielding real definition) and as meanings conceived by the coiner (yielding nominal definition). The passage also explains the hierarchy of interrogative tools (alat al-talab): ma sharhah (asking for interpretation of a name), hal basitah (asking for existence), ma haqiqiyyah (asking for essence/haqiqa), and hal murakkabah (asking for attributes). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul for proper conceptual analysis before deriving rulings.

Key Terms
ما شارجة (ma sharhah): An interrogative particle asking for the interpretation or explanation (sharh) of a name.
ھل بسیطہ (hal basitah): An interrogative particle asking about the existence of a thing, i.e., 'Is it?'
ما حقيقية (ma haqiqiyyah): An interrogative particle used to ask about the essence and reality of a thing.
ھل مرکبہ (hal murakkabah): An interrogative particle asking about the attributes or properties of a thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which tool of inquiry is used to ask about the essence (mahiyya) of a thing?
A) Ma sharhah
B) Hal basitah
C) Ma haqiqiyyah
D) Hal murakkabah

Key Takeaway
The order of interrogative tools (ma sharhah → hal basitah → ma haqiqiyyah → hal murakkabah) is essential for progressing from nominal to real definitions.

Method of Learning

Five Probable Meanings of 'Ma laha wa ma 'alayha' in Abu Hanifa's Definition
Analyzing the meanings of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' in Abu Hanifa's definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the five possible interpretations of the phrase 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' in Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh, and explain which interpretations are preponderant.

Core Idea
The phrase 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' in Abu Hanifa's definition has five distinct meanings; the preponderant one includes all legal categories.

This lesson explores the rich hermeneutics behind a single defining phrase of fiqh. The author presents three distinct interpretations (reward/punishment, permissibility/obligation, permissibility/prohibition) from which five probabilities emerge. Understanding these nuances is essential for grasping the early Hanafi conception of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three interpretations
List the three meanings of 'ma laha' and 'ma 'alayha' as explained in the passage: (1) reward and punishment, (2) permissible and obligatory, (3) permissible and forbidden.
The third interpretation is explicitly labeled as 'third meaning' in the text.
2
Derive the five probabilities
From these three interpretations, five probabilities are extracted: (1) reward and punishment, (2) punishment and no punishment, (3) reward and no reward, (4) permissibility and obligation, (5) permissibility and prohibition.
The text states: 'خلاصہ یہ نکلا کہ مالھا اور اعلیھا کی مراد میں کل پانچ احتمال ہیں' (Summary: there are five probabilities).
3
Determine the preponderant
Identifies which interpretation(s) include all twelve categories of actions. The passage says three probabilities (second, third, and fifth) are preponderant because they include all twelve categories.
The phrase 'فائل علی وجہ' indicates the preponderant one.
4
Assess implications for definition scope
Consider how each probability affects whether specific acts (e.g., haram, makruh tahrimi, tark wajib) fall under 'ma laha' or 'ma 'alayha' or are excluded.
For example, under the second interpretation, prohibited acts are excluded from the definition entirely.
