هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِكُلِ الاحْكامِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ العَمَلِيَّةِ اللَّتِي قَدْ ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا وَاللَّتِي انْعَقَدَ الْإِجْمَاعُ عَلَيْهَا مِنْ اَدِلَّتِهَا مَعَ مَلَكَةِ الْاسْتِنْبَاطِ الصَّحِيحِ مِنْهَا یہ تعریف ماتن نے کی ہے کہ فقہ ان تمام احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کو دلائل سے جانے کا نام ہے جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو چکا ہو اور ان پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہو استنباط صحیح کے ملکہ کے ساتھ ، اب تعریف میں تمام احکام سے مراد وہ احکام شرعیہ عملیہ ہیں جو قرآن و حدیث اور اجماع سے ثابت ہیں ان میں مسائل قیاسیہ داخل نہیں ہونگے اور جو احکام قرآن و حدیث اور اجماع سے حاصل ہو چکے وہ محصور اور متعین ہیں۔ اور جو یہ کہا گیا کہ تمام احکام شرعیہ عملیہ کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے اس سے مراد وہ احکام ہیں جو مجتہد کے زمانہ تک نازل ہو چکے یہی وجہ ہے کہ صحابہ کرامر بعد والے مسائل کو نہیں جانتے تھے اس کے باوجود بھی وہ فقیہ تھے اس تعریف میں ظہور کی قید لگائی اس لئے کہ اگر احکام نازل ہوئے ہوں لیکن مجتہد کو معلوم نہ ہوں تو ان کا جاننا بھی ضروری نہیں کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ وحی نازل ہوئی ہو مجتہد کو پتہ ہی نہ ہو، اور یہ قید کہ اجتماع منعقد ہو یہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے دور کے بعد والوں کے لئے ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے دور میں یہ شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس وقت اجماع تھا ہی نہیں اور نہ ہی اس کی ضرورت تھی باقی یہ قید کہ استنباط صحیح کا ملکہ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صحابی عربی تھے اور عربی دان تھے اس کے باوجود تمام وفقیہ نہیں کہا گیا بلکہ فقیہ انہیں کو کہا گیا جو استنباط احکام پر قدرت رکھتے تھے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ قید ضروری ہے مسائل قیاسیہ کے جانے کا نام فقہ نہیں ہے ور نہ دور لازم آئے گا کیونکہ مسائل قیاسیہ فقیہ کی فقاہت کا نتیجہ ہیں تو مسائل قیاسیہ فقیہ کی فقاہت پر موقوف ہوئے اگر فقیہ بننا مسائل قیاسیہ پر موقوف ہو تو اس سے توقف الشئی علی نفسہ لازم آئے گا کیونکہ فقیہ کی فقاہت موقوف ہوگی مسائل قیاسیہ کے جانے پر اور مسائل قیاسیہ کا جاننا موقوف ہوگا فقیہ کی فقاہت پر تو مسائل قیاسیہ کے واسطے سے فقیہہ موقوف ہوگی فقاہت پر تو یہ توقف الشئی علی نفسہ ہے اور یہ دور ہے اور دور باطل ہے اور جو ستلزم دور ہو وہ بھی باطل ہے تو فقہ کے لئے مسائل قیاسیہ کے جانے کا ضروری ہونا بھی باطل ہے۔
کیا فقہ پر علم کا اطلاق درست ہے
و ما قیل :۔ یہاں سے ماتن ایک اعتراض کر کے اس کے تین جواب دیتے ہیں اعتراض یہ ہے کہ فقہ ظنی چیز ہے کیونکہ اس میں اکثر مسائل قیاسیہ ہیں اور مسائل قیاسیہ ظن کا فائدہ دیتے ہیں جب اکثر مسائل ظنی ہیں تو یہ فن ظنی ہوا اور ظلیات پر علم کا اطلاق نہیں ہو سکا بلکہ قطعی اور یقینی چیز پر ہرعلم کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے تو اس کو علمہ 14 ہ نہیں کہنا چاہیئے ۔
جواب : بھائی ہماری تعریف کے مطابق فقہ قطعی ہے ہماری تعریف میں مسائل قیاسیہ داخل ہی نہیں کیونکہ ہماری تعریف میں فقہ ان احکام کے جانے کا نام ہے جو قرآن وحدیث اور اجماع سے حاصل ہیں اور یہ سب قطعی ہیں ۔ جواب (۲):- اگر ظنی مان لیں تو بھی علم کا اطلاق درست ہے کیونک خلیات پر بھی علم کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے جیسے علم الطب علم الصرف وغیرہ کیونکہ یہ لوگوں نے لکھے ہیں یہ منزل من اللہ تو نہیں ہیں جب خلیات پر علم کا اطلاق ہوسکتا ہے تو علم الفقہ کہنا بھی صحیح ہے۔ جواب (۳):۔ اگر مسائل قیاسیہ کو داخل کریں پھر بھی فقہ قطعی ہے کیونکہ جو احکام قیاس سے ثابت ہیں شریعت نے ان کا اعتبار کیا ہے چنانچہ اللہ تعالی نے حکم دیا کہ فاعتبروا یا اولی الابصار اسی طرح حضور اللہ نے حضرت معادؓ سے سوال کیا کہ اگر مسائل کا جواب قرآن وحدیث میں صراحتہ نہ پاؤ تو کیا کرو گے تو جواب میں انہوں نے کہا اجتہد برائی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دعادی اور نکیر نہ فرمائی حلقہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی تقریر سے ثابت ہوا کہ مسائل قیاسیہ معتبر ہیں اب گویا کہ شارع نے کہا كلما غلب علیه ظن المجتهد فيقبت الحكم قطعا ئیہ تقیہ ان کے نزدیک جو ہر مجتہد کو مصیب سمجھتے ہیں اپنے ظاہر پر ہے اور وہ لوگ جو ہر مجتہد کو مصیب نہیں مجھے اور حق بھی یہی ہے ان کے نزدیک یہ قضیہ درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اگر غلطی ہوتو وہ اللہ تعالی کے ہاں ثابت نہیں ہیں تو وہ مصیب کا معنی یوں کریں گے كلما غلب علیہ ظن: محمد فقد يجب اعمل عالیہ جب عمل واجب ہے تو قطعی ہوا پھر قطعی پر المجهد عمل واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا جب شریعت کے اعتبار سے قطعی ہے تو قطعیات پر علم کا اطلاق ہوسکتا ہے یا یہ لوگ یوں کہیں گے كلما غلب عليه ظن المجتهد يثبت الحکم بالنظر الى الدلیل یعنی وہ احکام جو قیاس سے ثابت ہیں وہ دلیل کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ثابت ہیں اگر چہ نفس الامر اور اللہ تعالیٰ کے ہاں ثابت نہ ہوں اور جو حکم دلیل سے ثابت ہو وہ بھی قطعی ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ فقہ میں مسائل قطعیہ کا ذکر کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے اس پر علم کا اطلاق ہو سکتا ہے (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)
تلویح
قَوْلُهُ ، ( بَلْ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ تَعْرِيفٌ مُخْتَرَعٌ لِلْفِقْهِ بِحَيْثُ تَنْضَبِطُ مَعْلُومَاتُهُ وَالتَّقْسِيدُ بِكُلّ الأحْكَامِ يَخْرُجُ بِهِ الْبَعْضُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ إِذَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِحُكْمِ أَوْ بِحُكْمَيْنِ فَالْعَالِمُ بِهِ مَعَ الْمَلَكَةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ لَا يُسَمَّى فَقِيهَا وَإِذَا عَلِمَ ثَلاثَةَ أَحْكَامٍ يُسَمَّى فَقِيهَا وَقَيَّدَ نُزُولَ الْوَحْيِ بِالظُّهُورِ احْتِرَازًا عَمَّا نَزَلَ بِهِ الْوَحْيُ وَلَمْ يَبْلُغُ بَعْدُ فَلَيْسَ مِنْ شَرْطِ الْفَقِيهِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ
Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: The definition free from objections is: 'It is knowledge of all the practical legal rulings regarding which the revelation has descended and upon which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, along with the faculty of correct derivation from them.' The author of the matn gave this definition: Fiqh is the name for knowing all these practical legal rulings from their evidences, which have become manifest from revelation and upon which consensus has been concluded, with the faculty of correct derivation. Now in the definition, 'all rulings' means those practical legal rulings that are proven by Quran, hadith, and consensus; qiyasi matters are not included in them. And those rulings that have been obtained from Quran, hadith, and consensus are limited and determined. And what is said that fiqh is the knowledge of all practical legal rulings, it means those rulings that have been revealed up to the time of the mujtahid. This is why the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not know later issues, yet they were jurists. In this definition, the restriction of 'manifestation' is placed so that if rulings have been revealed but the mujtahid is not aware of them, knowing them is not necessary, because it is possible that revelation came and the mujtahid did not know of it. And the restriction that consensus is concluded is for those after the Prophet's era; in the Prophet's era this condition is not required because there was no consensus then and it was not needed. As for the restriction of having the faculty of correct derivation, its proof is that the Companion was an Arab and knew Arabic, yet not all of them were called jurists; rather, only those who had the ability to derive rulings were called jurists. Thus, this restriction is necessary. Knowing qiyasi matters is not the same as fiqh, otherwise circularity would arise: qiyasi matters are the result of the jurist's juristic ability, so if being a jurist depends on knowing qiyasi matters, and knowing qiyasi matters depends on being a jurist, that would be a circularity, and circularity is false. So it is also false that fiqh necessarily includes knowing qiyasi matters. Is it correct to apply 'ilm to fiqh? 'And what was said': From here the author of the matn raises an objection and gives three answers. The objection is that fiqh is a speculative thing because most of its matters are qiyasi, and qiyasi matters yield speculation. Since most matters are speculative, this discipline is speculative, and the term 'ilm is not applied to speculative matters; rather it is applied only to certain and definite matters. So it should not be called 'ilm. Answer (1): According to our definition, fiqh is certain; qiyasi matters are not included in our definition, because in our definition fiqh is the knowledge of those rulings obtained from Quran, hadith, and consensus, and all of these are certain. Answer (2): Even if we consider it speculative, the application of 'ilm is valid, because 'ilm is also applied to speculative matters, such as medicine, grammar, etc., since they are written by people and are not revealed. When 'ilm can be applied to speculative matters, calling it 'ilm al-fiqh is also correct. Answer (3): Even if we include qiyasi matters, fiqh is still certain, because rulings proven by analogy have been given weight by the Shari'ah. For example, Allah commanded: 'Then take heed, O people of insight' (Quran 59:2). Similarly, the Prophet asked Mu'adh what he would do if he didn't find an answer in Quran and hadith; Mu'adh said he would exercise ijtihad, and the Prophet did not disapprove but said praise. From this approval, it is established that qiyasi matters are valid. Now it is as if the Lawgiver said: 'Whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion prevails upon, the ruling is established definitively.' For those who believe that every mujtahid is correct, this is apparent. For those who do not believe that every mujtahid is correct (and that is the correct view), this statement is not valid, because if he errs, the ruling is not established in the sight of Allah. So they interpret 'whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion prevails upon, the ruling is established' to mean that action upon it becomes obligatory. When action is obligatory, the ruling is certain for the mujtahid, so it is certain by the Shari'ah's consideration. Or they say: 'whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion prevails upon, the ruling is established with respect to the evidence' – meaning that the rulings proven by analogy are established in terms of the evidence, even if they are not established in actual reality (nafs al-amr) before Allah. And a ruling proven by evidence is also certain. In summary, fiqh mentions certain matters, so 'ilm can be applied to it. (And Allah knows best what is correct.) Talwih: 'His statement: 'Rather it is knowledge' is an invented definition for fiqh such that its known matters are controlled. The restriction to 'all rulings' excludes the partial. However, it indicates that when revelation has appeared with one or two rulings, the scholar who knows them with the mentioned faculty is not called a faqih, but when he knows three rulings he is called a faqih. And he restricted the descent of revelation to 'appearance' to exclude what has descended but has not yet reached (the scholar), so it is not a condition for the faqih to know it.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a dispute over the definition of fiqh and whether it qualifies as 'ilm (knowledge). The commentary first presents the author's definition: fiqh is knowledge of all practical legal rulings that have been revealed and upon which there is consensus, combined with the faculty of correct derivation. This definition deliberately excludes qiyasi (analogical) rulings to avoid circularity: if fiqh required knowledge of analogical rulings, and analogical rulings are known through fiqh, a vicious circle would result. The proof that the faculty of correct derivation is necessary is that not all Arabs, even though they knew Arabic, were called jurists; only those capable of deriving rulings were.

Then an objection is raised: fiqh cannot be called 'ilm because it is primarily speculative (zanni) due to its reliance on analogy. The author gives three responses: (1) According to this definition, qiyas is excluded, so fiqh deals only with certain knowledge from Quran, hadith, and ijma. (2) Even if it were speculative, the term 'ilm is used for speculative fields like medicine and grammar. (3) Even if qiyasi matters are included, they are effectively certain because the Shari'ah has validated them through the Quranic verse 'فاعْتَبِرُوا' and the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's use of ijtihad. The Lawgiver's validation makes the mujtahid's predominant opinion decisive in practice, thus it becomes certain in terms of evidence. The final Talwih super-commentary clarifies that the definition is an invented one to delimit fiqh's scope, and that a person must know at least three such rulings to be called a faqih; the condition of 'appearance' ensures that rulings not yet transmitted to the scholar are not required.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of all practical legal rulings that have been revealed and upon which consensus has been reached, along with the faculty of correct derivation
العلم (al-ilm): In this passage, 'ilm is applied both to certain (qat'i) knowledge and to speculative (zanni) knowledge as used in other disciplines
الظن (al-zann): Preponderant opinion that is not certain; rulings from qiyas are zanni in themselves but become effectively certain due to Shari'ah validation
القطع (al-qat'): Certain knowledge; the definition restricts fiqh to qat'i matters from Quran, hadith, and ijma
الاستنباط (al-istinbat): The faculty of correctly deriving rulings from their evidences
الملكة (al-malaka): A firmly established faculty or ability that enables correct derivation
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars after the Prophet's era; a source of qat'i rulings
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; excluded from the narrow definition of fiqh to avoid circularity, but acknowledged as valid by Shari'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the responses given to the objection that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm?
A) Fiqh by definition excludes qiyas, so it is certain.
B) 'Ilm is applied to speculative fields like medicine.
C) The Shari'ah validates qiyas, making it effectively certain.
D) The faculty of istinbat is not necessary for fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh, in the Hanafi usul, is a certain knowledge either by narrow definition or by Shari'ah validation of its sources, thus it is properly called 'ilm.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
Critique of the Definition of Fiqh and the Role of Qiyas
Commentary critiquing a definition of fiqh and its implications for analogical issues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critique the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of what has been revealed' and explain why knowledge of analogical rulings cannot be a condition for being a faqih, using the argument of circularity (dawr) and the principle that qiyas is a muzhir (revealer), not a muthbit (establisher).

Core Idea
Analogical rulings are the fruit of faghanah, not its root; requiring them creates a vicious circle.

This passage is a commentary that critically examines a definition of fiqh. It argues that fiqh cannot be defined merely as knowledge of revealed rulings because that would exclude analogical issues, which form the bulk of fiqh. The commentator uses the concept of circularity (dawr) to show that analogical issues are a product of ijtihad, not a prerequisite. The discussion also addresses objections regarding later mujtahids and the nature of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
The passage critiques the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of what has been revealed' (al-ilm bima zahara nuzul al-wahi bihi). Note the key elements: 'manifestation of revelation' and the role of consensus.
The definition is seen as problematic because it excludes analogical rulings.
2
Understand the circularity (dawr) argument
The commentator argues that if knowledge of analogical issues (masa'il qiyasiyya) were a condition for being a faqih, then one would need to already be a faqih to know them, since they are derived by ijtihad. This creates a vicious circle.
Circularity (dawr) is a key logical argument in usul al-fiqh to reject impossible conditions.
3
Examine the objection and response about mujtahid generations
An objector says circularity only applies to the first mujtahid; later mujtahids could simply learn the analogical rulings from earlier ones. The response: a mujtahid cannot do taqlid; he must derive them himself, so circularity persists for every mujtahid.
However, a mujtahid must know the opinions of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus.
4
Analyze the four investigations (abhath)
The first investigation argues that the definition makes fiqh a universal concept that changes over time, which is unusual. The second: it does not apply to the Companions before consensus. The third: it excludes most analogical rulings. The fourth: the condition of 'manifestation' is ambiguous or unworkable.
These points collectively show the definition's inadequacy.
5
Summarize the overall assessment
The passage concludes that this definition is not free from difficulty and disorder. It fails to capture the dynamic and ijtihad-dependent nature of fiqh.
The Hanafi definition of fiqh emphasizes the faculty (malakah) of istinbat, which this critique supports.

پیدا نہ ہو۔ قَوْلُهُ ) لَا الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ ) أَى لَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِي الْفِقْهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِل الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ ؛ لأنَّهَا نَتِيجَةُ الْفَقَاهَةِ وَالاجْتِهَادِ لِكَوْنِهَا فُرُوعًا مُسْتَتْبَطَةٌ بِالِاجْتِهَادِ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا عَلَى كَوْنِ الشَّخْصِ فَقِيهَا فَلَوْ تَوَقَّفَتِ الْفَقَاهَةُ عَلَيْهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوُرُ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ هَذَا إِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ فِى أَوَّلِ الْقَائِسِينَ . وَأَمَّا مَنْ بَعْدَهُ فَيَجُوزُ أَن يُشْتَرَطَ فِيهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ الَّتِي اسْتَنْبَطَهَا الْمُجْتَهِدُ الْأَوَّلُ مِنْ غَيْرِ لُزُومِ دَوْرٍ قُلْنَا لَا يَجُوزُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ التَّقْلِيدُ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ الْمَسَائِلَ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ بِاجْتِهَادِهِ فَلَوْ اُشْتَرَطَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوْرُ نَعَمُ يُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ أَقْوَالَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فِي الْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ لِئَلَّا يَقَعَ فِى مُخَالَفَةِ الْإِجْمَاعِ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ مِمَّا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحى بها ، إذ القِيَاسُ مُظْهِرُ لَا مُثْبِتْ فَيُشْتَرَطُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ الْأَخِيرِ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا قُلْنَا نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا إِنَّمَا ظَهَرَ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ السَّابِقِ لَا فِي الْوَاقِعِ وَلَا عِنْدَ الْمُجْتَهِدِ الثَّانِي وَلَيْسَ لَهُ تَقْلِيدُ الْأَوَّلِ فَلا يُشْتَرَطُ لَهُ مَعْرِفَتُهُ وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ لَا بِتُوَسُطِ الْقِيَاسِ ، ثُمَّ هَهُنَا أَبْحَاتُ الْأَوَّلُ أَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ تَعْرِيفُ الْفِقْهِ الْمُصْطَلَحٍ بَيْنَ الْقَوْمِ ، وَهُوَ عِنْدَهُمُ اسْمٌ لِعِلْمٍ مَخْصُوصِ مُعَيَّنٍ كَسَائِرِ الْعُلُومِ وَعَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ هُوَ اسْمٌ لِمَفْهُومٍ كُلِّى يَتَبَدَّلُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَيَّامِ وَالْأَعْصَارِ فَيَوْمًا يَكُونُ عِلْمًا بِجُمْلَةٍ مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ وَيَوْمًا بِأَكْثَرَ وَأَكْثَرَ وَهَكَذَا يَتَزَايَدُ إِلَى انُقِرَاضِ زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ، ثُمَّ أَخَذَ يَتَزَايَدُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَعْصَارِ وَانْعِقَادِ الْإِجْمَاعَاتِ وَأَيْضًا يَنتَقِصُ بِحَسَبِ النَّوَاسِخِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَى خِلَافِ أَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى فِقْهِ الصَّحَابَةِ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِعَدَمِ الْإِجْمَاعِ فِى زَمَانِهِ وَكَأَنَّهُ أَرَادَ أَنَّهُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ فَقَطْ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنُ إِجْمَاعٌ وَبِهِ وَبِمَا انْعَقَدَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِجْمَاعُ إِنْ كَانَ وَمِثْلُهُ فِي التَّعْرِيفَاتِ بَعِيدٌ الثَّالِثُ أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْعِلْمُ بِالأحْكَامِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ خَارِجًا عَنْ الْفِقْهِ ، وَذَلِكَ عِندَهُمْ مُعَظَّمُ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ اللَّهُمَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَالَ إِنَّهُ فِقْةٌ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى مَنْ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ اجَتِهَادُهُ ، إِذْ قَدْ ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهِ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَكُونُ الْفِقْهُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى كُلِّ مُجْتَهِد شَيْئًا آخَرَ . الرَّابِعُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ أُرِيدَ بِظُهُورِ نُزُولِ الْوَحْيِ الطُّهُورُ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ فَكَثِيرٌ مِنْ فُقَهَاءِ الصَّحَابَةِ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا كَثِيرًا مِنْ الْأحْكَامِ الَّتِى ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ الصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا رَجَعُوا فِى كَثِيرٍ مِنْ الْوَقَائِعِ إِلَى عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهَا وَلَمْ يَقْدَحُ ذَلِكَ فِي فَقَاهَتِهِمْ ، وَإِنْ أُرِيدَ الطُّهُورُ عَلَى الْأَعَمِّ الْأَغْلَبِ فَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَضْبُوطٍ لِكَثْرَةِ الرُّوَاةِ وَتَفَرُّقِهِمْ فِي الْأَسْفَارِ وَالْأَشْغَالِ وَلَوْ سُلَّمَ فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْحُكْمِ الَّذِى يَرُوِيهِ الْآحَادُ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ حَتَّى يَصِيرَ شَائِعًا ظَاهِرًا عَلَى الْأَكْثَرِ فَيَصِيرُ فِقَهَا وَبِالْجُمُلَةِ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفُ لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ الْإِشْكَالِ وَالِاخْتِلَالَ ترجمہ :۔ یعنی شرط نہیں ہے فقہ میں مسائل قیاسیہ جاننے کی اس لئے کہ یہ فقاہت اور اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہیں بوجہ ہونے ان کے اجتہاد سے مستنبط شدہ فروع کے پس ان کا علم موقوف ہوگا اس شخص کے فقیہ ہونے پر پس اگر فقاہت موقوف ہو ان مسائل کے جانے پر تو دور لازم آئے گا ، پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ یہ اعتراض سوائے اس کے نہیں درست ہوگا قیاس کرنے والوں میں سے پہلے شخص کے بارے میں اور وہ لوگ جو اس کے بعد میں آئے پس جائز ہے شرط لگانا اس میں ان مسائل قیاسیہ کے جاننے کی جن کو مجتہد اول نے قیاس کیا ہے بغیر دور کے لازم آنے کے تو ہم جواب میں کہیں گے جائز نہیں ہے مجتہد کے لئے تقلید کرنا بلکہ اس پر واجب ہے کہ وہ مسائل قیاسیہ کو جانے اپنے اجتہاد کے ذریعے پس اگر شرط قرار دیا جائے ان مسائل قیاسیہ کے جانے ) کو تو دور لازم آئے گا۔ ہاں شرط ہے یہ کہ وہ ( مجتہد ) جانے تمام مجتہدین کے اقوال کو مسائل قیاسینہ میں تا کہ اجتماع مرکب کی مخالفت میں واقع نہ ہو جائے۔ پس اگر یہ سوال کیا جائے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ ان احکام میں سے ہیں جن کا ظہو، نزول
Even knowledge: This is the second part of the statement, in which the commentator has explained the benefit of the condition 'with malakah' (faculty), that if someone knows a ruling merely through linguistic ability, he will not be called a faqih until he develops the malakah of istinbat and aptitude. His statement: 'Not the analogical issues' means that knowledge of analogical issues is not a condition in fiqh, because they are the result of faghanah (jurisprudential skill) and ijtihad, as they are branches derived by ijtihad. So knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih. If faghanah were dependent on them, circularity would arise. If it is said: This is only valid for the first of those who perform qiyas. As for those after him, it is permissible to condition knowledge of the analogical issues extracted by the first mujtahid without circularity. We say: A mujtahid is not allowed to perform taqlid; rather, he must know the analogical issues through his own ijtihad. If knowledge of them were a condition, circularity would arise. Yes, it is a condition that he knows the statements of the mujtahids concerning the analogical issues so as not to fall into violation of ijma. If it is said: The analogical issues are among those whose revelation has become manifest, because qiyas is a revealer, not an establisher, so knowledge of them is a condition for the later mujtahid. We say: That revelation of them is manifest only for the earlier mujtahid, not in reality, nor in the view of the later mujtahid, and he is not allowed to follow the earlier, so knowledge of them is not a condition for him. It is possible that what is meant is 'what revelation has been revealed with' without intermediation of qiyas. Then here are investigations: The first: The intended meaning is the definition of fiqh as a term among the people. According to them, it is the name of a specific, particular science like other sciences. According to what the author mentioned, it is a name for a universal concept that changes according to days and eras. One day it is knowledge of a set of rulings, another day it is knowledge of more, and so on it increases until the end of the Prophet's time. Then it continued to increase according to eras and the formation of ijmas, and also decreases according to abrogations and consensus contrary to ahad reports. The second: The definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions in the time of the Prophet, due to the absence of ijma in his time. It is as if he meant that it is knowledge of what revelation has been revealed with only, if there is no ijma, and together with what ijma has been formed upon, if it exists. Such a definition is far-fetched. The third: It would require that knowledge of analogical rulings be outside fiqh, whereas according to them the majority of fiqh issues are analogical. Except if it is said that it is fiqh relative to the one whose ijtihad leads to it, since revelation has become manifest to him. Then fiqh would be something different for each mujtahid. The fourth: If by 'manifestation of revelation' is meant absolute manifestation, many of the jurists among the Companions did not know many rulings whose revelation was manifest to some Companions, as they referred in many incidents to Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), and that did not detract from their faghanah. If it is meant manifestation in the most common way, it is not delimited due to the large number of narrators and their dispersal in travels and occupations. Even if that is granted, then knowledge of a ruling reported by ahad would not be considered fiqh until it becomes widespread and manifest to the majority, then it becomes fiqh. In summary, this definition is not free from difficulty and disorder. Translation: i.e., knowledge of analogical issues is not a condition in fiqh, because they are the result of faghanah and ijtihad, due to being branches derived by ijtihad. So their knowledge depends on the person being a faqih. If faghanah were dependent on knowing them, circularity would arise. If an objection is made that this objection is valid only for the first of those who perform qiyas, and those who come after, it is permissible to condition knowledge of those analogical issues that the first mujtahid extracted without circularity, then we reply: A mujtahid is not allowed to perform taqlid; rather, it is obligatory upon him to know the analogical issues through his own ijtihad. If knowledge of them is made a condition, circularity would arise. Yes, it is a condition that he knows the statements of all mujtahids concerning the analogical issues so that he does not fall into violation of composite consensus. If this question is asked: The analogical issues are among those whose revelation has manifest...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of fiqh. It begins by explaining the benefit of the condition 'with malakah' (faculty) in the definition of a faqih. The commentator states that mere knowledge of rulings without the ability to derive is insufficient. The discussion then moves to the exclusion of analogical issues (masa'il qiyasiyya) from being a condition in fiqh. The reason given is that analogical issues are the result of faghanah and ijtihad, so requiring them would cause circularity (dawr): one would need to already be a faqih to know them, but being a faqih would require knowing them. A potential objection is raised: this circularity only applies to the first mujtahid, not later ones. The response is that a mujtahid cannot imitate others; he must derive analogical rulings himself, so circularity persists. However, he must know the opinions of earlier mujtahids to avoid violating consensus. Another objection states that analogical rulings are based on revelation (qiyas only reveals what is already revealed), so later mujtahids must know them. The response: revelation of these rulings was only apparent to the earlier mujtahid, and the later one cannot simply follow him, so knowledge is not required. The passage concludes with four investigations (abhath) pointing out problems with the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of what has been revealed': (1) it makes fiqh a changing concept; (2) it does not apply to Companions' fiqh before consensus; (3) it would exclude most analogical rulings; (4) the condition of 'manifestation' is ambiguous or unworkable. The overall assessment is that the definition is problematic.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): Knowledge of specific shar'i rulings derived from detailed evidence, which changes over time and eras.
مسائل قياسية (masa'il qiyasiyya): Rulings derived through analogical reasoning (qiyas), which are branches of ijtihad.
دور (dawr): Logical circularity where a condition and its consequence depend on each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is knowledge of analogical issues (masa'il qiyasiyya) not required as a condition for fiqh?
A) Because they are too numerous to know.
B) Because they are the result of faghanah and ijtihad, so requiring them would cause circularity.
C) Because they are not considered part of fiqh.
D) Because they can only be known through taqlid.

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh as knowledge of what has been revealed is inadequate because it excludes analogical rulings and involves circularity; a true faqih is one with the faculty of istinbat.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Definition of Usul al-Fiqh as a Discipline
Commentary defining usul al-fiqh as a discipline with logical precision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh, identify its key components (universal principles, close means, verification), and distinguish it from preliminary sciences and ilm al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of universal principles that lead to fiqh rulings through verification, not mere debate.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the technical definition of usul al-fiqh as a distinct discipline. You will see how each phrase in the definition serves to exclude related fields — from grammar to dialectics — and how universal propositions function as the logical core of legal derivation. Pay close attention to the contrast with 'ilm al-khilaf, as this is a frequent point of confusion.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the exact Arabic sentence defining usul al-fiqh as a science: 'wa 'ilmu uṣūli al-fiqhi al-'ilmu bi al-qawā'idi allatī yutawassalu bihā ilayhi 'alā wajhi al-taḥqīqi.'
This definition treats usul al-fiqh as a proper noun for a specific discipline.
2
Parse the definition components
Break down the definition: 'al-qawā'id' are universal propositions (qadaya kulliyyah); 'yutawassalu bihā ilayhi' indicates a close means (tawassul qarīb); 'alā wajh al-taḥqīq' specifies verification as the method.
Each component restricts the scope of usul al-fiqh.
3
Identify what is excluded
The phrase 'close means' excludes preliminary sciences like Arabic grammar (nahw) and theology (kalam). The phrase 'verification' excludes the science of disputation (ilm al-khilaf) and dialectics (jadal), whose goal is to compel an opponent, not to reach truth.
This is the key distinction that many students overlook.
4
Understand the logical structure
The universal propositions serve as the major premise in a first-figure syllogism or as universal correlations (mulāzamāt). The example given: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established. This ruling is indicated by qiyas, therefore it is established.'
This shows how usul principles are applied to derive fiqh rulings.
5
Grasp the subsumption idea
The commentator notes that a universal proposition may not be explicitly stated in usul al-fiqh texts but is subsumed under a broader principle. This allows flexibility in applying the discipline.
This is an advanced nuance: principles are not always verbatim but are implied.

وَلَمَّا عَرَّف أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْإِضَافَةِ فَالآنَ يُعَرِّفُهُ بِاعْتِبَارٍ أَنَّهُ لَقَبْ لِعِلْمٍ مَخْصُوص فَيَقُولُ ) وَعِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَيْهِ عَلَى وَجُهِ التَّحْقِيقِ ) أَى الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةِ الَّتِى يُتَوَكَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ تَوَصُّلًا قَرِيبًا وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا تَوَصَّلَا قَرِيبًا احْتِرَازًا عَنْ الْمَبَادِئِي كَالْعَرَبِيَّةِ وَالْكَلَامِ وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا عَلَى وَجهِ التَّحْقِيقِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْخِلافِ وَالْجَدَلِ فَإِنَّهُ وَإِنْ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْقَوَاعِدِ الْمُوْصِلَةِ إلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ لَكِنْ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّحْقِيقِ ، بَلْ الْغَرَضُ مِنْهُ الْزَامُ الْخَصْمِ وَذَلِكَ كَقَوَاعِدِهِمُ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْإِرْشَادِ وَالْمُقَدَّمَةِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا لِتُبْتَنَى عَلَيْهَا التِّكَتُ الْخِلَافِيَّةُ ) وَنَعْنِي بِالْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ مَا يَكُونُ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَى الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ ) أَى إِذَا اسْتَدْلَلْتَ عَلَى حُكم مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالشَّكْلِ الأَوَّلِ فَكُبُرَى الشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ هِيَ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةُ كَقَوْلِنَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ حُكُمْ يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ وَكُلُّ حُكُم يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ وَإِذَا اسْتَدْلَلْتَ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالْمُلَازَمَاتِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ مَعَ وُجُودِ المَلْزُومِ فَالْمُلَازَمَاتُ الْكُلِّيَّةُ هِيَ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا كَقَوْلِنَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ كُلَّمَا دَلْ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى ثُبوتِ هَذَا الْحُكُم يَكُونُ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتا لَكِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ دَلْ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ فَيَكُونُ ثَابِتا وَاعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ هَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةُ الكُلِّيَّةُ بِعَيْنِهَا مَذْكُورَةٌ فِى مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ لَكِنْ تَكُونُ مُنْدَرِجَةً فِي قَضِيَّةٍ كُلِّيَّةٍ
And when he defined usul al-fiqh with consideration of the addition, now he defines it with consideration that it is a name for a specific science, and says: 'The knowledge of usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at it (fiqh) in a verified manner.' That is, knowledge of the universal propositions by which one reaches fiqh through a close means. And we said 'close means' to exclude preliminaries like Arabic grammar and theology. And we said 'in a verified manner' to exclude the science of disputation and dialectics, for even though it includes principles that lead to fiqh issues, it does not do so in a verified manner; rather its purpose is to compel the opponent. That is like their principles mentioned in Al-Irshad and Al-Muqaddimah and similar works, on which the disputational points are based. And by 'the universal propositions mentioned' we mean that which is one of the two premises of the proof for fiqh issues. That is, when you prove a ruling of fiqh issues by the first figure, then the major premise of the first figure is those universal propositions, like our statement: 'This ruling is established because it is a ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment, and every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established.' And when you prove fiqh issues by universal correlations (mulazamat kulliyyah) with the existence of the correlative (malzum), then the universal correlations are those propositions, like our statement: 'This ruling is established because whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, this ruling is established, but qiyas does indicate the establishment of this ruling, so it is established.' And know that it is possible that this universal proposition itself is not mentioned in the issues of usul al-fiqh, but it is subsumed under a universal proposition.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh as a distinct discipline. The author first notes that the previous definition considered usul al-fiqh as an 'idafah' (construct phrase), but now he defines it as a proper name for a specific science. The definition given is: 'The knowledge of the principles by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner.' The commentary then unpacks each part: 'the principles' means universal propositions (qadaya kulliyyah) that serve as a direct means to fiqh, not indirect like grammar or theology. 'In a verified manner' (ala wajh al-tahqiq) excludes the science of disputation (ilm al-khilaf) and dialectics (jadal), whose aim is not to discover truth but to compel an opponent. The universal propositions are further explained as the major premise in a first-figure syllogism used to prove fiqh rulings, or as universal correlations. Finally, the author notes that these universal propositions may not be explicitly stated in usul al-fiqh works but are implied under broader principles.

Key Terms
القَضَايَا الكُلِّيَّة (al-qadaya al-kulliyyah): Universal propositions that serve as the major premise in a syllogism for proving fiqh rulings.
التَّحْقِيق (al-tahqiq): Verification; the method of deriving rulings with certainty or strong likelihood, as opposed to mere dialectical persuasion.
عِلْم الخلاف (ilm al-khilaf): The science of disputation that aims to refute opponents rather than to establish rulings with verification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The science of Arabic grammar and theology.
B) The science of disputation and dialectics.
C) The use of Qiyas as a proof.
D) The acquisition of knowledge from the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the discipline of verified universal principles that directly lead to fiqh rulings, distinct from preliminary sciences and mere dialectics.

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh as a Science: Its Scope and Purpose
Defining the science of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of usul al-fiqh as a science and distinguish it from related disciplines like Arabic grammar and jadal.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is knowledge of universal rules for deriving fiqh thoroughly—not for mere dispute.

In this passage, the commentator builds on an earlier definition of usul al-fiqh as a genitive construction and now defines it as a specific science. He carefully delimits its scope: it is knowledge of universal propositions that serve as immediate premises for fiqh, excluding foundational tools like Arabic and polemical sciences like disputation. This refined definition highlights the epistemic seriousness of usul al-fiqh as a truth-seeking discipline.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
The passage states: 'And the science of usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at it (fiqh) on a thorough basis.' Identify each key term: rules (qawa'id), arrives at (tawassul), thorough basis (tahqiq).
The definition is given after a contrast with the genitive definition.
2
Exclude foundational sciences
The phrase 'proximate means' excludes Arabic grammar and theology, which are distant means. These are prerequisites but not part of usul itself.
The commentator emphasizes 'proximate' to keep the scope tight.
3
Exclude disputation sciences
The phrase 'on a thorough basis' excludes khilaf and jadal, which aim to compel opponents rather than establish truth.
This distinguishes usul from mere dialectics.
4
Identify universal propositions as major premises
The 'rules' are universal propositions that serve as the major premise in syllogisms (first figure) or as universal implications. Example: 'Every ruling that analogy indicates is established.'
This shows usul's role in structuring arguments.
5
Understand subsumption of particular propositions
A specific universal proposition (e.g., 'whenever analogy indicates obligation, obligation is established') falls under a more general one ('whenever analogy indicates any ruling, it is established').
This explains how usul principles are hierarchical.

وَلَمَّا عَرَّف أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْإِضَافَةِ فَالآنَ يُعَرِّفُهُ بِاعْتِبَارٍ أَنَّهُ لَقَبْ لِعِلْمٍ مَخْصُوص فَيَقُولُ ) وَعِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَيْهِ عَلَى وَجُهِ التَّحْقِيقِ ) أَى الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةِ الَّتِى يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ تَوَصُّلًا قَرِيبًا وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا تَوَصُّلًا قَرِيبًا احْتِرَازًا عَنْ الْمَبَادِئِ كَالْعَرَبِيَّةِ وَالْكَلَامِ وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّحْقِيقِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْخِلافِ وَالْجَدَلِ فَإِنَّهُ وَإِنْ اشْتَمَلَ عَلَى الْقَوَاعِدِ الْمُوْصِلَةِ إلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ لَكِنْ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّحْقِيقِ ، بَلْ الْغَرَضُ مِنْهُ إلْزَامُ الْخَصْمِ وَذَلِكَ كَقَوَاعِدِهِمُ الْمَذْكُورَةِ فِي الْإِرْشَادِ وَالْمُقَدَّمَةِ وَنَحْوِهِمَا لِتُبْتَنَى عَلَيْهَا النُّكَت الْخِلَافِيَّةُ ) وَنَعْنِي بِالْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ مَا يَكُونُ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَى الدَّلِيلِ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ ) أَى إِذَا اسْتَدْلَلْتَ عَلَى حُكم مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالشَّكْلِ الأَوَّلِ فَكُبُرَى الشَّكْلِ الْأَوَّلِ هِيَ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةُ كَقَوْلِنَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ ; لِأَنَّهُ حُكْمٌ يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ وَكُلُّ حُكْمٍ يَدُلُّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِهِ الْقِيَاسُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ وَإِذَا اسْتَدْلَلْتَ عَلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ بِالْمُلَازَمَاتِ الْكُلِّيَّةِ مَعَ وُجُودِ الْمَلْزُومِ فَالْمُلَازَمَاتُ الْكُلِّيَّةُ هِيَ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا كَقَوْلِنَا هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتٌ ; لِأَنَّهُ كُلَّمَا دَلَّ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ يَكُونُ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ ثَابِتاً لَكِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ دَلَّ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ هَذَا الْحُكْمِ فَيَكُونُ ثَابِتاً وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ هَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةُ الْكُلِّيَّةُ بِعَيْنِهَا مَذْكُورَةً فِي مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ لَكِنْ تَكُونُ مُنْدَرِجَةً فِي قَضِيَّةٍ كُلِّيَّةٍ هِيَ مَذْكُورَةٌ فِي مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ كَقَوْلِنَا كُلَّمَا دَلَّ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى الْوُجُوبِ فِي صُورَةِ النِّزَاعِ يَثْبُتُ الْوُجُوبُ فِيهَا فَإِنَّ هَذِهِ الْمُلَازَمَةَ مُنْدَرِجَةٌ تَحْتَ هَذِهِ الْمُلَازَمَةِ وَهِيَ كُلَّمَا دَلَّ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى ثُبُوتِ كُلِّ حُكْمٍ هَذَا شَأْنُهُ يَثْبُتُ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ وَ الْوُجُوبُ مِنْ جُزْئِيَّاتِ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ فَكَأَنَّهُ قِيلَ كُلَّمَا دَلَّ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى الْوُجُوب يَثْبُت الْوُجُوبُ وَكُلَّمَا دَلَّ الْقِيَاسُ عَلَى الْجَوَاز يَثْبُتُ الْجَوَازُ فَالْمُلَازَمَةُ الَّتِي هِيَ إِحْدَى مُقَدِّمَتَى الدَّلِيلِ تَكُونُ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ بِطَرِيقِ التَّضَمُّنِ
And when he defined usul al-fiqh by way of addition, now he defines it by way of it being a title for a specific science. So he says: 'And the science of usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at it (fiqh) on a thorough basis.' That is, knowledge of the universal propositions by which one arrives at fiqh as a proximate means. We only said 'proximate means' to exclude the foundational sciences like Arabic grammar and theology. And we only said 'on a thorough basis' to exclude the science of disputation and argumentation, for even though it includes rules that lead to fiqh issues, it is not on a thorough basis; rather its purpose is to compel the opponent — like their rules mentioned in al-Irshad, al-Muqaddima, and similar works upon which disputation points are built. And by 'universal propositions' we mean what is one of the two premises of the proof for fiqh issues. That is, when you infer a ruling of fiqh issues by the first figure, the major premise of the first figure is those universal propositions, as in our statement: 'This ruling is established because analogy indicates its establishment, and every ruling that analogy indicates its establishment is established.' And when you infer fiqh issues by universal implications with the existence of the implied, the universal implications are those propositions, as in our statement: 'This ruling is established because whenever analogy indicates the establishment of this ruling, this ruling is established, but analogy indicates the establishment of this ruling, so it is established.' And know that it is possible that this particular universal proposition is not explicitly mentioned in the issues of usul al-fiqh, but it falls under a universal proposition that is mentioned in the issues of usul al-fiqh, as in our statement: 'Whenever analogy indicates obligation in a disputed case, obligation is established therein.' For this implication falls under the implication: 'Whenever analogy indicates the establishment of any ruling with this status, this ruling is established.' And obligation is one of the particulars of that ruling. So it is as if it was said: 'Whenever analogy indicates obligation, obligation is established; and whenever analogy indicates permissibility, permissibility is established.' So the implication, which is one of the two premises of the proof, is part of the issues of usul al-fiqh by way of inclusion.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the science of usul al-fiqh by the commentator. It begins by noting that the author previously defined usul al-fiqh as an 'idafa' (genitive construction), and now provides a definition as a proper science. The definition: 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh on a thorough basis' (al-qawa'id allati yutawassalu biha ilayhi 'ala wajh al-tahqiq). The commentator unpacks this: 'rules' are universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya); 'arrives at' means as a proximate means (tawassulan qariban), excluding foundational sciences like Arabic grammar (nahw, sarf, lugha) and theology (kalam) which are distant means. 'On a thorough basis' ('ala wajh al-tahqiq) distinguishes usul al-fiqh from the sciences of khilaf (disputation) and jadal (argumentation), which also use universal rules leading to fiqh but their aim is to compel the opponent, not to establish truth thoroughly. The commentator then explains that these universal propositions serve as the major premise in syllogistic reasoning (al-shakl al-awwal) or as universal implications (mulazamat kulliyya). Two examples illustrate: one using the first figure (the major premise is 'every ruling that analogy indicates is established'), and another using implication (the conditional: 'whenever analogy indicates a ruling, it is established'). The passage further clarifies that a particular universal proposition may not be explicitly listed in usul works but is subsumed under a more general one. For instance, the implication 'whenever analogy indicates obligation, obligation is established' falls under 'whenever analogy indicates any ruling of this status, it is established.' Thus, such implications are included in usul al-fiqh by way of implication (tatamman). This highlights the systematic and hierarchical nature of usul principles. Although the passage does not engage in inter-madhhab dispute, it reflects the Hanafi inclination toward rigorous logical structuring of the discipline.

Key Terms
القواعد (al-qawa'id): Universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that form the major premise or implication in proofs for fiqh rulings.
التحقيق (al-tahqiq): Thorough establishment of truth, as opposed to mere polemical persuasion. It implies that the science aims at certain or valid knowledge.
الملازمات الكلية (al-mulazamat al-kulliyya): Universal implications (conditional statements) that serve as premises in arguments, e.g., 'Whenever analogy indicates obligation, obligation is established.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the phrase 'to a thorough basis' (على وجه التحقيق) included in the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) To exclude foundational sciences like Arabic grammar and theology
B) To exclude the sciences of khilaf and jadal, which aim to compel the opponent rather than establish truth
C) To ensure that the rules are universal propositions
D) To indicate that usul al-fiqh uses the first figure of syllogism

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal propositions that serve as premises for deriving fiqh rulings, distinguished from foundational and polemical sciences by its aim of thorough truth establishment.

The Universal Propositions of Usul al-Fiqh as the Major Premises of Qiyas
Expounds the definition of usul al-fiqh and its role in deriving fiqh through syllogisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh to identify universal propositions and their role in qiyas-based derivation.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of universal propositions that serve as the major premise in qiyas to derive fiqh rulings in a verifying manner.

The passage defines usul al-fiqh not just as a collection of rules, but as a science that provides the logical framework—the universal propositions—that form the backbone of qiyas. The definition distinguishes usul from auxiliary sciences (like grammar) and polemical disciplines (like jadal) by insisting on proximate access (tawassul qarib) and a verifying manner (tahqiq). We will unpack how these universal propositions function in both conjunctive and exceptional syllogisms, and how even seemingly specific rules are subsumed under broader principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Locate the phrase in the source that defines usul al-fiqh as 'knowledge of rules by which one reaches fiqh in a verifying manner by proximate access.'
The definition is given in the Arabic portion and elaborated in the Urdu commentary.
2
Understand the qualifiers
Analyze the qualifiers 'tawassul qarib' (proximate access) and 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' (verifying manner). The first excludes auxiliary sciences (e.g., Arabic grammar, kalam) that only provide distant access; the second excludes polemical sciences (jadal, munazara) which aim to silence opponents, not verify truth.
These qualifiers define the precise scope of usul al-fiqh as a distinct science.
3
Recognize the nature of the rules
Understand that the 'rules' (qawa'id) in the definition are universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that serve as one of the two premises in a proof (syllogism) for deriving fiqh rulings.
The passage explicitly states that these propositions are the major premise in conjunctive syllogisms or the universal concomitant in exceptional syllogisms.
4
Distinguish between qiyas iqtirani and istithna'i
For conjunctive syllogism (first figure), the major premise is a universal proposition from usul. For exceptional syllogism, the universal concomitant (malzuma) serves as the premise. The passage gives examples: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established.'
Both types rely on universal propositions from usul al-fiqh as a premise.
5
Apply the subsumption principle
Note that even if a specific universal proposition (e.g., 'Whenever qiyas indicates prohibition...') is not explicitly listed in usul books, it falls under a broader universal that is listed (e.g., 'Whenever qiyas indicates any ruling, that ruling is established'). Thus, all such propositions are part of usul by implication (bil-tadammun).
This ensures the completeness of usul al-fiqh as a framework.

التَّرُويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلْويج
مذکور ہو گا اصول فقہ کے مسائل میں بطریق تضمن ۔
اصول فقہ کی تعریف لقمی

تشریح: ولما عرف:۔ اس عبارت کے پانچ حصے ہیں حصہ اول لما عرف سے وعلم اصول الفقہ تک ہے حصہ ثانی و تم اصول الفقہ سے وانما قلنا تک ہے حصہ ثالث وانما قلنا سے لیکر یعنی تک ہے اور حصہ رابع نعنی بالقضایا سے لے کر واعلم تک ہے اور حصہ خامس و اعلم سے لیکر آخر تک ہے اب ہم ہر حصہ کی غرض بیان کرتے ہیں۔
حصہ اول: سے غرض ماتن ماقبل سے ربط بیان کرنا ہے کہ پہلے اصول فقہ کی حد اضافی بیان کی گئی تھی اور اب اصول فقہ کی حد قمی بیان کی جارہی ہے۔ حصہ ثانی:۔ سے غرض ماتن اصول فقہ کی حدیقی کو بیان کرنا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے اعلم بالقواعد التی پیتوصل بہا الیہ علی وجہ التحقیق یعنی اصول فقہ جانتا ہے ایسے قواعد کو کہ ان قواعد کے ذریعے فقہ تک توصل قریب حاصل ہو تحقیق کے طریقہ پری حصہ ثالث:۔ سے غرض ماتن فوائد قیود کو بیان کرنا ہے ماتن نے تو صل قریب کی قید لگائی ہے تو صل قریب کی قید سے علم نحو اور دیگر علوم مثلا علم کلام خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ ان سے فقہ تک توصل بعید حاصل ہوتا ہے یعنی بالواسطہ توصل ہوتا ہے اور جب کہا علی وجہ التحقیق تو اس سے علم جدل اور مناظرہ وغیرہ کو خارج کردیا کیونکہ علم مناظرہ سے بھی توصل الی الفقہ تو ہوتا ہے لیکن ضمناً ہوتا ہے اصل میں مقصود خصم کو چپ کرانا ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ توصل غیر تحقیقی ہوتا ہے۔ حصہ رابع نعنی بالقضایا:۔ سے غرض ماتن مرادی تحقیق کو بیان کرنا ہے لیکن مراد کو مجھنے سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔
مقدمہ: یہ ہے کہ قیاس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) قیاس اقترانی (۲) قیاس استثنائی ۔ قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم بیان کیا جاتا ہے اور پھر لکن سے استثناء کیا جاتا ہے اور قیاس اقترانی میں لزوم بیان نہیں کیا جاتا اور قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے بعد اگر استثناء معین مقدم ہو تو نتیجہ عین تالی ہوگا۔ اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ یہ جو کہا گیا ہے کہ اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کو جاننے کا نام ہے کہ جن کے ذریعہ فقہ تک توصل قریب ہو ان قواعد سے مراد وہ قضا یا کلیہ میں جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک مقدمہ بنتے ہیں یعنی اگر دلیل قیاس اقترانی کی شکل اول کے ذریعہ ہو تو شکل اول کا کبری و بعینہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ ہوگا اور اگر استدلال قیاس استثنائی کے ذریعہ ہو تو اس کا ملازمہ کلیہ یعنی مقدم
It is mentioned in the issues of usul al-fiqh, like our statement: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation in a disputed case, obligation is established therein.' Indeed, this concomitant (mulazama) is subsumed under this larger concomitant: 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling of this nature, that ruling is established.' And obligation is one of the particulars of that ruling. As if it were said: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established; and whenever qiyas indicates permissibility, permissibility is established.' Thus, the concomitant which is one of the two premises of the proof becomes from the issues of usul al-fiqh by way of implication (tadammun).
Translation: When the definition of usul al-fiqh was given in terms of its addition, now we define it in terms of it being a title for a specific science. The matn says: 'Usul al-fiqh is knowledge of such rules by which fiqh is reached in a verifying manner.' That is, knowing such universal propositions by which fiqh is reached in the sense of proximate access (tawassul qarib). We said 'proximate access' to exclude preliminary sciences like Arabic sciences (sarf, nahw, lugha, etc.) and kalam. And our statement 'in a verifying manner' excludes the science of khilaf and jadal, because even though they contain rules that lead to fiqh issues, it is not in a verifying manner; rather, the purpose is to silence the opponent. And these are the rules mentioned in the books Irshad and Muqaddima and their likes, so that points of disagreement are built upon them. And by these universal propositions we mean those that are one of the two premises of the proof upon fiqh issues: when you reason about fiqh issues using the first figure, the major premise of the first figure is precisely these universal propositions, like our statement: 'This ruling is established because qiyas indicates its establishment, and every ruling whose establishment qiyas indicates is established.' And when you reason about the ruling of fiqh issues using universal concomitants along with the existence of the antecedent, then the universal concomitants are the universal propositions, as in our statement: 'This ruling is established because whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, this ruling is established. However, qiyas has indicated the establishment of this ruling, so it is established.' And know that it is possible that this universal proposition itself is not mentioned among the issues of usul al-fiqh, but it falls under such a universal proposition that is mentioned among the issues of usul al-fiqh, like our statement: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation in a disputed case, obligation is established therein.' Indeed, this universal concomitant falls under the universal concomitant: 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling of this nature, the ruling is established.' And obligation and prohibition are among the particulars of that ruling. So as if it were said: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established; and whenever qiyas indicates permissibility, permissibility is established.' Thus, the universal concomitant which is one of the two premises of the proof will be mentioned among the issues of usul al-fiqh by way of implication.

Altarweeh li-hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
It will be mentioned in the issues of usul al-fiqh by way of implication.
Definition of usul al-fiqh by the commentator.

Commentary: 'When he defined...' This statement has five parts. Part one: from 'when he defined' to 'and knowledge of usul al-fiqh'. Part two: from 'and you... usul al-fiqh' to 'and we only said'. Part three: from 'and we only said' to 'that is'. Part four: from 'we mean by the propositions' to 'and know'. Part five: from 'and know' to the end. Now we explain the purpose of each part.
Part one: The matn's purpose is to express connection with what preceded: previously the relative definition (hadd idafi) of usul al-fiqh was given, and now the essential definition (hadd haqiqi) is being given. Part two: The matn's purpose is to express the true definition of usul al-fiqh, which is: 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at it in a verifying manner' — i.e., usul al-fiqh knows such rules by which proximate access to fiqh is achieved in the manner of verification. Part three: The matn's purpose is to explain the benefits of the qualifiers. The matn placed the condition of 'proximate access'; by this condition, nahw and other sciences like kalam are excluded because they give distant access (tawassul ba'id), i.e., indirect access. And when he said 'in a verifying manner', he excluded the science of jidal and munazara etc., because while they also lead to fiqh, it is incidental; the real purpose is to silence the opponent. In summary, the access is not verificatory. Part four: 'We mean by the propositions...' The matn's purpose is to express the intended meaning, but before clarifying the intended meaning, it is necessary to understand a preliminary point.
Preliminary: Qiyas has two types: (1) conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) and (2) exceptional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). In the exceptional syllogism, the entailment (luzum) between premise and conclusion is expressed, and then an exception is made using 'lakin'. In the conjunctive syllogism, entailment is not expressed. In the exceptional syllogism, if the exception is of the affirmative premise, the result is exactly the conclusion. After this preliminary, understand that what was said — 'usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of rules by which proximate access to fiqh is achieved' — by these rules is meant those universal propositions that become one of the two premises of the proof. That is, if the proof is through a conjunctive syllogism in the first figure, then the major premise of the first figure is precisely the universal proposition of usul al-fiqh. And if the reasoning is through an exceptional syllogism, then its universal concomitant — i.e., the premise...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of usul al-fiqh. The author first notes that universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) like 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established' are among the issues of usul al-fiqh. These are subsumed under an even more universal proposition. The Urdu translation clarifies that after defining usul al-fiqh relative to addition, the matn now defines it as a specific science. The definition is: knowledge of rules by which one reaches fiqh in a verifying manner. The qualifier 'proximate access' excludes preliminary sciences like Arabic grammar and kalam, which provide only distant access. 'In a verifying manner' excludes polemical sciences (jadal, munazara) which aim to silence opponents rather than verify the truth. The author then explains that the rules of usul al-fiqh are the major premises of syllogisms (qiyas) used to derive fiqh. Two types of qiyas are distinguished: conjunctive (iqtirani) and exceptional (istithna'i). In the first figure of conjunctive qiyas, the major premise is a universal proposition from usul al-fiqh. In exceptional qiyas, the universal concomitant serves as the premise. The passage also notes that even if a particular universal proposition is not explicitly listed in usul al-fiqh books, it falls under a broader universal proposition that is listed. Thus, the science of usul al-fiqh provides the logical framework for deriving fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
قضية كلية (qadiyya kulliyya): Universal proposition that serves as a major premise in a syllogism to derive a fiqh ruling.
توصل قريب (tawassul qarib): Proximate access to fiqh through direct application of usul rules, as opposed to distant access through auxiliary sciences like grammar.
على وجه التحقيق (ala wajh al-tahqiq): In a verifying manner, i.e., aiming for truth rather than merely silencing an opponent.
قياس اقتراني (qiyas iqtirani): Conjunctive syllogism where a universal proposition is used as a major premise without explicitly stating entailment.
قياس استثنائي (qiyas istithna'i): Exceptional syllogism where the entailment (luzum) between antecedent and consequent is stated, and then an exception is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary function of the universal propositions in usul al-fiqh?
A) They are the conclusions of fiqh rulings
B) They serve as the minor premise in analogical reasoning
C) They serve as the major premise in syllogisms to derive fiqh rulings
D) They are only used in exceptional syllogisms, not conjunctive ones

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal propositions that serve as the major premises in qiyas to derive fiqh rulings in a verifying and proximate manner.

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
The Definition of Usul al-Fiqh and Its Essential Restrictions
Definition with explanatory restrictions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the complete Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and explain how the restrictions 'tawassul qarib' and 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' exclude auxiliary sciences and dialectics.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh: knowledge of rules for direct, precise derivation of fiqh — excluding indirect sciences and adversarial methods.

This lesson unpacks the definition of usul al-fiqh as presented in the classical Hanafi commentary. The author divides the definition into core components and two critical restrictions that delineate the scope of this science. Understanding these restrictions is essential for distinguishing usul al-fiqh from other Islamic sciences like nahw, kalam, and jadal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the complete definition
Find the sentence that gives the full definition of usul al-fiqh in the source text. It is 'عِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ...' but the Urdu commentary states it as 'اعلم بالقواعد التی پیتوصل بہا الیہ علی وجہ التحقیق'.
The definition has two key qualifiers: tawassul qarīb and alā wajh al-tahqīq.
2
Analyze the first restriction: tawassul qarīb
Understand that 'tawassul qarīb' means direct derivation. It excludes sciences like nahw and kalam because they lead to fiqh indirectly, through intermediate steps.
Excluded: nahw (grammar), kalam (theology), etc.
3
Analyze the second restriction: alā wajh al-tahqīq
This means 'in a precise manner' or 'investigative manner.' It excludes sciences like jadal (dialectics) and munāẓara (debate) because their primary goal is to silence the opponent, not to achieve certainty.
Excluded: jadal, munāẓara.
4
Summarize the scope
Combine the definition with the restrictions to articulate what usul al-fiqh includes and excludes.

تشریح: ولما عرف:۔ اس عبارت کے پانچ حصے ہیں حصہ اول لما عرف سے وعلم اصول الفقہ تک ہے حصہ ثانی و تم اصول الفقہ سے وانما قلنا تک ہے حصہ ثالث وانما قلنا سے لیکر یعنی تک ہے اور حصہ رابع نعنی بالقضایا سے لے کر واعلم تک ہے اور حصہ خامس و اعلم سے لیکر آخر تک ہے اب ہم ہر حصہ کی غرض بیان کرتے ہیں۔
حصہ اول: سے غرض ماتن ماقبل سے ربط بیان کرنا ہے کہ پہلے اصول فقہ کی حد اضافی بیان کی گئی تھی اور اب اصول فقہ کی حد قمی بیان کی جارہی ہے۔ حصہ ثانی:۔ سے غرض ماتن اصول فقہ کی حدیقی کو بیان کرنا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے اعلم بالقواعد التی پیتوصل بہا الیہ علی وجہ التحقیق
یعنی اصول فقہ جانتا ہے ایسے قواعد کو کہ ان قواعد کے ذریعے فقہ تک توصل قریب حاصل ہو تحقیق کے طریقہ پری حصہ ثالث:۔ سے غرض ماتن فوائد قیود کو بیان کرنا ہے ماتن نے تو صل قریب کی قید لگائی ہے تو صل قریب کی قید سے علم نحو اور دیگر علوم مثلا علم کلام خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ ان سے فقہ تک توصل بعید حاصل ہوتا ہے یعنی بالواسطہ توصل ہوتا ہے اور جب کہا علی وجہ التحقیق تو اس سے علم جدل اور مناظرہ وغیرہ کو خارج کردیا کیونکہ علم مناظرہ سے بھی توصل الی الفقہ تو ہوتا ہے لیکن ضمناً ہوتا ہے اصل میں مقصود خصم کو چپ کرانا ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ توصل غیر تحقیقی ہوتا ہے۔ حصہ رابع نعنی بالقضایا:۔ سے غرض ماتن مرادی تحقیق کو بیان کرنا ہے لیکن مراد کو مجھنے سے پہلے بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدمہ
سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔
مقدمہ: یہ ہے کہ قیاس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) قیاس اقترانی (۲) قیاس استثنائی ۔
قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم بیان کیا جاتا ہے اور پھر لکن سے استثناء کیا جاتا ہے اور قیاس اقترانی میں لزوم بیان نہیں کیا جاتا اور قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے بعد اگر استثناء معین مقدم ہو تو نتیجہ عین تالی ہوگا۔ اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ یہ جو کہا گیا ہے کہ اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کو جاننے کا نام ہے کہ جن کے ذریعہ فقہ تک توصل قریب ہو ان قواعد سے مراد وہ قضا یا کلیہ میں جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک مقدمہ بنتے ہیں یعنی اگر دلیل قیاس اقترانی کی شکل اول کے ذریعہ ہو تو شکل اول کا کبری و و بعینہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ ہوگا اور اگر استدلال قیاس استثنائی کے ذریعہ ہو تو اس کا ملازمہ کلیہ یعنی مقدم اور تالی کے در یان جولزوم بیان کیا ہے یہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ ہو گا مثلاً ایک حکم کے بارہ میں ہمارا دعویٰ ہے کہ یہ حکم ثابت ہے اس پر استدلال اگر قیاس اقترانی کی شکل اول کے ذریعہ ہو تو تو استدلال یوں ہوگا ہذا الحکم بدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس یہ صغریٰ ہے اور ہذا الحکم موضوع ہے اور اگلی عبارت محمول ہے اور وکل حکم یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس فہو ثابت یہ کبرئی ہے اس میں کل حکم یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس موضوع ہے اور فہو ثابت یہ محمول ہے اور یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس حد اوسط کو گرایا تو باقی نتیجہ نکلا ہذا الحکم ثابت ، اس استدلال میں جینہ اصول فقہ کا اصل ہے اور اگر ہذا الحکم ثابت پر استدلال قیاس استثنائی کے ذریعہ ہو تو استدلال یوں ہوگا کلما دل القياس على ثبوت ہذا الحكم فيكون بذا الحکم چاہتا یہ ملازمہ کلیہ ہے اور آگے لکن سے استثناء ہے لکن القياس دن علی ثبوت ہذا الحکم ، سیہ
استثناء بعینہ مقدم ہے لہذا اس کا نتیجہ بعینہ تالی ہوگا یعنی فیکون ہذا الحکم ثابتا تو اس میں ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ کا ضابطہ ہے۔ حصہ خامس و اعلم :۔ سے غرض پاتن سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلیہ بنتے ہیں اور کبری اور بلازمہ کلیہ بعینہ اصول فقہ کا ضابطہ ہیں ہمیں یہ تسلیم نہیں ہے مثلا کسی حکم کے وجوب پر استدلال کریں ملازمہ کلیہ کے ذریعہ تو استدلال یوں ہوگا کلما دل القیاس علی وجوب ہذا الحکم فیکون ہذا الحکم و اجبا یہ ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ کی کسی کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے اور اگر استدلال شکل اول کے ذریعہ سے کریں تو استدلال یوں ہو گا ہذا الحکم بدل علی وجوبه القياس و کل حکم یدل علی وجوبه القیاس فہو واجب یہ کبری اصول فقہ کی کسی کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو کہا گیا ہے کہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلی اصول فقہ میں پایا جاتا ہے یہ عام ہے بعینہ پایا جاتا ہو یا دوسرے قضیہ کے ضمن میں پایا جائے اور مذکورہ ملازمہ کلیہ اور کبرٹی بھی اگر چہ صراحتا اصول فقہ میں مذکور نہیں ہے لیکن یہ دوسرے قضیہ کے ضمن میں پائے جاتے ہیں اور یہ ملازمہ کلیہ اور کبری جس قضیہ کے ضمن میں پائے جاتے ہیں وہ یہ ہے کلمادل القیاس علی ثبوت ہذا الحکم فیکون ہذا الحکم ثابتاً کیونکہ ثبوت حکم عام ہے وجوب ، جواز ، اور استحباب سب کو شامل ہے پس گویا کہ یوں کہا گیا کہ کلما دل القیاس على الوجوب فيكون واجباً و كلما دل القياس على الجواز فیکون جائز ۔ ( فلا اعتراض)
تلویح
.( قَوْلُهُ وَعِلْمُ أَصُولِ الْفِقْهِ بَعْدَ مَا تَقَرَّرَ أَنَّ أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ لَقَبٌ لِلْعِلْمِ الْمَخْصُوصِ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى إِضَافَةِ الْعِلْمِ إِلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقْصَدَ زِيَادَةُ بَيَانٍ وَتَوْضِيحٍ
The passage is primarily in Urdu, with key Arabic phrases. Translation of main parts: 'Usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh in a precise manner.' 'Qiyas has two types: conjunctive and disjunctive.' 'The universal proposition of usul al-fiqh serves as the major premise in first-figure syllogisms or as the conditional premise in disjunctive syllogisms.' 'The response: the major premise and conditional premise are found within another universal proposition, such as 'whatever qiyas indicates about the establishment of a ruling, that ruling is established.' This includes obligation, permissibility, and recommendation.'
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the definition of usul al-fiqh. The author divides the original text into five sections. The first section links to the previous discussion. The second section presents the complete definition: usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) through which one reaches fiqh in a precise manner (ala wajh al-tahqiq). The third section explains the benefits of the restrictions: 'direct derivation' (tawassul qarib) excludes auxiliary sciences like nahw and kalam because they lead to fiqh indirectly; 'precise manner' excludes dialectics and debate because their primary aim is silence the opponent, not achieve certainty. The fourth section elaborates on the intended meaning of 'rules' (qadaya kulliyya). The author first introduces a preamble on the two types of qiyas: conjunctive (iqtirani) and disjunctive (istithna'i). In disjunctive qiyas, the connection between the antecedent and consequent is expressed, and then an exception is made with 'but' (lakin). In conjunctive qiyas, there is no expression of connection. When the muqaddam (antecedent) is affirmed in disjunctive qiyas, the result is the consequent. The author then explains that the rules of usul al-fiqh become either the major premise in first-figure syllogisms or the conditional premise in disjunctive syllogisms. Examples are given: for conjunctive, the major is 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established'; for disjunctive, the conditional is 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, then this ruling is established.' The fifth section answers a potential objection: these specific premises are not found explicitly in usul al-fiqh books. The response: they are included implicitly within a general universal proposition, such as 'Whatever qiyas indicates about the establishment of a ruling, that ruling is established,' which covers obligation, permissibility, and recommendation. The Arabic line from the super-commentary (Talwih) notes that after establishing that 'usul al-fiqh' is a title for a specific science, adding the word 'science' ('ilm) is redundant unless for further clarification.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usūl al-fiqh): The knowledge of rules (qawā'id) by which one arrives at fiqh in a precise manner.
قضیہ کلیہ (qaḍiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as a premise in qiyas, either as major premise in conjunctive syllogism or conditional premise in disjunctive syllogism.
قیاس اقترانی (qiyās iqtirānī): A conjunctive syllogism where the connection between premises is not explicitly stated; the major premise is a universal affirmative.
قیاس استثنائی (qiyās istithnā'ī): A disjunctive syllogism where the connection between antecedent and consequent is stated, and an exception is made with 'but' (lākin).
توصل قریب (tawassul qarīb): Direct derivation of fiqh rules, as opposed to indirect derivation through intermediate sciences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' in the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) To exclude sciences like nahw and kalam.
B) To exclude dialectics and debate because they aim to silence opponents, not achieve certainty.
C) To ensure that only qiyas is used.
D) To include secondary sciences.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is precisely defined as direct and investigative knowledge of the rules of derivation, excluding indirect sciences and adversarial methods.

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
The Role of Qadaya Kulliyya in Qiyas: Premises for Derivation
Function of qadaya kulliyya in qiyas and defense against objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) of usul al-fiqh function as major premises in conjunctive syllogisms or as conditional premises in disjunctive syllogisms, and defend their presence in usul works through implicit inclusion.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh's universal propositions are the major premises (conjunctive) or conditional premises (disjunctive) in qiyas, often implied within a general principle.

This lesson dives into the fourth and fifth sections of the commentary, where the author specifies what is meant by 'rules' (qadaya kulliyya) in the definition of usul al-fiqh. These universal propositions serve as the backbone of qiyas, forming the major premise in conjunctive syllogisms or the conditional premise in disjunctive syllogisms. The lesson also addresses a common objection about the explicit presence of these premises in usul works.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two types of qiyas
Review the preamble that distinguishes conjunctive (iqtirani) and disjunctive (istithna'i) qiyas. Note that in conjunctive qiyas the connection is not stated, while in disjunctive qiyas the connection (luzum) is expressed and an exception is made with 'lakin'.
Conjunctive: major premise + minor premise → conclusion; Disjunctive: conditional premise + exception → conclusion.
2
Identify how qadaya kulliyya serve as premises
Understand that a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) from usul al-fiqh becomes either the major premise in a first-figure conjunctive syllogism or the conditional premise in a disjunctive syllogism.
Example major premise: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established'.
3
Work through the conjunctive example
Analyze the example given: for a ruling claiming 'this ruling is established', the syllogism is: Minor: 'This ruling is indicated by qiyas' (this is the subject); Major: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established'; Conclusion: 'This ruling is established'. The major premise is the usul qadiyya kulliyya.
The major premise is a universal affirmative.
4
Work through the disjunctive example
Analyze the disjunctive example: 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, then this ruling is established; but qiyas indeed indicates it; therefore it is established.' The conditional premise is the usul qadiyya kulliyya.
Here the conditional expresses a cause-and-effect relationship.
5
Address the objection and response
Understand the objection that specific premises (e.g., for wujub) are not found explicitly in usul books. The response: they are implied within a general principle like 'Whatever qiyas indicates about the establishment of a ruling, that ruling is established,' which covers all specific rulings (wujub, jawaz, istihbab).
This shows that usul premises are not limited to explicit statements but are embedded in comprehensive rules.
