قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم بیان کیا جاتا ہے اور پھر لکن سے استثناء کیا جاتا ہے اور قیاس اقترانی میں لزوم بیان نہیں کیا جاتا اور قیاس استثنائی میں مقدم وتالی کے بعد اگر استثناء معین مقدم ہو تو نتیجہ عین تالی ہوگا۔ اس تمہید کے بعد یہ سمجھیں کہ یہ جو کہا گیا ہے کہ اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کو جاننے کا نام ہے کہ جن کے ذریعہ فقہ تک توصل قریب ہو ان قواعد سے مراد وہ قضا یا کلیہ میں جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں سے ایک مقدمہ بنتے ہیں یعنی اگر دلیل قیاس اقترانی کی شکل اول کے ذریعہ ہو تو شکل اول کا کبری و و بعینہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ ہوگا اور اگر استدلال قیاس استثنائی کے ذریعہ ہو تو اس کا ملازمہ کلیہ یعنی مقدم اور تالی کے در یان جولزوم بیان کیا ہے یہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ ہو گا مثلاً ایک حکم کے بارہ میں ہمارا دعویٰ ہے کہ یہ حکم ثابت ہے اس پر استدلال اگر قیاس اقترانی کی شکل اول کے ذریعہ ہو تو تو استدلال یوں ہوگا ہذا الحکم بدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس یہ صغریٰ ہے اور ہذا الحکم موضوع ہے اور اگلی عبارت محمول ہے اور وکل حکم یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس فہو ثابت یہ کبرئی ہے اس میں کل حکم یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس موضوع ہے اور فہو ثابت یہ محمول ہے اور یدل علی ثبوتہ القیاس حد اوسط کو گرایا تو باقی نتیجہ نکلا ہذا الحکم ثابت ، اس استدلال میں جینہ اصول فقہ کا اصل ہے اور اگر ہذا الحکم ثابت پر استدلال قیاس استثنائی کے ذریعہ ہو تو استدلال یوں ہوگا کلما دل القياس على ثبوت ہذا الحكم فيكون بذا الحکم چاہتا یہ ملازمہ کلیہ ہے اور آگے لکن سے استثناء ہے لکن القياس دن علی ثبوت ہذا الحکم ، سیہ
استثناء بعینہ مقدم ہے لہذا اس کا نتیجہ بعینہ تالی ہوگا یعنی فیکون ہذا الحکم ثابتا تو اس میں ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ کا ضابطہ ہے۔ حصہ خامس و اعلم :۔ سے غرض پاتن سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا قضیہ کلیہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلیہ بنتے ہیں اور کبری اور بلازمہ کلیہ بعینہ اصول فقہ کا ضابطہ ہیں ہمیں یہ تسلیم نہیں ہے مثلا کسی حکم کے وجوب پر استدلال کریں ملازمہ کلیہ کے ذریعہ تو استدلال یوں ہوگا کلما دل القیاس علی وجوب ہذا الحکم فیکون ہذا الحکم و اجبا یہ ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ کی کسی کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے اور اگر استدلال شکل اول کے ذریعہ سے کریں تو استدلال یوں ہو گا ہذا الحکم بدل علی وجوبه القياس و کل حکم یدل علی وجوبه القیاس فہو واجب یہ کبری اصول فقہ کی کسی کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو کہا گیا ہے کہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلی اصول فقہ میں پایا جاتا ہے یہ عام ہے بعینہ پایا جاتا ہو یا دوسرے قضیہ کے ضمن میں پایا جائے اور مذکورہ ملازمہ کلیہ اور کبرٹی بھی اگر چہ صراحتا اصول فقہ میں مذکور نہیں ہے لیکن یہ دوسرے قضیہ کے ضمن میں پائے جاتے ہیں اور یہ ملازمہ کلیہ اور کبری جس قضیہ کے ضمن میں پائے جاتے ہیں وہ یہ ہے کلمادل القیاس علی ثبوت ہذا الحکم فیکون ہذا الحکم ثابتاً کیونکہ ثبوت حکم عام ہے وجوب ، جواز ، اور استحباب سب کو شامل ہے پس گویا کہ یوں کہا گیا کہ کلما دل القیاس على الوجوب فيكون واجباً و كلما دل القياس على الجواز فیکون جائز ۔ ( فلا اعتراض)
تلویح
.( قَوْلُهُ وَعِلْمُ أَصُولِ الْفِقْهِ بَعْدَ مَا تَقَرَّرَ أَنَّ أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ لَقَبٌ لِلْعِلْمِ الْمَخْصُوصِ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى إِضَافَةِ الْعِلْمِ إِلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقْصَدَ زِيَادَةُ بَيَانٍ وَتَوْضِيحٍ
The passage is primarily in Urdu, with key Arabic phrases. Translation of main parts: 'Usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh in a precise manner.' 'Qiyas has two types: conjunctive and disjunctive.' 'The universal proposition of usul al-fiqh serves as the major premise in first-figure syllogisms or as the conditional premise in disjunctive syllogisms.' 'The response: the major premise and conditional premise are found within another universal proposition, such as 'whatever qiyas indicates about the establishment of a ruling, that ruling is established.' This includes obligation, permissibility, and recommendation.'
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the definition of usul al-fiqh. The author divides the original text into five sections. The first section links to the previous discussion. The second section presents the complete definition: usul al-fiqh is knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) through which one reaches fiqh in a precise manner (ala wajh al-tahqiq). The third section explains the benefits of the restrictions: 'direct derivation' (tawassul qarib) excludes auxiliary sciences like nahw and kalam because they lead to fiqh indirectly; 'precise manner' excludes dialectics and debate because their primary aim is silence the opponent, not achieve certainty. The fourth section elaborates on the intended meaning of 'rules' (qadaya kulliyya). The author first introduces a preamble on the two types of qiyas: conjunctive (iqtirani) and disjunctive (istithna'i). In disjunctive qiyas, the connection between the antecedent and consequent is expressed, and then an exception is made with 'but' (lakin). In conjunctive qiyas, there is no expression of connection. When the muqaddam (antecedent) is affirmed in disjunctive qiyas, the result is the consequent. The author then explains that the rules of usul al-fiqh become either the major premise in first-figure syllogisms or the conditional premise in disjunctive syllogisms. Examples are given: for conjunctive, the major is 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established'; for disjunctive, the conditional is 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, then this ruling is established.' The fifth section answers a potential objection: these specific premises are not found explicitly in usul al-fiqh books. The response: they are included implicitly within a general universal proposition, such as 'Whatever qiyas indicates about the establishment of a ruling, that ruling is established,' which covers obligation, permissibility, and recommendation. The Arabic line from the super-commentary (Talwih) notes that after establishing that 'usul al-fiqh' is a title for a specific science, adding the word 'science' ('ilm) is redundant unless for further clarification.

Key Terms
اصول فقہ (usūl al-fiqh): The knowledge of rules (qawā'id) by which one arrives at fiqh in a precise manner.
قضیہ کلیہ (qaḍiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as a premise in qiyas, either as major premise in conjunctive syllogism or conditional premise in disjunctive syllogism.
قیاس اقترانی (qiyās iqtirānī): A conjunctive syllogism where the connection between premises is not explicitly stated; the major premise is a universal affirmative.
قیاس استثنائی (qiyās istithnā'ī): A disjunctive syllogism where the connection between antecedent and consequent is stated, and an exception is made with 'but' (lākin).
توصل قریب (tawassul qarīb): Direct derivation of fiqh rules, as opposed to indirect derivation through intermediate sciences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi school respond to the objection that specific usul premises (e.g., for wujub) are not explicitly found in usul books?
A) They admit the premises are missing and rely on other evidence.
B) They argue that the specific premises are implicitly included within a general universal proposition that is found in the books.
C) They say that such specific premises are not needed because qiyas does not require a major premise.
D) They claim that the books actually contain all specific premises verbatim.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh's universal propositions function as major premises (conjunctive qiyas) or conditional premises (disjunctive qiyas), and specific premises are implicitly included in general rules, making the system comprehensive and efficient.

Usul al-Fiqh Propositions as Major Premises in Syllogisms
Explaining how usul axioms serve as major premises in deductive reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of universal usul propositions as major premises in Hanafi syllogistic reasoning and explain how they are implicit in broader principles.

Core Idea
Universal usul propositions are the major premises of syllogisms; even if not explicitly stated, they are implied in general principles.

In this lesson, we explore how usul al-fiqh propositions function as the backbone of deductive reasoning. The passage demonstrates their use in both conjunctive and exceptional syllogisms, and addresses a subtle objection about their explicit presence in usul texts. By understanding this, you will see how Hanafi jurists derive rulings through logical inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two syllogistic forms used
The passage illustrates reasoning in the first form of conjunctive syllogism and exceptional syllogism.
2
Locate the usul proposition in the first form
The major premise 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established' is a universal usul proposition.
This serves as the major premise (kubra) in the categorical syllogism.
3
Locate the usul proposition in exceptional syllogism
The universal conditional 'Whenever qiyas indicates establishment, then it is established' serves as the major premise.
This is called the mulāzama kulliyya.
4
Analyze the objection
The objector claims that specific propositions like 'qiyas indicates obligation → obligatory' are not found in usul books.
The objection doubts the completeness of usul texts.
5
Understand the response
The author explains that these specific propositions are implicit in broader principles because 'establishment' includes obligation, permissibility, etc.
Thus, no explicit mention is necessary; the general principle suffices.

گیا کہ کلما دل القياس على الوجوب فيكون واجباً و كلما دل القياس على الجواز فیکون جائز ۔ ( فلا اعتراض)
And what is stated between the consequent and the antecedent is a universal proposition of usul al-fiqh. For example, regarding a ruling we claim that it is established. If the inference is via the first form of conjunctive syllogism, the inference is: This ruling by qiyas indicates its establishment—this is the minor premise, and this ruling is the subject, and the next phrase is the predicate. And every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established—this is the major premise; in it, 'every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment' is the subject, and 'it is established' is the predicate. Dropping the middle term 'indicates its establishment by qiyas', the remaining result is: This ruling is established. In this inference, what is from usul al-fiqh is the original. And if the inference that this ruling is established is via exceptional syllogism, the inference is: Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, then this ruling is established? This is a universal conditional premise. Then there is an exception with 'but': But qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling. This exception is exactly the antecedent, so its result is exactly the consequent, i.e., then this ruling is established. So in this, the universal conditional is the rule of usul al-fiqh. The fifth section: 'And know' is intended to answer a hypothetical question. Question: You said that a universal proposition of usul al-fiqh serves as the major premise of the first form and as the universal conditional of exceptional syllogism, and that major premise and universal conditional are exactly the rules of usul al-fiqh. We do not accept this. For example, if we infer the obligation of a ruling via a universal conditional, the inference would be: Whenever qiyas indicates the obligation of this ruling, then this ruling is obligatory. This universal conditional is not mentioned in any book of usul al-fiqh. And if we infer via the first form, the inference would be: This ruling by qiyas indicates its obligation, and every ruling that qiyas indicates its obligation is obligatory. This major premise is not mentioned in any book of usul al-fiqh. Answer: The summary is that what was said—that the major premise of the first form and the universal conditional of exceptional syllogism are found in usul al-fiqh—is general: they are found either verbatim or within another proposition. And the mentioned universal conditional and major premise, though not explicitly mentioned in usul al-fiqh, are found within another proposition. And that proposition is: Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, then this ruling is established. Because the establishment of a ruling is general, including obligation, permissibility, and recommendation. So it is as if it were said: Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, it is obligatory; and whenever qiyas indicates permissibility, it is permissible. (So no objection.)
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how universal propositions of usul al-fiqh function as the major premises in logical syllogisms used to derive fiqh rulings. The author first illustrates the use of the first form (shakl awwal) of categorical syllogism: the minor premise states that a particular ruling is indicated by qiyas, the major premise is a universal usul principle that 'every ruling indicated by qiyas is established', and the conclusion is that the ruling is established. The middle term is 'indicated by qiyas'. Then he illustrates the use of exceptional syllogism (qiyas istithnai) where the universal conditional premise is 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of a ruling, then it is established', and the exception affirms the antecedent. A hypothetical objection is raised: specific propositions like 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, it is obligatory' are not explicitly found in usul books. The answer is that they are implicit in the broader usul principle about 'establishment' (thubut) which encompasses all legal values (obligation, permission, recommendation). Thus, the usul principles are comprehensive and cover all particular applications.

Key Terms
قضیہ کلیہ (qadiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that applies to all particulars of its subject, serving as a major premise or universal conditional in syllogistic reasoning.
ملازمہ کلیہ (mulāzama kulliyya): A universal conditional proposition (if-then) used in exceptional syllogism, connecting the indication of qiyas to the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the first form of conjunctive syllogism, what role does the usul proposition 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates its establishment is established' play?
A) Minor premise
B) Major premise
C) Middle term
D) Conclusion

Key Takeaway
Universal usul propositions function as major premises in syllogisms; specific instances are implied by broader principles.

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: Qa'idah and Near Conveyance
Defining usul al-fiqh through qa'idah and tawassul qarib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a qa'idah (rule) and explain why usul al-fiqh is a 'near conveyance' (tawassul qarib) to fiqh, distinguishing it from Arabic grammar and kalam.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of universal rules that directly lead to fiqh, unlike Arabic and kalam which are only preliminaries.

What exactly is usul al-fiqh? The passage defines it as a set of universal rules that provide a near conveyance to fiqh rulings. We will explore the key terms: qa'idah and tawassul qarib, and see how this distinguishes usul al-fiqh from other Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Define 'qa'idah' as a universal legal rule
Identify the definition of qa'idah from the text: a hukm kulli that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it. Note the example: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.'
This is the foundational unit of usul al-fiqh.
2
Understand 'tawassul qarib' (near conveyance)
Explain that usul al-fiqh provides a direct means to reach fiqh rulings without an intermediary, derived from the causative ba and the immediate link to fiqh.
Contrast with distant conveyances that require intermediate steps.
3
Distinguish usul al-fiqh from Arabic grammar and kalam
Show why Arabic grammar and kalam are excluded: they are only preliminaries (mabadi) and lead to fiqh only indirectly (through knowledge of word meanings or proving the authenticity of sources).
This clarifies the boundary of usul al-fiqh.

كَشَجَرَةِ الْأَرَاكِ وَالْقَاعِدَةُ حُكْمٌ كُلّى يَنْطَبِقُ عَلَى جُزْئِيَّاتِهِ لِيُتَعَرَّفَ أَحْكَامُهَا مِنْهُ كَقَوْلِنَا كُلُّ حُكْمِ دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ الْقِيَاسُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ الْقَرِيبُ مُسْتَفَادٌ مِنَ الْبَاء السَّبَبِيَّةِ الظَّاهِرَةِ فِي السَّبَبِ الْقَرِيبِ وَمِنْ إطْلَاقِ التَّوَصُّلِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ ، إِذْ فِي الْبَعِيدِ يُتَوَصَّلُ إِلَى الْوَاسِطَةِ وَمِنْهَا إلَى الْفِقْهِ فَيَخْرُجُ الْعِلْمُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ وَالْكَلَامِ ؛ لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ مَبَادِى أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ بِهِمَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ لَيْسَ بِقَرِيبٍ ، إِذْ يَتَوَكَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ إِلَى مَعْرِفَةِ كَيْفِيَّةِ دَلَالَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ عَلَى مَدْلُولَاتِهَا الْوَضْعِيَّةِ وَبِوَاسِطَةِ ذَلِكَ يَقْتَدِرُ عَلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِنْ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ يَتَوَصَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْكَلَامِ إِلَى ثُبُوتِ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَوُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمَا لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَالتَّحْقِيقُ فِى هَذَا الْمَقَامِ أَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَمْ يُخْلَقُ عَبَثًا وَلَمْ يُتْرَكَ سُدًى ، بَلْ تَعَلَّقَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ أَعْمَالِهِ حُكْمٌ مِنْ قِبَلِ الشَّارِعِ مَنُوطٌ بِدَلِيلٍ يَخُصُّهُ لِيَسْتَنْبِطَ مِنْهُ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ وَيُقَاسُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ مَا يُنَاسِبُهُ لِتَعَدُّرِ الْإِحَاطَةِ بِجَمِيعِ الْجُزْئِيَّاتِ فَحَصَلَتْ قَضَايَا مَوْضُوعَاتُهَا أَفْعَالُ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ وَمَحْمُولَاتُهَا أَحْكَامُ الشَّارِعِ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ فَسُمِّيَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا الحَاصِلُ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِقْهًا ، ثُمَّ نَظَرُوا فِي تَفَاصِيلٍ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَعُمُومِهَا فَوَجَدُوا الْأَدِلَّةَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ وَالْأَحْكَامَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْوُجُوبِ وَالنَّدْبِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ وَالْكَرَاهَةِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ وَتَأَمَّلُوا فِي كَيْفِيَّةِ الاسْتِدْلَالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَظَرٍ إِلَى تَفَاصِيلِهِمَا إِلَّا عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْمِثَالِ فَحَصَلَ لَهُمْ قَضَايَا كُلِّيَّةٌ مُتَعَلَّقَةٌ بِكَيْفِيَّةِ الاستدلالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا وَبَيَانُ طُرُقِهِ وَشَرَائِطِهِ لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا إِلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ عَنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ فَضَبَطُوهَا وَدَوَّنُوهَا وَأَضَافُوا إِلَيْهَا مِنْ اللَّوَاحِقِ وَالْمُتَمِّمَاتِ وَبَيَانِ الاخْتِلَافَاتِ مَا يَلِيقُ بِهَا وَسَمَّوُا الْعِلْمَ بِهَا أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ فَصَارَتْ عِبَارَةً عَنْ الْعِلْمِ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَلَفْظُ الْقَوَاعِدِ مُشْعِرٌ بِقَيْدِ الْإِجْمَالِ وَزَادَ الْمُصَنِّفُ قَيْدَ التَّحْقِيقِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْخِلَافِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَمْنَعَ كَوْنَ قَوَاعِدِهِ مِمَّا يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ تَوَصُّلًا قَرِيبًا ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا يُتَوَكَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مُحَافَظَةِ الْحُكْمِ الْمُسْتَنْبَطِ أَوْ مُدَافَعَتِهِ وَنِسْبَتِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَغَيْرِهِ عَلَى السَّوِيَّةِ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَلِيَّ إِمَّا مُجِيبٌ يَحْفَظُ وَضْعًا ، وَإِمَّا مُعْتَرِضٌ يَهْدِمُ وَضْعًا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْفُقَهَاءَ أَكْثَرُوا فِيهِ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ وَبَنَوْا نِكَاتَهُ عَلَيْهَا حَتَّى تُوُهِّمَ أَنَّ لَهُ اخْتِصَاصًا بِالْفِقْهِ. ترجمہ: قوله وعلم اصول الفقه . بعد اس کے ثابت ہو چکی ہے یہ بات کہ بیشک اصول فقہ لقب ہے ایک علم مخصوص کا نہیں ہے کوئی حاجت علم کی اضافت کرنے کی اس کی طرف مگر یہ کہ ارادہ کیا جائے بیان اور توضیح کی زیادتی کا جیسے شجرة الا راک ( پیلو کا درخت ) اور قاعدہ ایسا حکم کلی ہے جو منطبق ہوتا ہو اپنی جزئیات پر تاکہ پہچانے جائیں اس کے احکام اس سے جیسے ہمارا قول۔ ہر ایسا حکم جس پر قیاس دلالت کرے وہ ثابت ہے اور توصل قریب مستفاد ہوتا ہے اس بائے سبیہ سے جو ظاہر ہے سبب قریب میں اور توصل کی نسبت کرنے سے فقہ کی طرف اس لئے کہ نسبت بعید میں تو صل ہوتا ہے واسطہ کی طرف پھر اس واسطہ سے توصل ہوتا ہے فقہ کی طرف۔ پس خارج ہو جائے گا وہ علم جو حاصل ہوتا ہے علوم عربیہ اور علم کلام سے اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں اصول فقہ کے مبادی میں سے ہیں اور توصل ان دونوں سے فقہ تک توصل قریب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ قواعد عربیہ سے توصل ہوتا ہے الفاظ کی مدلولات وضعیہ پر دلالت کرنے کی کیفیت کی معرفت کی طرف۔ اور اس واسطہ کے ساتھ وہ قدرت حاصل ہوتی ہے احکام کے استنباط کرنے پر کتاب سے اور سنت سے۔ اور اسی طرح توصل حاصل ہوتا ہے قواعد کلام کے ساتھ کتاب وسنت کے ثبوت کی طرف اور ان دونوں کے صدق کے وجوب کی طرف تاکہ توصل حاصل ہو اس کے ساتھ فقہ تک اور تحقیق اس مقام میں یہ ہے کہ بیشک انسان نہیں پیدا کیا گیا بے کار اور نہیں چھوڑا گیا فضول بلکہ متعلق ہے اس کے ہر عمل کے ساتھ حکم شارع کی جانب سے مدار اس حکم کا ایسی دلیل کے ساتھ ہے کہ خاص کرے وہ دلیل اس علم کو تا کہ استنباط کیا جائے اس سے ضرورت کے وقت اور قیاس کیا جائے اس حکم پر ایسے حکم کو جو اس کے مناسب ہو بوجہ تمام جزئیات کے احاطے کے مشکل ہونے کے۔ پس حاصل ہوئے چند ایسے قضایا کہ ان کا موضوع مکلفین کے افعال ہیں اور ان کا معمول شارع کے احکام ہیں تفصیلا ۔ پس نام رکھا گیا اس علم کا جو حاصل ہونے والا ہے ان ادلہ سے فقہ ۔ پھر غور کیا انہوں نے اولہ اور احکام کی تفصیل میں
Like the araak tree; and al-qa'idah is a universal ruling that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it, like our saying: Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established. And 'near conveyance' (tawassul qarib) is derived from the causative ba' which is apparent in the near cause, and from the unrestricted application of 'conveyance' to fiqh. For in 'distant' (conveyance), one conveys to an intermediary, and from it to fiqh. Thus, the knowledge of the rules of Arabic (grammar) and kalam (theology) is excluded because they are from the preliminaries (mabadi) of usul al-fiqh, and conveyance by them to fiqh is not near. For through the rules of Arabic one arrives at knowledge of how words indicate their conventional meanings, and by that means one is able to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, through the rules of kalam one arrives at the establishment of the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness, so that by that one may reach fiqh. The verification in this context is that man was not created in vain nor left neglected; rather, attached to each of his actions is a ruling from the Lawgiver, contingent upon a specific evidence so that he may derive from it when needed, and analogize to that ruling what is appropriate, due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars. Thus, propositions arose whose subjects are the acts of the mukallaf and whose predicates are the rulings of the Lawgiver in detail, and the knowledge derived from those evidences was called fiqh. Then they examined the details of those evidences and rulings and their generality, and found that the evidences reduce to the Book, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, and the rulings reduce to obligation (wujub), recommendation (nadb), prohibition (hurmah), dislike (karahah), and permissibility (ibahah). They reflected on the manner of inference (istidlal) from those evidences to those rulings in general (ijmalan), without regard to their details except by way of example, and thus universal propositions were obtained relating to the manner of inference from those evidences to those rulings in general, and the exposition of its ways and conditions, so that through each of those propositions one may derive many of those particular rulings from their detailed evidences. So they recorded them, codified them, and added to them what befits of supplements, completions, and exposition of differences, and they called the knowledge of them usul al-fiqh. Thus it came to be an expression of the knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) by which one reaches fiqh. The term 'rules' indicates the condition of generality. And the author added the condition of 'verification' (tahqiq) to exclude the science of disputation (ilm al-khilaf). And someone might argue that its rules are not a means of near conveyance to fiqh, but rather they are used to preserve the derived ruling, or to defend it, and to ascribe it to fiqh or other sciences equally. For the dialectician is either a respondent who preserves a position or an objector who demolishes a position, but the jurists have included many fiqh issues in it and built its points upon them, so that it was imagined that it is specific to fiqh.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the science of usul al-fiqh. It begins by defining a 'qa'idah' (rule) as a universal proposition that applies to its particulars, exemplified by the statement 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.' Then it discusses the concept of 'tawassul qarib' (near conveyance) versus 'tawassul ba'id' (distant conveyance) to fiqh. The author explains that usul al-fiqh provides near conveyance to fiqh, whereas Arabic grammar and theology (kalam) are only distant conveyances because they are preliminaries (mabadi) that lead to understanding the sources but not directly to fiqh rulings. The passage then traces the historical development: human actions have rulings from the Lawgiver attached to specific evidences; since encompassing all particulars is impossible, qiyas (analogy) is used. This produced detailed propositions about acts of mukallaf and divine rulings, called fiqh. Then scholars examined the evidences (Book, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and rulings (obligation, recommendation, etc.) and studied the general method of deriving rulings from them. This gave rise to universal propositions about the method of inference, which they codified as usul al-fiqh. The definition: 'knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh.' The term 'rules' (qawa'id) indicates generality, and the author's addition of 'verification' (tahqiq) excludes the science of disputation (jadal) which is also concerned with rules but not specifically for deriving fiqh. The passage clarifies that while disputation (jadal) might seem similar, it is not specifically a near conveyance to fiqh, but the jurists included many fiqh issues in it, giving the impression that it is specific to fiqh.

Key Terms
الْقَاعِدَةُ (al-qa'idah): A universal ruling (hukm kulli) that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it.
التَّوَصُّلُ الْقَرِيبُ (al-tawassul al-qarib): A direct means of reaching fiqh rulings without an intermediate science; usul al-fiqh itself provides this.
الْجَدَلِيُّ (al-jadali): The science of disputation (ilm al-jadal) which is concerned with preserving or demolishing positions, not specifically with deriving fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the relationship between usul al-fiqh and the science of Arabic grammar?
A) Arabic grammar is a sub-branch of usul al-fiqh
B) Arabic grammar is a distant conveyance to fiqh, while usul al-fiqh is a near conveyance
C) Usul al-fiqh and Arabic grammar are identical sciences
D) Arabic grammar is unnecessary for usul al-fiqh

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that provide immediate access to fiqh rulings, unlike Arabic and kalam which are only preparatory.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Genesis and Scope of Usul al-Fiqh: Sources, Aḥkām, and Distinction from Jadal
The genesis of usul al-fiqh and its distinction from jadal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how usul al-fiqh originated from the examination of the four sources (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and the five ahkam, and explain why the science of disputation (jadal) is not usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh was born from systematic reflection on the sources and rulings, and is distinct from jadal because it aims to derive, not just defend.

The passage traces the development of usul al-fiqh from the recognition of human accountability and the need for qiyas. It then describes how scholars codified universal rules for derivation. Finally, it distinguishes usul from the science of disputation (jadal), a common confusion.

Guided Path
1
Trace the rationale for usul al-fiqh
Explain why usul al-fiqh became necessary: because humans are not created in vain; their actions have rulings from the Lawgiver attached to specific evidences. Since it is impossible to enumerate all particular cases, analogy (qiyas) is used to extend rulings to new cases. This produced detailed propositions (fiqh).
The passage uses 'tahqiq' to emphasize this is verified knowledge.
2
Identify the four sources and five ahkam
List the evidences (adillah) that the scholars found: the Book (Quran), Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). Then list the categories of rulings (ahkam): wujub (obligation), nadb (recommendation), hurmah (prohibition), karahah (dislike), and ibahah (permissibility).
These are the raw materials that usul al-fiqh systematizes.
3
Understand the method of universal rules
Describe how scholars reflected on the manner of inference (istidlal) from those evidences to those rulings in a general way (ijmalan), without looking at details except for examples. This gave them universal propositions about the method, which they codified as usul al-fiqh.
The phrase 'by way of example' indicates they used particular cases to illustrate the universal rules.
4
Distinguish usul from jadal
Explain why the author added 'tahqiq' to exclude the science of disputation (ilm al-khilaf/jadal). The dialectician (jadali) either preserves a position or demolishes it; they are not concerned with deriving rulings. Even though jurists include many fiqh examples in jadal, its purpose is different from usul.
This is a key boundary that prevents conflating debate with derivation.

كَشَجَرَةِ الْأَرَاكِ وَالْقَاعِدَةُ حُكْمٌ كُلّى يَنْطَبِقُ عَلَى جُزْئِيَّاتِهِ لِيُتَعَرَّفَ أَحْكَامُهَا مِنْهُ كَقَوْلِنَا كُلُّ حُكْمِ دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ الْقِيَاسُ فَهُوَ ثَابِتٌ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ الْقَرِيبُ مُسْتَفَادٌ مِنَ الْبَاء السَّبَبِيَّةِ الظَّاهِرَةِ فِي السَّبَبِ الْقَرِيبِ وَمِنْ إطْلَاقِ التَّوَصُّلِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ ، إِذْ فِي الْبَعِيدِ يُتَوَصَّلُ إِلَى الْوَاسِطَةِ وَمِنْهَا إلَى الْفِقْهِ فَيَخْرُجُ الْعِلْمُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ وَالْكَلَامِ ؛ لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ مَبَادِى أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ وَالتَّوَصُّلُ بِهِمَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ لَيْسَ بِقَرِيبٍ ، إِذْ يَتَوَكَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْعَرَبِيَّةِ إِلَى مَعْرِفَةِ كَيْفِيَّةِ دَلَالَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ عَلَى مَدْلُولَاتِهَا الْوَضْعِيَّةِ وَبِوَاسِطَةِ ذَلِكَ يَقْتَدِرُ عَلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِنْ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ يَتَوَصَّلُ بِقَوَاعِدِ الْكَلَامِ إِلَى ثُبُوتِ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَوُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمَا لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِذَلِكَ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَالتَّحْقِيقُ فِى هَذَا الْمَقَامِ أَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَمْ يُخْلَقُ عَبَثًا وَلَمْ يُتْرَكَ سُدًى ، بَلْ تَعَلَّقَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ أَعْمَالِهِ حُكْمٌ مِنْ قِبَلِ الشَّارِعِ مَنُوطٌ بِدَلِيلٍ يَخُصُّهُ لِيَسْتَنْبِطَ مِنْهُ عِنْدَ الْحَاجَةِ وَيُقَاسُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ مَا يُنَاسِبُهُ لِتَعَدُّرِ الْإِحَاطَةِ بِجَمِيعِ الْجُزْئِيَّاتِ فَحَصَلَتْ قَضَايَا مَوْضُوعَاتُهَا أَفْعَالُ الْمُكَلَّفِينَ وَمَحْمُولَاتُهَا أَحْكَامُ الشَّارِعِ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ فَسُمِّيَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا الحَاصِلُ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِقْهًا ، ثُمَّ نَظَرُوا فِي تَفَاصِيلٍ تِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَعُمُومِهَا فَوَجَدُوا الْأَدِلَّةَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ وَالْأَحْكَامَ رَاجِعَةً إِلَى الْوُجُوبِ وَالنَّدْبِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ وَالْكَرَاهَةِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ وَتَأَمَّلُوا فِي كَيْفِيَّةِ الاسْتِدْلَالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا مِنْ غَيْرِ نَظَرٍ إِلَى تَفَاصِيلِهِمَا إِلَّا عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْمِثَالِ فَحَصَلَ لَهُمْ قَضَايَا كُلِّيَّةٌ مُتَعَلَّقَةٌ بِكَيْفِيَّةِ الاستدلالِ بِتِلْكَ الْأَدِلَّةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ إِجْمَالًا وَبَيَانُ طُرُقِهِ وَشَرَائِطِهِ لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِكُلِّ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْقَضَايَا إِلَى اسْتِنْبَاطِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ عَنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا التَّفْصِيلِيَّةِ فَضَبَطُوهَا وَدَوَّنُوهَا وَأَضَافُوا إِلَيْهَا مِنْ اللَّوَاحِقِ وَالْمُتَمِّمَاتِ وَبَيَانِ الاخْتِلَافَاتِ مَا يَلِيقُ بِهَا وَسَمَّوُا الْعِلْمَ بِهَا أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ فَصَارَتْ عِبَارَةً عَنْ الْعِلْمِ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَلَفْظُ الْقَوَاعِدِ مُشْعِرٌ بِقَيْدِ الْإِجْمَالِ وَزَادَ الْمُصَنِّفُ قَيْدَ التَّحْقِيقِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْخِلَافِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَمْنَعَ كَوْنَ قَوَاعِدِهِ مِمَّا يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ تَوَصُّلًا قَرِيبًا ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا يُتَوَكَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مُحَافَظَةِ الْحُكْمِ الْمُسْتَنْبَطِ أَوْ مُدَافَعَتِهِ وَنِسْبَتِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَغَيْرِهِ عَلَى السَّوِيَّةِ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَلِيَّ إِمَّا مُجِيبٌ يَحْفَظُ وَضْعًا ، وَإِمَّا مُعْتَرِضٌ يَهْدِمُ وَضْعًا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْفُقَهَاءَ أَكْثَرُوا فِيهِ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ وَبَنَوْا نِكَاتَهُ عَلَيْهَا حَتَّى تُوُهِّمَ أَنَّ لَهُ اخْتِصَاصًا بِالْفِقْهِ. ترجمہ: قوله وعلم اصول الفقه . بعد اس کے ثابت ہو چکی ہے یہ بات کہ بیشک اصول فقہ لقب ہے ایک علم مخصوص کا نہیں ہے کوئی حاجت علم کی اضافت کرنے کی اس کی طرف مگر یہ کہ ارادہ کیا جائے بیان اور توضیح کی زیادتی کا جیسے شجرة الا راک ( پیلو کا درخت ) اور قاعدہ ایسا حکم کلی ہے جو منطبق ہوتا ہو اپنی جزئیات پر تاکہ پہچانے جائیں اس کے احکام اس سے جیسے ہمارا قول۔ ہر ایسا حکم جس پر قیاس دلالت کرے وہ ثابت ہے اور توصل قریب مستفاد ہوتا ہے اس بائے سبیہ سے جو ظاہر ہے سبب قریب میں اور توصل کی نسبت کرنے سے فقہ کی طرف اس لئے کہ نسبت بعید میں تو صل ہوتا ہے واسطہ کی طرف پھر اس واسطہ سے توصل ہوتا ہے فقہ کی طرف۔ پس خارج ہو جائے گا وہ علم جو حاصل ہوتا ہے علوم عربیہ اور علم کلام سے اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں اصول فقہ کے مبادی میں سے ہیں اور توصل ان دونوں سے فقہ تک توصل قریب نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ قواعد عربیہ سے توصل ہوتا ہے الفاظ کی مدلولات وضعیہ پر دلالت کرنے کی کیفیت کی معرفت کی طرف۔ اور اس واسطہ کے ساتھ وہ قدرت حاصل ہوتی ہے احکام کے استنباط کرنے پر کتاب سے اور سنت سے۔ اور اسی طرح توصل حاصل ہوتا ہے قواعد کلام کے ساتھ کتاب وسنت کے ثبوت کی طرف اور ان دونوں کے صدق کے وجوب کی طرف تاکہ توصل حاصل ہو اس کے ساتھ فقہ تک اور تحقیق اس مقام میں یہ ہے کہ بیشک انسان نہیں پیدا کیا گیا بے کار اور نہیں چھوڑا گیا فضول بلکہ متعلق ہے اس کے ہر عمل کے ساتھ حکم شارع کی جانب سے مدار اس حکم کا ایسی دلیل کے ساتھ ہے کہ خاص کرے وہ دلیل اس علم کو تا کہ استنباط کیا جائے اس سے ضرورت کے وقت اور قیاس کیا جائے اس حکم پر ایسے حکم کو جو اس کے مناسب ہو بوجہ تمام جزئیات کے احاطے کے مشکل ہونے کے۔ پس حاصل ہوئے چند ایسے قضایا کہ ان کا موضوع مکلفین کے افعال ہیں اور ان کا معمول شارع کے احکام ہیں تفصیلا ۔ پس نام رکھا گیا اس علم کا جو حاصل ہونے والا ہے ان ادلہ سے فقہ ۔ پھر غور کیا انہوں نے اولہ اور احکام کی تفصیل میں
Like the araak tree; and al-qa'idah is a universal ruling that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it, like our saying: Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established. And 'near conveyance' (tawassul qarib) is derived from the causative ba' which is apparent in the near cause, and from the unrestricted application of 'conveyance' to fiqh. For in 'distant' (conveyance), one conveys to an intermediary, and from it to fiqh. Thus, the knowledge of the rules of Arabic (grammar) and kalam (theology) is excluded because they are from the preliminaries (mabadi) of usul al-fiqh, and conveyance by them to fiqh is not near. For through the rules of Arabic one arrives at knowledge of how words indicate their conventional meanings, and by that means one is able to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, through the rules of kalam one arrives at the establishment of the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness, so that by that one may reach fiqh. The verification in this context is that man was not created in vain nor left neglected; rather, attached to each of his actions is a ruling from the Lawgiver, contingent upon a specific evidence so that he may derive from it when needed, and analogize to that ruling what is appropriate, due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars. Thus, propositions arose whose subjects are the acts of the mukallaf and whose predicates are the rulings of the Lawgiver in detail, and the knowledge derived from those evidences was called fiqh. Then they examined the details of those evidences and rulings and their generality, and found that the evidences reduce to the Book, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, and the rulings reduce to obligation (wujub), recommendation (nadb), prohibition (hurmah), dislike (karahah), and permissibility (ibahah). They reflected on the manner of inference (istidlal) from those evidences to those rulings in general (ijmalan), without regard to their details except by way of example, and thus universal propositions were obtained relating to the manner of inference from those evidences to those rulings in general, and the exposition of its ways and conditions, so that through each of those propositions one may derive many of those particular rulings from their detailed evidences. So they recorded them, codified them, and added to them what befits of supplements, completions, and exposition of differences, and they called the knowledge of them usul al-fiqh. Thus it came to be an expression of the knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) by which one reaches fiqh. The term 'rules' indicates the condition of generality. And the author added the condition of 'verification' (tahqiq) to exclude the science of disputation (ilm al-khilaf). And someone might argue that its rules are not a means of near conveyance to fiqh, but rather they are used to preserve the derived ruling, or to defend it, and to ascribe it to fiqh or other sciences equally. For the dialectician is either a respondent who preserves a position or an objector who demolishes a position, but the jurists have included many fiqh issues in it and built its points upon them, so that it was imagined that it is specific to fiqh.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the science of usul al-fiqh. It begins by defining a 'qa'idah' (rule) as a universal proposition that applies to its particulars, exemplified by the statement 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.' Then it discusses the concept of 'tawassul qarib' (near conveyance) versus 'tawassul ba'id' (distant conveyance) to fiqh. The author explains that usul al-fiqh provides near conveyance to fiqh, whereas Arabic grammar and theology (kalam) are only distant conveyances because they are preliminaries (mabadi) that lead to understanding the sources but not directly to fiqh rulings. The passage then traces the historical development: human actions have rulings from the Lawgiver attached to specific evidences; since encompassing all particulars is impossible, qiyas (analogy) is used. This produced detailed propositions about acts of mukallaf and divine rulings, called fiqh. Then scholars examined the evidences (Book, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and rulings (obligation, recommendation, etc.) and studied the general method of deriving rulings from them. This gave rise to universal propositions about the method of inference, which they codified as usul al-fiqh. The definition: 'knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh.' The term 'rules' (qawa'id) indicates generality, and the author's addition of 'verification' (tahqiq) excludes the science of disputation (jadal) which is also concerned with rules but not specifically for deriving fiqh. The passage clarifies that while disputation (jadal) might seem similar, it is not specifically a near conveyance to fiqh, but the jurists included many fiqh issues in it, giving the impression that it is specific to fiqh.

Key Terms
الْقَاعِدَةُ (al-qa'idah): A universal ruling (hukm kulli) that applies to its particulars so that their rulings may be known from it.
التَّوَصُّلُ الْقَرِيبُ (al-tawassul al-qarib): A direct means of reaching fiqh rulings without an intermediate science; usul al-fiqh itself provides this.
الْجَدَلِيُّ (al-jadali): The science of disputation (ilm al-jadal) which is concerned with preserving or demolishing positions, not specifically with deriving fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of usul al-fiqh compared to ilm al-jadal?
A) Usul derives rulings; jadal defends or attacks positions.
B) They are identical in purpose and method.
C) Usul is about Arabic grammar and jadal is about theology.
D) Jadal is a branch of usul al-fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of deriving fiqh rulings from their sources through universal rules, while jadal is a separate art of disputation.

Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
Defining Usul al-Fiqh: The Rules That Lead to Fiqh
Defining usul al-fiqh and distinguishing it from dialectical theology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Usul al-Fiqh as the science of rules leading to fiqh and identify the key restrictions (ijmal and tahqiq) that distinguish it from dialectical theology.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh: knowledge of general rules that directly lead to fiqh, not mere dialectic.

This passage presents a refined definition of Usul al-Fiqh, emphasizing that it is a science of general rules (qawa'id) that provide a direct path to fiqh. The author stresses two essential restrictions: the rules are general (ijmal), and the definition includes verification (tahqiq) to exclude the dialectical science of argumentation. Understanding this definition helps you grasp the unique role of Usul al-Fiqh in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
The passage defines Usul al-Fiqh as knowledge of rules by which one arrives at fiqh. Note the three components: 'ilm (knowledge), qawa'id (rules), and tawassul ila al-fiqh (means to fiqh).
Each word in the definition is chosen deliberately by the scholars.
2
Understand the restriction of ijmal
The word 'rules' (qawa'id) implies generality (ijmal). This means usul al-fiqh deals with universal principles, not detailed individual cases.
This distinguishes usul from the detailed furu' of fiqh itself.
3
Understand the restriction of tahqiq
The author adds 'tahqiq' (verification) to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf (dialectical theology). In dialectics, one aims only to preserve or demolish a position, not to derive rulings with verification.
Tahqiq ensures the rules are sound and lead to fiqh through proper evidence.
4
Analyze the objection against direct derivation
An objector claims that usul rules are not a direct means to fiqh; they are only used to preserve and defend already derived rulings, and they apply equally to non-fiqh matters.
This is a serious challenge to the definition.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The commentator replies that jurists have embedded many fiqh issues into usul and built its principles upon them. Therefore, usul al-fiqh appears specifically related to fiqh, making it a direct means to derive or defend fiqh.
This response solidifies usul al-fiqh as an independent science tied to fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُتَمِّمَاتِ وَبَيَان الاخْتِلافَاتِ مَا يَلِيقُ بهَا وَسَمَّوُا الْعِلْمَ بهَا أُصُولَ الْفِقْهِ فَصَارَتْ عِبَارَةً عَنْ العِلم بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِى يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَلَفْظُ الْقَوَاعِدِ مُشْعِرٌ بِقَيْدِ الْإِجْمَالِ وَزَادَ الْمُصَنِّفُ قَيْدَ التَّحْقِيقِ احْتِرَازًا عَنْ عِلْمِ الْخِلَافِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَمْنَعَ كَوْنَ قَوَاعِدِهِ مِمَّا يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ تَوَصُّلا قَرِيبًا ، بَلْ إِنَّمَا يُتَوَكَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مُحَافَظَةِ الْحُكم المُسْتَنبَطِ أَوْ مُدَافَعَتِهِ وَنِسْبَتِهِ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ وَغَيْرِهِ عَلَى السَّوِيَّةِ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَلِيَّ إمَّا مُجِيبٌ يَحْفَظُ وَضْعًا ، وَإِمَّا مُعْتَرِضْ يَهْدِمُ وَضْعًا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْفُقَهَاء أَكْثَرُوا فِيهِ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ وَبَنَوْا نِكَاتَهُ عَلَيْهَا حَتَّى يُتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّ لَهُ اخْتِصَاصًا بالفِقْهِ.
And the completions and the explanation of the differences that befit it, and they called the knowledge of it 'Usul al-Fiqh'. So it became an expression for the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh. The word 'rules' indicates the restriction of generality (ijmal). The author added the restriction of verification (tahqiq) as a precaution against the science of dialectic ('ilm al-khilaf). And someone can deny that its rules are among the things by which one arrives at fiqh in a near manner. Rather, they are only used for preserving the derived ruling or defending it and attributing it to fiqh or other things equally. For the dialectician is either a responder who preserves a position or an objector who demolishes a position. However, the jurists have included many fiqh issues in it and built its points upon them, such that it is imagined to be specifically related to fiqh.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a definition and clarification of the science of Usul al-Fiqh. The author begins by stating that the scholars named this discipline 'Usul al-Fiqh' and that it came to express knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) by which one reaches fiqh. The term 'rules' indicates that it deals with general principles, not detailed issues. The author then notes that the original author (al-Musannif, i.e. Sadr al-Shariah) added the qualification 'tahqiq' (verification) to distinguish Usul al-Fiqh from 'ilm al-khilaf (dialectical theology), which is concerned only with preserving or destroying a position. An objector might argue that the rules of Usul al-Fiqh are not a direct means to derive fiqh; rather, they are used to preserve and defend already derived rulings. The objection claims that dialectical rules could apply equally to fiqh and non-fiqh matters. However, the commentator responds that the jurists have enriched Usul al-Fiqh with many fiqh examples and built its principles upon them, so it appears to be specific to fiqh. Thus, Usul al-Fiqh remains a distinct science with its own subject matter and methods.

Key Terms
القواعد (al-qawa'id): Universal rules (plural of qa'idah) that are general and not specific to individual cases.
الإجمال (al-ijmal): Summariness or generality, as opposed to detailed exposition (tafsil).
التوصل القريب (al-tawassul al-qarib): A direct or near means of reaching the goal, without intermediary.
علم الخلاف ('ilm al-khilaf): The science of dialectical disputation, focusing on preserving or demolishing a position rather than deriving rulings.
التحقيق (al-tahqiq): Verification; the qualification added to ensure the rules are based on evidence, not pure dialectic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author add the qualification 'tahqiq' (verification) to the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) To emphasize that it is a science of detailed rulings.
B) To exclude the science of dialectic ('ilm al-khilaf) from the definition.
C) To show that the rules are only preserved, not derived.
D) To indicate that it applies to all religious sciences equally.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the science of general, verified rules that directly lead to fiqh, distinguished from mere dialectical disputation.

Defining Usul al-Fiqh: Scope and Inclusion of Taqlid
Defining usul al-fiqh and explaining inclusion of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and explain why some scholars include discussions of taqlid and istifta' within its scope.

Core Idea
For the muqallid, the mujtahid's opinion functions as a proof, making taqlid a legitimate part of usul al-fiqh.

Usul al-fiqh is typically defined as the knowledge of the rules that lead to fiqh rulings. But is this definition limited to the mujtahid who directly uses the four proofs? In this passage, the author explores the rationale for including taqlid and istifta' in usul, arguing that the muqallid's reasoning—relying on the mujtahid's opinion as his evidence—constitutes a second proposition within usul. This lesson unpacks the standard definition, the distinction between mujtahid and muqallid, and the justification for expanding the scope of usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard definition
Read the Arabic text: عِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ (knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh). Note that it says 'to the issues of fiqh' (ila masa'il al-fiqh), not 'to fiqh' (ila al-fiqh). Explain why that nuance matters.
The exclusion of 'fiqh' from the definition indicates that arriving at fiqh itself requires direct engagement with proofs, which only a mujtahid does.
2
Distinguish mujtahid and muqallid
The text states that the four proofs are used by the mujtahid, not the muqallid. For the muqallid, the proof is the statement of the mujtahid (قَوْلُ الْمُجْتَهِدِ). The muqallid says: 'This ruling is established for me because Abu Hanifa held it.'
3
Analyze the inclusion of taqlid
The author argues that the muqallid's reasoning—taking the mujtahid's opinion as evidence—is a 'second proposition' (القَضِيَّةُ الثَّانِيَة) of usul al-fiqh. Therefore some scholars include discussions of taqlid and istifta' in usul books.
This does not mean taqlid is a proof in itself, but that the process of relying on a mujtahid is a legitimate topic within the methodology.
4
Verify the muqallid's path
The text concludes that the muqallid's verification (tahqiq) is to follow a mujtahid believing his opinion to be true. This does not contradict the definition of usul because it is a derived form of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تُذكَرُ مَبَاحِثُ التَّقْلِيدِ وَالاسْتِفْتَاء فِى كُتبنَا وَلَا يَبْعُدُ أَنْ يُقَالَ إِنَّهُ يَعُمُ الْمُجْتَهَدَ وَالْمُقَلّد والأدِلَّةُ الْأَرْبَعَةُ إِنَّمَا يَتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا الْمُجْتَهِدُ لَا الْمُقَلِّدُ فَأَمَّا الْمُقَلِّدُ فَالدَّلِيلُ عِنْدَهُ قَوْلُ الْمُجْتَهِدِ فَالْمُقَلّهُ يَقُولُ هَذَا الْحُكْمُ وَاقِعٌ عِنْدِي ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأَى أبي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ وَكُلُّ مَا أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ رَأْيُهُ فَهُوَ وَاقِعٌ عِنْدِى فَالْقَضِيَّةُ الثَّانِيَةُ مِنْ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ أَيْضًا فَلِهَذَا ذَكَرَ بَعْضُ الْعُلَمَاءِ فِى كُتُبِ الْأُصُولِ مَبَاحِتَ التَّقْلِيدِ وَالاسْتِفْتَاء فَعَلَى هَذَا عِلْمُ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِي يُتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا إِلَى مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ ، وَلَا يُقَالُ إِلَى الْفِقْهِ ؛ لأنَّ الْفِقْهَ هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِالأحكام مِنَ الأدِلَّةِ وَقَوْلُنَا عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّحْقِيقِ لَا يُنَافِى هَذَا الْمَعْنَى فَإِنَّ تَحْقِيقَ الْمُقَلِّدِ أَنْ يُقَلَّدَ مُجْتَهِدًا يَعْتَقِدُ ذَلِكَ الْمُقَلِّدُ حَقِيقَةَ رَأْي ذَلِكَ الْمُجْتَهِدِ
Discussions of taqlid (following a school) and istifta' (seeking legal opinion) are mentioned in our books. It is not far to say that it includes both the mujtahid and the muqallid. The four proofs are only used by the mujtahid to arrive at rulings, not the muqallid. As for the muqallid, his proof is the statement of the mujtahid. So the muqallid says: 'This ruling is established for me because the opinion of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) led to it.' And everything that his opinion leads to is established for me. Thus this second proposition is also from usul al-fiqh. For this reason, some scholars have mentioned discussions of taqlid and istifta' in books of usul. According to this, the science of usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh—not 'to fiqh' because fiqh is the knowledge of rulings from the proofs. Our statement 'in a true manner' does not contradict this meaning, for the verification of the muqallid is that he follows a mujtahid, believing the truth of that mujtahid's opinion.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope of usul al-fiqh and whether topics like taqlid (following a mujtahid) and istifta' (asking for a fatwa) belong to it. The author notes that some classical works include these topics, arguing that a muqallid's proof is the mujtahid's opinion—the muqallid says, 'This ruling is established for me because Abu Hanifa held it.' This makes the muqallid's reasoning a second proposition of usul, hence some include it. The standard definition of usul al-fiqh is 'knowledge of the rules leading to the issues of fiqh' (al-ilm bil-qawa'id allati yutawassalu biha ila masa'il al-fiqh). The author clarifies that it is not 'to fiqh' (ila al-fiqh) because fiqh is knowledge of rulings directly from proofs—only a mujtahid does that. The muqallid's 'fiqh' is a derived knowledge based on the mujtahid's opinion. The Urdu commentary expands on the conditions for a valid major premise (kubra): it must not be abrogated, must have no equal or stronger opposing evidence, and any personal ijtihad must not contradict earlier consensus. These conditions are necessary for the reason that the major premise in a syllogism or the conjunctive premise in an exceptional syllogism is only valid when these constraints are met. The author then addresses a potential objection: why discuss conditions and related topics in usul if the definition only mentions rules? The answer: conditions and related matters are part of discussing the rule itself.

Key Terms
تَقْلِيد (taqlid): Following the opinion of a mujtahid without direct evidence from the four proofs.
اسْتِفْتَاء (istifta'): Seeking a legal verdict from a qualified jurist.
مُجْتَهِد (mujtahid): A scholar capable of deriving rulings directly from the primary sources.
مُقَلِّد (muqallid): A non-mujtahid who follows a mujtahid's opinion.
كُبْرَى (kubra): The major premise in a syllogism; here, the general rule from which a fiqh ruling is deduced.
مُعَارِض (mu'arid): A conflicting evidence or proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why do some scholars include discussions of taqlid in books of usul al-fiqh?
A) Because taqlid is one of the four primary proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
B) Because the muqallid's proof (the mujtahid's opinion) is considered a 'second proposition' of usul.
C) Because the mujtahid cannot derive rulings without first studying taqlid.
D) Because the muqallid must independently verify all rulings using the four proofs.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh encompasses the rules that lead to fiqh rulings, including the muqallid's reliance on the mujtahid's opinion as a legitimate part of its scope.

Definition of Usul al-Fiqh and the Concept of Mutawassil
Definition and expansion of usul al-fiqh with conditions and mutawassil analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh, identify the conditions for a rule to serve as a premise in qiyas, and explain who is considered a mutawassil and why.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of rules for arriving at fiqh issues, used by both mujtahid and muqallid through their own verification.

In this lesson, we unpack the classical Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and its key components. The passage from the sharh clarifies why the definition speaks of 'issues of fiqh' rather than 'fiqh' itself, and who exactly can be considered a 'mutawassil'—one who uses these rules to reach rulings. We also examine the conditions that make a rule valid as a premise, and how a muqallid's verification differs from a mujtahid's.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its key terms
Locate the precise definition: 'al-'ilm bi al-qawa'id allati tawassalu biha ila masa'il al-fiqh'. Note the use of 'masa'il al-fiqh' instead of 'al-fiqh'.
This distinction is pivotal for including the muqallid.
2
Explain the conditions for rules to serve as premises
The text lists conditions: the rule must not be abrogated, must not have equal or preponderant counter-evidence, and must not oppose prior ijma'. Understand why these are necessary for a sound qiyas.
These conditions ensure the major premise is reliable.
3
Analyze the two probabilities for mutawassil
First probability: mutawassil is only the mujtahid (because fiqh requires knowing rulings from the four proofs). Second: includes muqallid by redefining the goal as 'masa'il al-fiqh'. Note the preponderant view is the first.
This ikhtilaf affects the scope of usul al-fiqh.
4
Understand the muqallid's tahqiq
The muqallid's verification is accepting his imam's statement as true, not deriving from proofs. The passage argues this is a valid form of tahqiq, making the muqallid a mutawassil.
This refutes the objection that a muqallid lacks certainty.
5
Connect the logical terminology
The Talwih excerpt defines a proposition (qadiyya) and its various names (khabar, muqaddima, matlub, etc.). Recognize that these are the building blocks of usul reasoning.
This prepares you for later lessons on qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتابوں میں تقلید اور استفتاء کے مسائل کو پس اس تفصیل پر اصول فقہ کا علم ہو العلم بالقواعد التی توصل بہا الی مسائل الفقہ اور نہیں کہا جائے گا الی الفقہ اس لئے کہ فقہ وہ جانتا ہے احکام کو ادلہ سے اور ہمارا قول علی وجہ التحقیق نہیں ہے منافی اس معنی کے پس بیشک مقلد کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ تقلید کرے مجتہد کی بایں طور کہ اعتقاد ر کھے وہ مقلد اس مجتہد کی رائے کی حقیت کا۔ تشریح : ثم اعلم : ۔ پیچھے یہ بات گذری ہے کہ فقہ کی دلیل شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ کے قواعد و ضوابط ہیں تو اب فرمایا کہ یہ قواعد کلیہ جو دلیل بنتے ہیں اس کے دلیل بننے کے لئے کچھ شرائط ہیں مثلاً جس کو دلیل بنایا ہے کام پر وہ منسوخ نہ ہو جیسے قرآن کی وہ آیات جو منسوخ الحکم ہیں اور اس دلیل کا معارض مساوی نہ ہو مثلا مشہور حدیث کے مقابلہ میں مشہور حدیث نہ ہو اور اس کا معارض راجح نہ ہو مثلا خبر واحد کے مقابلہ میں خبر مشہور نہ ہو اور اگر کوئی اجتہاد کرتا ہے تو اس سے پہلے جتنے اجتہادات ہیں ان کی مخالفت نہ کرے ورنہ اجماع کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی مثلاً ایک زمانہ میں چار مجہتدین نے اجتہاد کیا تو گویا اس پر اجماع ہو گیا کہ اس مسئلہ میں اتنی اراء ہیں ان کے علاوہ کوئی رائے نہیں اب یہ اجتہاد کر کے نئی رائے نہیں دے سکتا ہاں ان آراء میں سے کسی رائے کو ترجیح دے سکتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ کلیہ اس وقت تک مکمل نہیں ہوں گے جب تک شرائط کا اعتبار نہ کیا جائے جب شرائط ہوں گی کبری اور ملازمہ مکمل ہوگا۔ فالعلم بالمباحث:۔ اس عبارت میں مائن نے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔
سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا اصول فقہ میں ان قواعد کو بیان کریں گے جو شکل اول کا کبری اور قیاس استثنائی کا ملازمہ بنیں گے پھر اصول فقہ میں انہی سے بحث ہونی چاہئیے حالانکہ دوسری اشیاء سے بحث ہوتی ہے مثلا احوال ادلہ اور شرائط وغیرہ ان کو ذکر نہیں کرنا چاہیے ۔
جواب: یہ ہے کہ باقی اشیاء کبری کی شرائط میں سے ہیں اور ملازمات کلیہ کے متعلقات میں سے ہیں اور شئی کی شرائط اور متعلقات سے بحث کرنا اس شئے سے بحث کرنا ہے لہذا ان شرائط وغیرہ کو ذکر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
قولنا تتوصل : تعریف میں توصل کا لفظ آیا ہے اب ماتن وضاحت فرماتے ہیں کہ متوصل کون ہے؟ تو اس میں دو احتمال بیان کئے ہیں (۱) پہلا احتمال یہ ہے کہ متوصل مجتہد ہے کیونکہ تعریف میں الیہ یعنی الی الفقہ کی قید ہے اور فقہ نام ہے دلائل اربعہ سے احکام کو جانے کا اور یہ مجتہد ہی جان سکتا ہے مقلد نہیں جان سکتا بلکہ مقلد مجتہد کے قول سے معلوم کرتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ بعض حضرات نے اصول فقہ میں تقلید اور فتاویٰ کے مسائل بیان نہیں کئے اور راجح احتمال یہی ہے (۲) دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ مجتہد اور مقلد دونوں مراد ہوں اب مجتہد کا متوصل ہونا ظاہر ہے اور مقلد بھی متوصل بن سکتا ہے اگر اولہ میں تقسیم کر دیں کہ ادلہ عام ہیں کہ ادلہ اربعہ ہوں یا ان کے ماسواہ تو اب مقلد بھی متوصل بن سکتا ہے کیونکہ مقلد بھی احکام کو دلیل سے معلوم کرتا ہے لیکن فرق صرف اتنا ہے کہ مجتہد کے لئے دلیل ادلہ اربعہ سے ہے اور مقلد کے لئے دلیل مجتہد کا قول ہے چنانچہ مقلد کہے گا هذا الحكم ثابت لانه ادى اليه رأى ابي حنيفة وكل حكم ادى اليه رأى ابي حنيفة فهو ثابت عندى لیکن جب متوصل عام ہو گا تو تعریف میں تھوڑی سی تبدیلی کریں گے۔ الی الفقہ کی بجائے الی مسائل الفقہ کہیں گے ۔ کیونکہ مقلد مسائل فقہ کو جانتا ہے۔ فقہ تو ادلہ اربعہ سے احکام کو جانے کا نام ہے اور یہ مجتہد کا کام ہے اور مقلد تو صرف مسائل جان سکتا ہے۔ وقولنا علی وجہ التحقیق:۔ اس عبارت میں مائن نے سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔
سوال:۔ متوصل کو عام کرنا درست نہیں۔ اسلئے کہ اگر چہ الی الفقہ کی بجائے الی مسائل الفقہ کہ دیں کیونکہ پھر بھی مقلد علی وجہ التحقیق کی قید سے نکل جائے گا کیونکہ تحقیق مجتہد کرتا ہے ملقد نہیں کرتا۔
جواب:۔ یہ علی وجہ اتحقیق کی قید مقاید کے متوصل ہونے کے منافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہر ایک کی تحقیق علیحدہ ہے۔ مجتہد کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ وہ ادلہ اربعہ سے احکام کو ثابت کرے اور مقلد کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ وہ یہ جان لے کہ اس کے امام اور مجتہد کا قول حق ہے۔ تو مقلد کہہ سکتا ہے کہ میرے مجتہد کا قول میرے نزدیک محقق ہے۔ یہ میرے امام کا قول ہے۔ لھذا پھر بھی مقلد متوصل ہو سکتا ہے۔ تلویح
قَوْلُهُ ) وَنَعُنِي بِالْقَضَايَا الْكُلِّيَّةِ اعْلَمُ أَنَّ الْمُرَكَّبَ النَّامُ الْمُحْتَمِلَ لِلصَّدْقِ وَالْكَذِبِ يُسَمَّى مِنْ حَيْثُ اشْتِمَالِهِ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ قَضِيَّةً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ احْتِمَالِهِ الصَّدْقَ وَالْكَذِبَ خَبَرًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِفَادَتِهِ الْحُكْمَ إِخْبَارًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ جُزْءا مِنْ الدَّلِيلِ مُقَدَّمَةً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ يُطْلَبُ بِالدَّلِيلِ مَطْلُوبًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ يَحُصُلُ مِنْ الدَّلِيلِ نَتِيجَةً وَمِنْ حَيْثُ يَقَعُ فِى الْعِلْمِ وَيُسْأَلُ عَنْهُ مَسْأَلَة فَالذَّاتُ وَاحِدَةٌ وَاخْتِلَافُ الْعِبَارَاتِ بِاخْتِلافِ الاعْتِبَارَاتِ وَالْمَحْكُومُ عَلَيْهِ فِى الْقَضِيَّةِ يُسَمَّى مَوْضُوعًا وَالْمَحْكُومُ بِهِ مَحْمُولًا وَمَوْضُوعُ المَطْلُوبِ يُسَمَّى أَصْغَرَ وَمَحْمُولُهُ أَكْبَرَ وَالدِّلِيلُ يَتَأَلفُ لَا
In books, the issues of taqlid and ifta'... so with this detail, knowledge of usul al-fiqh is 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh' (al-'ilm bi al-qawa'id allati tawassalu biha ila masa'il al-fiqh) and it will not be said 'ila al-fiqh' because fiqh is knowing rulings from proofs, and our statement 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is not contrary to this meaning. For indeed the tahqiq of a muqallid is that he performs taqlid of a mujtahid in such a way that he believes the correctness of the mujtahid's opinion. Commentary: Then know: Previously it passed that the proof of fiqh is the major premise of the first figure and the conjunctive premise of the exceptional syllogism, which are universal rules of usul al-fiqh. Now it is said that these universal rules, when they become proof, have certain conditions: for example, that which is taken as proof must not be abrogated, like verses of the Quran that are abrogated in ruling; and its counter-evidence must not be equal, e.g., a well-known hadith against a well-known hadith; and its counter-evidence must not be preponderant, e.g., a well-known hadith against a solitary hadith. And if someone performs ijtihad, he must not oppose the ijtihads that came before, otherwise opposition to ijma' would occur. For example, if four mujtahids in a time performed ijtihad, it is as if there is ijma' that in that issue there are only those opinions. Now this one cannot give a new opinion by ijtihad, though he can give preference to one of those opinions. In summary, the major premise of the first figure and the conjunctive premise of the exceptional syllogism will not be complete until the conditions are considered. When the conditions exist, the major premise and conjunctive premise will be complete. 'So knowledge of the discussions (fa al-'ilm bi al-mabahith)': In this phrase, the author has answered a hypothetical question. Question: You said that in usul al-fiqh we will explain those rules that become the major premise of the first figure and the conjunctive premise of the exceptional syllogism. Then in usul al-fiqh, only these should be discussed, whereas other things are discussed, like the states of proofs and conditions, etc. These should not be mentioned. Answer: The remaining things are among the conditions of the major premise and the correlates of the universal conjunctive premises. Discussing the conditions and correlates of a thing is equivalent to discussing that thing. Hence there is no harm in mentioning these conditions etc. 'Our statement tatawassalu': In the definition, the word 'tawassul' appears. Now the commentator clarifies: Who is the mutawassil (the one who arrives)? Two probabilities are stated: (1) The first probability is that mutawassil is the mujtahid, because in the definition there is the restriction 'ila al-fiqh', and fiqh is the name for knowing rulings from the four proofs, and only the mujtahid can know that; the muqallid cannot know it, but rather the muqallid knows from the statement of the mujtahid. This is why some scholars did not mention issues of taqlid and ifta' in usul al-fiqh. And this is the preponderant probability. (2) The second probability is that both mujtahid and muqallid are meant. Now the mujtahid's being mutawassil is obvious. The muqallid can also be mutawassil if we divide the proofs into general categories: either the four proofs or other than them. Then the muqallid can also be mutawassil because the muqallid also knows rulings from a proof, but the difference is only that for the mujtahid the proof is from the four proofs, and for the muqallid the proof is the statement of the mujtahid. Thus the muqallid would say: 'This ruling is established because it led to the opinion of Abu Hanifa, and every ruling that leads to the opinion of Abu Hanifa is established for me.' But when mutawassil is general, we will make a slight change in the definition: instead of 'ila al-fiqh' we will say 'ila masa'il al-fiqh', because the muqallid knows the issues of fiqh. Fiqh is the name for knowing rulings from the four proofs, and that is the work of the mujtahid. The muqallid only knows the issues. 'And our statement 'ala wajh al-tahqiq': In this phrase, the author has answered a hypothetical question. Question: Making mutawassil general is not correct, because even if we say 'ila masa'il al-fiqh' instead of 'ila al-fiqh', the muqallid still escapes the restriction of 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' because tahqiq is done by the mujtahid, not by the muqallid. Answer: The restriction 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is not contrary to the muqallid being mutawassil, because the tahqiq of each is separate. The tahqiq of the mujtahid is that he establishes rulings from the four proofs. The tahqiq of the muqallid is that he knows that the statement of his imam and mujtahid is true. So the muqallid can say: 'The statement of my mujtahid is verified for me. It is the statement of my imam.' Therefore the muqallid can still be mutawassil. Al-Talwih: 'His statement: "And we mean by universal propositions (al-qadaya al-kulliyya)" Know that a composite utterance that is subject to truth and falsehood is called, from the perspective of its containing a judgment, a proposition (qadiyya); from the perspective of its possibility of truth and falsehood, a report (khabar); from the perspective of its conveying a judgment, an informative statement (ikhbar); from the perspective of being a part of a proof, a premise (muqaddima); from the perspective that it is sought by a proof, a sought (matlub); from the perspective that it results from a proof, a conclusion (natija); and from the perspective that it occurs in knowledge and is asked about, a question (mas'ala). So the essence is one, and the variation of expressions is due to variation of perspectives. The subject of the judgment in a proposition is called the subject (mawdu'), and what is predicated is called the predicate (mahmul). The subject of the sought is called the minor term (asghar) and its predicate the major term (akbar). The proof is composed of...' [incomplete]
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of usul al-fiqh and its components. It begins by discussing the definition: usul al-fiqh is 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh' (al-'ilm bi al-qawa'id allati tawassalu biha ila masa'il al-fiqh). The author explains why it says 'masa'il al-fiqh' instead of 'al-fiqh': fiqh specifically means knowing rulings from the four proofs, which is the work of a mujtahid, while a muqallid only knows the issues (masa'il). The commentary then addresses conditions for the major premise and conjunctive premise of the syllogism: they must not be abrogated, must not have equal or preponderant counter-evidence, and must not oppose prior ijtihad (which would violate ijma'). A hypothetical question is answered: why does usul al-fiqh discuss topics beyond these premises? Because those topics are conditions and correlates of the premises. Next, the word 'mutawassil' (one who arrives) is analyzed. Two probabilities: (1) only mujtahid (rajih/preponderant), because only he knows fiqh; (2) both mujtahid and muqallid, if we define the goal as masa'il al-fiqh. The muqallid's proof is the mujtahid's statement. The objection that a muqallid lacks tahqiq (verification) is answered: each has his own tahqiq—the mujtahid through proofs, the muqallid through accepting his imam's statement as true. Finally, the Arabic text from Talwih defines a logical proposition (qadiyya) and its various names depending on perspective: qadiyya (judgment), khabar (report), muqaddima (premise), matlub (sought), natija (conclusion), mas'ala (question). This clarifies the building blocks of usul reasoning.

Key Terms
قضية (qadiyya): A composite utterance subject to truth and falsehood that contains a judgment; called by different names depending on perspective (khabar, muqaddima, matlub, natija, mas'ala).
متوصل (mutawassil): One who arrives at fiqh rulings using the rules of usul; can be mujtahid or muqallid depending on interpretation.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid's opinion, considering it verified (tahqiq) for himself; his proof is the mujtahid's statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) Knowledge of the four proofs.
B) Knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh.
C) Knowledge of the rulings of fiqh.
D) Knowledge of the conditions of qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of rules and conditions for deriving fiqh, and it serves both mujtahid and muqallid with distinct forms of verification.

Deriving Fiqh from General Rules via Syllogism
Explaining the derivation of fiqh from general principles via syllogism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical structure of a legal proof in Hanafi usul and apply the method of syllogism using general rules to deduce a fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
A general rule (qa'ida kulliyya) serves as the major premise in a syllogism; when combined with a minor premise, it yields a fiqh ruling.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text explains how fiqh rulings are not derived directly from texts but through the mediation of general principles. It introduces the logical framework of syllogism, breaking down a proof into minor and major premises with a middle term. By understanding this structure, you will see how Usul al-Fiqh provides the tools for legal deduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parts of the proof
In the example 'Hajj is wajib because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib', locate the minor term (Hajj), major term (wajib), and middle term (commanded).
The middle term is the element that appears in both premises.
2
Determine the figure of the syllogism
Check the position of the middle term: in the first figure, it is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise. Verify this in the example.
The passage identifies this as 'shakl awwal' (first figure).
3
Distinguish the premises
Label the minor premise (the specific fact: 'Hajj is commanded') and the major premise (the general rule: 'Everything commanded is wajib').
The general rule is the qa'ida kulliyya.
4
Apply to a new case
Practice by constructing a similar syllogism for another act, such as Zakat. Use the same general rule and a specific minor premise.
Ensure both premises are true to reach a valid conclusion.

Source Text

حیثیت سے کہ وہ علم میں واقع ہوتا ہے اور اس کے بارہ میں سوال کیا جاتا ہے مسئلہ ہے ۔ پس ذات ایک ہے اور عنوانات کا مختلف ہونا اعتباروں کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور قضیہ میں محکوم علیہ کا نام موضوع رکھا جاتا ہے اور محکوم بہ کا محمول۔ اور مطلوب کے موضوع کا نام اصغر رکھا جاتا ہے اور اس کے معمول کا نام رکھا جاتا ہے اکبر ۔ اور دلیل مر تکب ہوتی ہے لا محالہ دو مقدموں سے۔ ان دو ( مقدموں) میں ایک مشتمل ہوتا ہے اصغر پر اور اس کا نام صغری رکھا جاتا ہے۔ اور دوسرا مقدمہ ( مشتمل) ہوتا ہے ) اکبر پر اور اس کا نام کبڑی رکھا جاتا ہے ۔ اور وہ دونوں مقدمے مشتمل ہوتے ہیں ایک ایسے امر پر جوان دونوں میں مکرر ہوتا ہے اس امر کا نام حد اوسط رکھا جاتا ہے اور یہ حد اوسط یا تو صغریٰ میں محمول، کبری میں موضوع ہوگا اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے دلیل کا اس اعتبار سے شکل اول یا بر عکس ہو گا اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے شکل رابع ۔ یا محمول ہو گا دونوں میں اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے شکل ثانی یا موضوع ہوگا دونوں میں اور نام رکھا جاتا ہے شکل ثالث مثلاً جب ہم نے الحج واجب لانه مامور الشارع وكل مامور الشارع فهو واجب “ کہا پس الج اصغر ہے اور واجب اکبر ہے اور اور مامور حد اوسط ہے اور ہمارا قول الحج ما مور الشارع یہ مغرئی ہے اور ہمارا قول کل مامور الشارع فهو واجب ہے یہ کبری ہے اور مذکورہ دلیل شکل اول کے قبیل سے ہے۔ پس وہ قواعد کہ نو مسل ہوتا ہے ان کے ذریعہ فقہ تک وہ قضا یا کلیہ ہیں جو صغری سھلتہ الحصول کیلئے کبری واقع ہوتے ہیں مسائل فقہ پر شکل اول کے ذریعہ استدلال کے وقت۔ جیسا کہ مثال مذکور میں ہے اور قاعدہ کلیہ کو ملا نا صغری سھلتہ الحصول کی طرف (اس لیے ہے ) تاکہ نکل جائے مطلوب فقہی قوت سے فعل کی طرف اور یہی معنی ہے قواعد کے ذریعہ فقہ تک توصل کا ۔ لیکن قاعدہ کلیہ کا حاصل ہونا موقوف ہوتا ہے اولہ و احکام کے احوال سے بحث کرنے پر اور ان کی شرائط کے بیان کرنے پر اور دونوں کی قیمود پر جو معتبر ہیں قاعدہ کے کلیہ ہونے میں ۔ پس وہ مباحث جو ان چیزوں کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں وہ اصول فقہ کے مطالب ہیں اور مندرج ہیں یہ تمام ( ابحاث ) قاعدہ کلیہ کے علم کے تحت۔ اس تفصیل پر کہ جو وضاحت کی ہے مصنف نے کہ اس پر زیادتی کی گنجائش نہیں ہے۔
From the perspective that it occurs in knowledge and about it a question is asked: it is a mas'ala. So the essence is one, and the difference in titles is due to difference in aspects. In a proposition, the judged-upon is called subject, and the judged-with is called predicate. The subject of the sought is called minor term, and its predicate is called major term. The proof necessarily consists of two premises. Of these two premises, one contains the minor term and is called minor premise. The second premise contains the major term and is called major premise. Both premises contain a matter that is repeated in both; this matter is called the middle term. This middle term will either be predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise, and the proof is called first figure; or the opposite, and it is called fourth figure; or it will be predicate in both, and it is called second figure; or subject in both, and it is called third figure. For example, when we say: 'Hajj is wajib because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib.' So Hajj is the minor term, wajib is the major term, and commanded is the middle term. Our saying 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' is the minor premise, and our saying 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib' is the major premise. The mentioned proof is of the first figure. So the rules by which one arrives at fiqh are the general propositions that serve as major premises for the easy attainment of minor premises when deducing fiqh issues by the first figure, as in the mentioned example. And the general rule is attached to the easily obtained minor premise so that the sought fiqh matter emerges from power to act. This is the meaning of reaching fiqh through rules. But the attainment of the general rule depends on investigating the states of primary rulings and their conditions, and on establishing them as valid for being general rules. So the discussions related to these things are the topics of Usul al-Fiqh, and all these investigations are included under the knowledge of the general rule. This is the detail that the author has explained, beyond which there is no room for addition.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of deriving fiqh from general principles. It begins by explaining the logical structure of propositions and syllogisms, showing how a proof (dalil) consists of two premises containing a middle term. The author then applies this to fiqh: general rules (qawa'id kulliyya) serve as major premises, and when combined with specific minor premises (easily obtained facts), they yield fiqh rulings through the first figure of syllogism. The example given is the deduction that Hajj is wajib because it is commanded by the Lawgiver and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib. The passage emphasizes that attaining these general rules requires investigating the ahkam and their conditions, which are precisely the subjects of Usul al-Fiqh. Thus, Usul al-Fiqh is the science of the general rules used in legal deduction.

Key Terms
قاعدہ کلیہ (qa'ida kulliyya): A general proposition that serves as a major premise in legal deduction, e.g., 'Whatever is commanded is wajib.'
شکل اول (shakl awwal): The first figure of syllogism where the middle term is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It replaces the need for Quran and Sunnah.
D) It is irrelevant to legal deduction.

Key Takeaway
General rules (qawa'id kulliyya) are the major premises in legal syllogisms, and studying them is the essence of Usul al-Fiqh.

Logical Terminology in Usul al-Fiqh: The Seven Names and Syllogistic Structure
Defining logical terms and applying them to a fiqh example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven names of a compound proposition, define subject and predicate, and apply the four figures of syllogism to a legal proposition.

Core Idea
Logical terms like qadiyya and syllogism are the structural tools of legal proof in usul al-fiqh.

This passage introduces the foundational logical terminology used in usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains that a compound statement (kalam) has multiple names depending on the perspective: proposition, report, premise, etc. He then defines the roles of subject and predicate, and outlines the four figures of syllogism based on the position of the middle term. Finally, he applies these terms to the example 'Hajj is wajib', demonstrating how logical structure underpins legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compound proposition and its seven names
Recognize that a statement like 'Zaid is standing' is a compound (kalam) that can be called qadiyya, khabar, ikhbar, muqaddima, matlub, natija, or mas'ala depending on the perspective (e.g., possibility of truth, part of a proof, etc.).
These are not different entities but the same statement viewed differently.
2
Define subject and predicate
In a proposition, the thing judged upon (mahkum 'alayh) is the subject (mawdu'), and the thing judged with (mahkum bih) is the predicate (mahmul). In 'Zaid is standing', Zaid is subject, standing is predicate.
In syllogism, the subject is called the minor term (asghar) and the predicate the major term (akbar).
3
Understand the seven names from different perspectives
For each perspective (e.g., as part of a proof → muqaddima, as sought → matlub), map the same proposition to its corresponding name.
Practice with the example 'Zaid is standing' given in the text.
4
Learn the four figures of syllogism
The middle term (al-hadd al-awsat) appears in both premises. Its position determines the figure: 1st figure (predicate in minor, subject in major), 2nd (predicate in both), 3rd (subject in both), 4th (subject in minor, predicate in major).
The first figure is the most natural for legal deduction.
5
Apply the terms to 'Hajj is wajib'
Take the proposition 'Hajj is wajib'. Hajj is the subject (minor term), wajib is the predicate (major term). The middle term is 'commanded by the Lawgiver'. Premises: 'Hajj is commanded' (minor) and 'Whatever is commanded is wajib' (major). This is a first-figure syllogism.
This shows how logical form structures legal arguments.

Source Text

اصطلاحات منطقیہ کا بیان
تشریح قول یعنی بالقضایا:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارع امتن میں مذکور لفظ قضیہ کا معنی بیان کرتا ہے اور اس مناسبت سے کچھ اصطلاحات کو بیان کرتا ہے۔
